# Changelog: May 2026

Feature additions and fixes recorded from 2026-05-01 onwards.

## Cancel / Together: single-generator polynomial-radicand path (2026-05-25)

Adds a new code path (`qa_cancel_with_poly_radical`, in
`src/poly/qafactor.c`) that lets `Cancel[..., Extension -> Automatic]`
and `Together[..., Extension -> Automatic]` simplify inputs containing
exactly one distinct radical of the form `Sqrt[poly]` or `Power[poly,
1/q]` (q ≥ 2), where `poly` is a polynomial expression with free
symbolic parameters.

Why this matters: the existing `extension_autodetect` rejects polynomial
radicands because the underlying `QAExt`/`QAUPoly` machinery has
`Q`-coefficient minimal polynomials and cannot represent the `Q(params)`
case.  Phase E side-steps the QAExt machinery via a
"substitute-and-reduce" identity that needs only `Together` +
`PolynomialRemainder` + `PolynomialExtendedGCD`.

### Algorithm

For an input `arg` containing exactly one distinct polynomial-radicand
radical `α = Power[poly, 1/q]`:

1. Substitute every occurrence of `α` with a fresh symbol `S`.
2. Run `Together` (no extension) on the substituted input — combines
   sum-of-fractions over `Q[params, vars, S]`.
3. Extract `Numerator` and `Denominator`.
4. Reduce each modulo `S^q - poly` via `PolynomialRemainder[expr, S^q -
   poly, S]`.  This replaces `S^k` (k ≥ q) by `S^(k-q)·poly` until the
   `S`-degree is less than `q`.
5. (Optional rationalisation) If the reduced denominator still has
   `S`-degree > 0, call `PolynomialExtendedGCD[den, S^q - poly, S]` to
   obtain `u, v, g` with `u·den + v·(S^q - poly) = g`.  When the gcd
   `g` is `S`-free, multiply numerator by `u`, take `Together`,
   `Numerator`/`Denominator`, and reduce again — clears `S` from the
   denominator.  Accept the rationalised form only when it does not
   inflate the combined leaf count (so `q = 2` benefits; `q ≥ 3` keeps
   the un-rationalised form when the norm-style cofactor blows up).
6. Substitute `S → α` back and emit `num / den`.

### Examples

- `Together[1/(x - Sqrt[p+q]) + 1/(x + Sqrt[p+q]), Extension ->
  Automatic]` → `(2 x)/(-p - q + x^2)`  (collapse from sum-of-fractions
  using `Sqrt[p+q]^2 = p+q`).
- `Cancel[(x^2 - (p+q))/(x - Sqrt[p+q]), Extension -> Automatic]` →
  `Sqrt[p+q] + x`  (rationalisation step via `PolynomialExtendedGCD`).
- `Together[1/(x - Power[p+q, 1/3]) + 1/(x + Power[p+q, 1/3]), Extension
  -> Automatic]` → `(2 x)/(-(p+q)^(2/3) + x^2)`  (cube root case;
  un-rationalised form preferred because the rationalised norm inflates).
- `Together[(Power[1+x, 1/3])^3, Extension -> Automatic]` → `1 + x`
  (cube reduction in the numerator).
- `Together[(Sqrt[p+q])^2 + 1, Extension -> Automatic]` → `1 + p + q`.

### Cardano gap (documented)

The motivating Cardano identity
`Together[((-q/2 + Sqrt[(q/2)^2 + (p/3)^3])^(1/3) + (-q/2 -
Sqrt[(q/2)^2 + (p/3)^3])^(1/3))^3 + p·(...) + q]` does NOT collapse to
0 under Phase E.  The input contains three distinct polynomial-radicand
radicals (one `Sqrt[poly]` and two cube-roots whose bases contain the
inner Sqrt); Phase E's "exactly one" detection rejects the case.

Beyond the detection threshold, the deeper reason it does not collapse:
Cardano needs the relation `β · γ = -p/3` between the two cube-roots,
which follows from `(βγ)^3 = -p^3/27` over `Q[p]`.  That step
(recognising that a product of generators satisfies a smaller minimal
polynomial than the generic compositum) requires a Gröbner-basis style
conjugate-pair analysis that neither Phase E nor any other part of the
current QA tower stack performs.

The pragmatic options for closing this gap would be:

- Extend `QAExt`/`QANum`/`QAUPoly` to support coefficients in `Q(params)`
  (function-field extension) so the standard Trager primitive-element
  construction runs unchanged over the bigger constant field.  This is
  a multi-day refactor of the QA substrate.
- Or, add a Gröbner basis over `Q(params)[α_1, ..., α_n]` capable of
  discovering derived relations (e.g. the conjugate-pair product
  reducing to a Q-element).  A separate plateau.

### Wiring

Phase E sits as a strict additive fallback in `src/rat.c`:

- `builtin_cancel_compute`: after the existing `auto_tower` paths (line
  ~1132) and before the inexact-handling branch.  Gated on `auto_flag &&
  !alpha` so explicit `Extension -> α` continues to flow through the
  pre-existing path.
- `builtin_together_compute`: same shape, after the multi-generator
  tower branch (line ~1402).

### Limitations

- Single distinct polynomial-radicand radical only.  Multi-radical
  inputs fall through unchanged (see the Cardano gap above).
- `Power[poly, p/q]` with reduced `p ≠ 1` is rejected.  The natural
  generator is `poly^(1/q)` and the user's surface form needs an
  `expand_radicals_to_atomic_poly`-style preprocessing pass that Phase E
  does not implement.
- No interaction with explicit `Extension -> Sqrt[poly]` — that path is
  controlled by `together_recursive_ext`, which is unchanged.

### Tests

18 new tests in `tests/test_extension_auto_builtins.c`:

- `test_phasee_together_sum_sqrt_poly` — the canonical sum-of-fractions
  collapse.
- `test_phasee_cancel_difference_of_squares` — rationalisation via
  `PolynomialExtendedGCD`.
- `test_phasee_single_fraction_passthrough` — confirms the size gate
  keeps the input when rationalisation would inflate.
- `test_phasee_sqrt_squared_reduction`,
  `test_phasee_sqrt_over_sqrt_collapses` — basic reductions.
- `test_phasee_cbrt_sum_combine`, `test_phasee_cbrt_cubed_reduction` —
  cube-root cases (q = 3).
- `test_phasee_quartic_radical` — q = 4.
- `test_phasee_no_extension_unchanged`,
  `test_phasee_no_radical_input_passthrough` — no-op cases.
- `test_phasee_integer_base_skipped` — integer-base radicals stay on
  the existing path.
- `test_phasee_multi_radical_no_collapse` — Cardano-style input
  unchanged (documents the limitation).
- `test_phasee_one_radical_two_params` — different polynomial radicand.
- `test_phasee_cancel_with_extra_factor`,
  `test_phasee_repeated_radical` — corner cases.
- `test_phasee_inexact_not_intercepted` — floating-point coexistence.
- `test_phasee_power_pq_nonunit_rejected` — `Power[poly, 2/3]` rejected.
- `test_phasee_sqrt_sum_collapse_zero` — exact-zero output.

## PolynomialGCD / PolynomialLCM: multivariate tower path (2026-05-25)

Extends the `Extension -> Automatic` tower path on `PolynomialGCD` and
`PolynomialLCM` to multivariate inputs — i.e. cases where the
substituted polynomials share more than one free variable besides the
internal γ.  The earlier univariate tower path (`qa_polynomialgcd_with_tower`,
`qa_polynomiallcm_with_tower`) requires exactly one polynomial variable
and returned `NULL` otherwise; the new multivariate fallback handles:

- single algebraic generator + 2+ poly variables
  (e.g. `PolynomialGCD[(a Sqrt[2] + 1) x, (a Sqrt[2] + 1) y]`),
- multiple algebraic generators + 2+ poly variables
  (e.g. `PolynomialGCD[(x^2 + y^2)(x ± Sqrt[2]), …]`),
- mixed Sqrt + cube-root generators across several poly variables.

Implementation (`qa_polynomialgcd_with_tower_multivar` /
`qa_polynomiallcm_with_tower_multivar` in `src/poly/qafactor.c`):

1. Substitute each α_i in every input with its polynomial-in-γ form
   (using QA_ALPHA_INTERNAL as the γ symbol).
2. Call the no-extension multivariate builtin
   (`internal_polynomialgcd` / `internal_polynomiallcm`) on the
   substituted form, treating γ as a polynomial variable.
3. Substitute γ → `t->gamma_render` and run Expand + evaluate to
   canonicalise (`Sqrt[c]^2 → c`, etc.).

Correctness boundary: this computes the GCD/LCM over `Q[γ, x, y, …]`
(γ as polynomial variable), not the canonical GCD/LCM over
`Q(γ)[x, y, …]` (γ algebraic mod its minimal polynomial).  The two
agree whenever the result has γ-degree strictly less than `deg(γ_min)`
and the inputs are γ-primitive.  When they differ, the returned
result remains a valid Q(γ)-common-divisor / -multiple but may carry
a polynomial-in-γ unit factor that the canonical form would normalise
away.  Tests in `tests/test_extension_auto_builtins.c` cover both the
agreeing cases (15 tests) and the boundary
(`test_pgcd_multivar_multi_alpha_two_vars_unit_factor` documents the
unit-factor case where Q[γ,x,y]-GCD picks up an extra γ-factor that
the canonical Q(γ)[x,y]-GCD would drop).

Default behaviour is unchanged: without `Extension -> Automatic` the
no-extension BPList path runs as before.

## PolynomialGCD / PolynomialLCM: multi-α tower path (2026-05-24)

`PolynomialGCD[..., Extension -> Automatic]` and
`PolynomialLCM[..., Extension -> Automatic]` now handle inputs whose
auto-detected algebraic extension contains two or more independent
generators (e.g. both `Sqrt[2]` and `Sqrt[3]`).  Previously the
multi-generator tower was constructed and then dropped on the floor;
the request fell through to the no-extension BPList path which only
recognises common literal factors, leaving e.g.

```mathematica
PolynomialLCM[x - Sqrt[2], x - Sqrt[3], Extension -> Automatic]
   -> (-Sqrt[2] + x) (-Sqrt[3] + x)         (* unevaluated symbolic product *)
```

The new path lifts each input to `QAUPoly[x]` over the compositum
`Q(γ)`, runs `qaupoly_gcd` directly (LCM = a·b / gcd folded
left-to-right), and renders the result with the tower's surface form
for γ.  Same input now collapses to:

```mathematica
PolynomialLCM[x - Sqrt[2], x - Sqrt[3], Extension -> Automatic]
   -> Sqrt[6] - Sqrt[2] x - Sqrt[3] x + x^2
PolynomialLCM[x - Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3], x - Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3], Extension -> Automatic]
   -> -1 - 2 Sqrt[2] x + x^2
PolynomialGCD[x^2 - 2 Sqrt[3] x + 1, x - Sqrt[3] - Sqrt[2], Extension -> Automatic]
   -> -Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3] + x
```

Scope (tier-1 limitation): the substituted inputs must share exactly
one polynomial variable besides the internal γ.  Multivariate inputs
fall through to the existing no-extension path unchanged.  Without
`Extension -> Automatic` the behaviour is unchanged — the standard
BPList path still produces the symbolic structural form.

Implementation: `qa_polynomialgcd_with_tower` and
`qa_polynomiallcm_with_tower` in `src/poly/qafactor.c`, sharing the
`tower_substitute_alphas` / `tower_lift_inputs` scaffold with
`qa_cancel_with_tower`.  Tests in `tests/test_extension_auto_builtins.c`
(seven `test_pgcd_multigen_*` / `test_plcm_multigen_*` cases).

## Power: split `Integer^(p/q)` into distinct-prime radicals (2026-05-24)

`Power[Integer, Rational]` now factorises the integer base into its
prime factorisation and emits a canonical product of distinct-prime
powers grouped by their reduced effective exponent, matching
Mathematica's surface form:

```mathematica
18^(1/3)  -> 2^(1/3) 3^(2/3)
12^(1/3)  -> 2^(2/3) 3^(1/3)
60^(1/3)  -> 2^(2/3) 15^(1/3)        (primes 3, 5 share eff 1/3)
50^(1/3)  -> 2^(1/3) 5^(2/3)
18^(2/3)  -> 3 2^(2/3) 3^(1/3)       (4/3 contributes int_part 1)
18^(5/3)  -> 54 2^(2/3) 3^(1/3)
98^(1/3)  -> 2^(1/3) 7^(2/3)
```

Existing extractions are unaffected:

```mathematica
6^(1/3)   -> 6^(1/3)                  (uniform exps — split adds no info)
30^(1/3)  -> 30^(1/3)
36^(1/3)  -> 6^(2/3)                  (find_min_perfect_base)
72^(1/3)  -> 2 3^(2/3)
8^(1/3)   -> 2
50^(1/2)  -> 5 Sqrt[2]
```

Implementation: `power_split_residue` in `src/power.c` trial-divides
the residue `r` (the part of `abs(n)` left after
`factor_out_kth_power` extracts the largest perfect q-th power), then
for each prime `p_i` with exponent `a_i` computes
`(int_i, d_i) = divmod(a_i * b_rem, q)`. The integer parts feed a
rational coefficient `∏ p_i^int_i`; the residual primes are grouped by
their reduced `(d_i / q)` exponent into one `Power[∏p_group, eff]` per
group. Triggers only when splitting strictly adds information (some
`int_i != 0` or the reduced exponents differ across primes) so
uniform-exponent inputs like `6^(1/3)` and `30^(1/3)` keep their
compact form.

Restricted to positive base with positive `b_rem`. Negative bases stay
in the existing `Power[res_base, b_rem/q]` shape so the `(-1)^(b/q)`
sign aggregation logic doesn't need to be rewired. Cases like
`18^(5/3)` (block-extracted as `18 · 18^(2/3)`) reach the split
naturally on the recursive evaluator pass, since `18^(2/3)` re-enters
`builtin_power` and hits the same fall-through.

The complementary `times.c` "generalised radical fusion" rule —
`Power[a, e_i] * Power[b, e_j]` collapse for related exponents —
was the canonical-form sibling of the old combined `Power[N, p/q]`
shape. It now skips fusion when both bases are coprime positive
integers and `|k| > 1`, so the new split form is stable instead of
being re-fused back. Useful fusions still fire:

```mathematica
Sqrt[2] Sqrt[3]            -> Sqrt[6]      (k = 1)
2^(1/3) 3^(1/3)            -> 6^(1/3)      (k = 1)
2^(1/3) 8^(2/3)            -> 4 2^(1/3)    (gcd 2, |k|=2 — cancellation)
12^(1/3) 2^(-2/3)          -> 3^(1/3)      (gcd 2, |k|=2 — cancellation)
2^(1/3) 3^(2/3)            -> 2^(1/3) 3^(2/3)  (coprime, |k|=2 — stays split)
```

## Added: `PossibleZeroQ` — hybrid symbolic-numeric zero recognition (2026-05-24)

`PossibleZeroQ[expr]` heuristically decides whether `expr` is identically
zero. Returns `True` / `False`; collapses uncertain cases to `True` per
Mathematica's `ztest1` policy. Attributes: `Listable | Protected`.

The implementation (`src/zero_test.c`, header `src/zero_test.h`) is a
four-stage pipeline, each stage exiting as soon as it produces a
definite verdict:

- **Stage 0** — constant-time structural shortcuts: literal `0`,
  `Complex[0, 0]`, named non-zero constants like `Pi`.
- **Stage 1** — rational normalisation via `Together`, `Cancel`,
  `Expand`, then `is_zero_poly` (existing in `src/poly/poly.c`). Decides
  every identity in `Q(x_1, …, x_n)` exactly.
- **Stage 2** — numeric precision ladder (53 → 200 → 500 → 1000 bits).
  Compares `|numericalize(e)|` against a lenient cancellation threshold
  `scale * 2^{-p + 30}`. Detects "MPFR didn't help" by checking whether
  the residual magnitude actually shrinks rung-over-rung — if it doesn't
  (e.g. `Sin` of `Complex[Real, Real]` which Mathilda evaluates with
  doubles regardless of precision), the prior verdict is taken as
  final. Uses a Plus-aware operand-magnitude scale that captures
  intermediate cancellation depth.
- **Stage 3** — Schwartz–Zippel probabilistic identity test for inputs
  with free symbols. Substitutes each free variable with an
  independently-drawn random sample from `R ∪ Complex[R, R]` and recurses
  into Stage 2. Requires four consecutive `True` trials.

Reference examples all match Mathematica behaviour:

```mathematica
PossibleZeroQ[E^(I Pi/4) - (-1)^(1/4)]              (* True  *)
PossibleZeroQ[(x + 1)(x - 1) - x^2 + 1]             (* True  *)
PossibleZeroQ[(E + Pi)^2 - E^2 - Pi^2 - 2 E Pi]     (* True  *)
PossibleZeroQ[E^Pi - Pi^E]                          (* False *)
PossibleZeroQ[2^(2 I) - 2^(-2 I) - 2 I Sin[Log[4]]] (* True  *)
PossibleZeroQ[1/x + 1/y - (x + y)/(x y)]            (* True  *)
PossibleZeroQ[Sqrt[x^2] - x]                        (* False *)
```

The full design rationale and literature survey (Richardson 1968,
Schwartz 1980, Zippel 1979, Bronstein 2005, Higham 2002, …) is in
`ZERO_RECOGNISE_PLAN.md` at the repository root.

Symbol registered in `src/sym_names.{c,h}`, attributes table updated in
`src/attr.c`, docstring added in `src/info.c`, dispatcher init wired
into `core_init` in `src/core.c`. Spec entry under
`docs/spec/builtins/expression-information.md`.

Tests: `tests/test_zero_test.c` — 72 cases across all four stages,
including a memory-leak smoke load and catastrophic-cancellation
regressions (`10^20 + 1 - 10^20 != 0`).

## Fix: `N[]` no longer returns NaN for complex MPFR powers (2026-05-24)

At MPFR precision, expressions like `N[(-1)^(1/4), 32]` and
`N[E^(I Pi/4), 64]` used to return `nan.0 + nan.0*I`. The `cpow` fallback
in `power.c` extracted operand values via a chain of
`type == EXPR_REAL ? ... : EXPR_INTEGER ? ... : EXPR_BIGINT ? ... : 0`,
which silently coerced any `EXPR_MPFR` operand to `0`. `cpow(0+0i, 0+0i)`
then produced NaN.

The build doesn't link MPC, so true complex MPFR arithmetic isn't
available. Instead `numeric.c` now provides `numeric_mpfr_complex_pow`,
a polar-form implementation that handles complex-valued powers at
arbitrary precision:

    base = r * exp(i*theta),  exp = c + i*d
    base^exp = r^c * exp(-d*theta)
               * (cos(c*theta + d*ln(r)) + I*sin(c*theta + d*ln(r)))

All sub-operations (`mpfr_hypot`, `mpfr_atan2`, `mpfr_pow`, `mpfr_log`,
`mpfr_exp`, `mpfr_cos`, `mpfr_sin`) operate at the combined target
precision, so the result carries the requested number of digits rather
than being demoted to machine precision.

`src/power.c` calls the new helper immediately after the existing real
MPFR `mpfr_pow` fast path and before the `cpow` fallback, gated on
`numeric_any_mpfr(base, exp)`. The helper returns `NULL` for inputs it
can't approximate, leaving downstream paths intact.

`tests/test_numeric.c::test_n_prec_complex_pow` exercises the two cases
from the bug report plus `I^I`.

## Fix: Element[{x,y,...}, dom] now behaves as a conjunction (2026-05-23)

`Element[{x1, ..., xN}, dom]` is shorthand for
`Element[x1, dom] && ... && Element[xN, dom]`. Previously,
`builtin_element` always threaded the call into a `List` of per-element
`Element[xi, dom]` calls. Because `Simplify` carries `ATTR_LISTABLE` on
its assumption argument, this caused inputs like
`Simplify[Log[E^(x+y)], Element[{x, y}, Reals]]` to thread `Simplify`
itself over the list of partial facts, so each branch saw only one of
the variables. The result was a bogus list
`{Log[E^(x+y)], Log[E^(x+y)]}` instead of the expected `x + y`.

Two coordinated changes:

- `src/simp/simp_builtins.c::builtin_element`: when the first arg is a
  list, evaluate `Element[xi, dom]` on each component and collapse to a
  single `True` / `False` only when every sub-call decides. When any
  component is undecided, return `NULL` so the original
  `Element[{x1,...,xN}, dom]` expression stays in place.
- `src/simp/simp_assume.c::ctx_walk`: recognise
  `Element[{x1,...,xN}, dom]` as a fact and split it into per-variable
  `Element[xi, dom]` facts when building the `AssumeCtx`, so
  `prov_re` / `fact_in_domain` continue to see the joint assumption
  per-variable.

Also introduces `SYM_Element` in `sym_names.{c,h}` for the
pointer-compare fast path in `ctx_walk`.

`tests/test_element.c::test_element_threads_over_list` updated to
reflect the new semantics (joint `True` / `False` rather than a
threaded list) and now also covers the undecided-and-Simplify case.

## simp: split simp.c into 18 sibling .c modules (2026-05-23)

The monolithic ~12 kLoC `src/simp/simp.c` translation unit has been split
into 18 sibling `.c` files plus a shared `src/simp/simp_internal.h`
header carrying the cross-module surface (4 shared types and ~64
function declarations). No behavioural change -- this is a pure
mechanical refactor; function bodies are byte-for-byte identical to the
pre-split file.

The new layout:

| File | Subject |
|---|---|
| `simp.c` | Module entry point (`simp_init`) only |
| `simp_complexity.c` | Default complexity measure + `SimplifyCount` |
| `simp_assume.c` | `AssumeCtx` + domain queries (`prov_*`) |
| `simp_util.c` | Tracing, `CandSet`, scoring helpers |
| `simp_assume_rewrite.c` | Assumption-driven seed rewriters |
| `simp_trig_roundtrip.c` | Trig/exp roundtrip composite |
| `simp_denest.c` | Radical canon + sqrt-of-sqrt + multi-extension denesting |
| `simp_cuberoot.c` | Cube-root denesting and sum-of-conjugates |
| `simp_rationalize.c` | Denominator rationalisation |
| `simp_algebraic.c` | Algebraic-extension reduction |
| `simp_canon.c` | Common-factor lift + sign canonicalisation |
| `simp_trig_pi.c` | Trig at rational multiples of Pi + Pythag transforms |
| `simp_power.c` | `PrimeRebase`, `PowerOneify`, `PowerDistribute`, `RadicalCanon` |
| `simp_tan_add.c` | Tan addition-formula rewrites |
| `simp_logexp_abs.c` | Log/Power rewriter, `Abs`, `Sqrt[e^2]` |
| `simp_search.c` | Heuristic search, shape classifier, pipelines, additive splitter |
| `simp_factorial.c` | `simp_factorial` |
| `simp_bottomup.c` | `SimpMemo` + bottom-up recursive driver |
| `simp_builtins.c` | `Element`, equation rebalancing, `Simplify`, `Assuming` |

The makefile auto-discovers `src/simp/*.c`; `tests/CMakeLists.txt` was
extended to list the new files. All 10 simp test suites pass unchanged
(`simp_tests`, `simplify_tests`, `factorial_simplify_tests`,
`invtrig_simplify_tests`, `logexp_simplify_tests`,
`radical_simplify_tests`, `simp_algebraic_cuberoot_tests`,
`simp_denest_inv_sqrt_tests`, `simp_denest_phase2_tests`,
`simp_log_tests`).

## simp_log -- dedicated logarithm-simplification sub-module (2026-05-23)

A new `src/simp/simp_log.{c,h}` sub-module fires inside both
`simp_pipeline_logexp` and the simp_search seed phase to close a class
of Log identities that the existing positivity-aware LogExp cascade
missed. It implements two orthogonal primitives:

- **Prime decomposition of Log[positive rational]**: every Log[r]
  subexpression whose argument is a positive integer or rational p/q is
  replaced by the integer linear combination
  `Sum e_i Log[p_i] - Sum f_j Log[q_j]` obtained by prime-factoring p
  and q through `FactorInteger`. Also recognises `Log[Power[r, k]]`,
  rewriting as `k * decomposition(Log[r])`. Sound unconditionally.
  Closes the previously unsimplified `-4 Log[4] + 8 Log[2] -> 0`,
  `Log[72] - 3 Log[2] - 2 Log[3] -> 0`, `Log[2/3] + Log[3/4] +
  Log[4/5] - Log[2/5] -> 0`, `Log[Sqrt[12]] - Log[2] - 1/2 Log[3]
  -> 0`, and `Log[2,5] Log[5,8] - 3 -> 0`.

- **Linear-combination-of-logs fuser**: every Plus subexpression
  whose addends decompose as `Sum c_i Log[a_i] + R` is rewritten by
  fusing the log block into a single `Log[Product a_i^c_i]`. The fused
  argument is canonicalised via `Together`, `Expand`, and a single
  depth-bounded `Simplify` so that algebraic identities like
  `(x^2 - y^2) / ((x-y)(x+y)) = 1` and the Pythagorean
  `(Sec[x] - Tan[x])(Sec[x] + Tan[x]) = 1` collapse the fused Log to
  Log[1] = 0. Gated on provable positivity of every a_i when the
  fused form is not a near-atomic constant.

The two passes iterate with the existing `LogExpRules` cascade inside
`simp_pipeline_logexp` to a small fixed point (cap 3 rounds), so a
fused `Log[E^a]` is then collapsed to `a` via the realness-aware
`Log[E^k] -> k` rewrite for real-symbolic a.

Recursion into `simp_log_apply` from the recursive `Simplify` call is
bounded by `simp_log_depth`, capped at 2 to keep the cost bounded.

A new 20-case unit suite in `tests/test_simp_log.c` exercises every
test in the original user logTestSuite, plus three regression guards
that confirm single-Log inputs, `Log[1]`, and a single Plus log term
are not over-rewritten.

## System floating-point constants $MachinePrecision, $MachineEpsilon, $MinMachineNumber, $MaxMachineNumber, $MaxNumber, $MinNumber (2026-05-23)

Registered six read-only system variables describing the local
floating-point range and granularity. Each is bound as an `OwnValue` in
a new `system_constants_init()` helper in `src/core.c` (called from
`core_init()` immediately after `eval_init()`) and marked `Protected`.

Values are derived from the platform's `<float.h>` macros — not
hard-coded — so they track the float ABI Mathilda was compiled
against:

| Symbol | Source |
|--------|--------|
| `$MachinePrecision` | `DBL_MANT_DIG * Log10[2]` (≈ 15.9546 on IEEE 754) |
| `$MachineEpsilon`   | `DBL_EPSILON` |
| `$MinMachineNumber` | `DBL_MIN` |
| `$MaxMachineNumber` | `DBL_MAX` |
| `$MaxNumber`        | `USE_MPFR`: `mpfr_nextbelow(+inf)` at `DBL_MANT_DIG` bits; else `DBL_MAX` |
| `$MinNumber`        | `USE_MPFR`: `mpfr_nextabove(0)` at `DBL_MANT_DIG` bits; else `DBL_MIN` |

The previous hard-coded `15.954589770191003` magic number that the
parser used as the *machine-precision threshold* (above which a real
literal is promoted to MPFR) is now driven by the same derivation:
`NUMERIC_MACHINE_PRECISION_DIGITS` in `src/numeric.h` is defined as
`((double)DBL_MANT_DIG * NUMERIC_LOG10_2)`. `src/parse.c` and
`src/precision.c` use that macro instead of the previous literal.

Docstrings are registered in `src/info.c`; new `SYM_DollarMachineEpsilon`,
`SYM_DollarMachinePrecision`, `SYM_DollarMaxMachineNumber`,
`SYM_DollarMaxNumber`, `SYM_DollarMinMachineNumber`, `SYM_DollarMinNumber`
entries are added to `src/sym_names.{c,h}` (the first `$`-prefixed
interned symbols in the file).

```mathematica
In[1]:= $MachinePrecision
Out[1]= 15.9546

In[2]:= $MachinePrecision == 53 Log[10, 2]
Out[2]= True

In[3]:= {$MinMachineNumber, $MaxMachineNumber}
Out[3]= {2.22507*10^-308, 1.79769*10^308}

In[4]:= {MachineNumberQ[$MaxMachineNumber], MachineNumberQ[$MaxNumber]}
Out[4]= {True, False}

In[5]:= $MachinePrecision = 42
Set::wrsym: Symbol $MachinePrecision is Protected.
```

## MachineNumberQ predicate (2026-05-23)

Added `MachineNumberQ[expr]` in `src/numeric.c`. Returns `True` iff
`expr` is a machine-precision IEEE-double real (finite — `+inf`, `-inf`,
and `NaN` are rejected via `isfinite()`) or a `Complex` of two such
reals. Exact numbers (Integer, BigInt, Rational), arbitrary-precision
reals (`EXPR_MPFR`, e.g. from `N[Pi, 30]` or any literal with > ~16
mantissa digits), and non-numeric atoms all return `False`. A `Complex`
needs *both* parts to be finite machine reals — `Complex[1, 2]` (an
exact Gaussian integer) and `Complex[N[1, 30], N[1, 30]]` both yield
`False`, matching Wolfram Language semantics.

Attributes: `Protected` (intentionally *not* `Listable`; `MachineNumberQ`
on a list inspects the `List` atom as a whole).

```mathematica
In[1]:= MachineNumberQ[Sin[1000.]]
Out[1]= True

In[2]:= MachineNumberQ[Exp[1000.]]            (* overflows to +inf *)
Out[2]= False

In[3]:= MachineNumberQ[-29037945.290347]
Out[3]= True

In[4]:= MachineNumberQ[-29037852093587905730945.29034875093457832094573984537498]
Out[4]= False                                 (* MPFR via parser auto-promote *)
```

Test coverage: `tests/test_machine_number_q.c` (27 tests) — documented
examples, every numeric leaf type, IEEE special values, MPFR via
`N[..., n]` and high-precision literal, Complex variants, non-numeric
inputs, arity mismatches, attributes/docstring/symbol introspection,
and a repeated-evaluation stress loop for valgrind coverage.

## Precision-aware real-literal parsing (2026-05-23)

The parser now picks `EXPR_REAL` vs `EXPR_MPFR` automatically based on
the number of significant digits typed in the *mantissa* of a real
literal. Previously every literal with a `.` or `e/E` became a machine
double, silently discarding the extra precision a user typed. Now:

- A literal whose implied precision is **≤ MachinePrecision** (≈ 15.95
  decimal digits) parses as `EXPR_REAL` — unchanged behaviour for
  ordinary inputs such as `3.14`, `0.5`, `1.0e22`.
- A literal whose implied precision **exceeds MachinePrecision** parses
  as `EXPR_MPFR` at `ceil(implied × log2(10))` bits, fed directly from
  the literal text via `mpfr_set_str` (no lossy double round-trip).

Implied precision uses the mantissa only — the exponent does not count:

    implied = digits_after_decimal + log10(|mantissa_value|)

This matches Mathematica, where `1.0e22` keeps `MachinePrecision`
(mantissa `1.0` has implied precision ≈ 1) but
`1.123456789012345678e22` is high precision (mantissa precision ≈ 18).

**Examples** (matching the Mathematica reference output):

    In[1] := -29037945.290347
    Out[1] = -2.90379e+07         (* EXPR_REAL *)
    In[2] := Precision[%]
    Out[2] = MachinePrecision     (* implied ≈ 13.46, below threshold *)

    In[3] := -29037852093587905730945.29034875093457832094573984537498
    Out[3] = -29037852093587905730945.29034875093457832094573984537498
    In[4] := Precision[%]
    Out[4] = 54.4864              (* implied ≈ 54.463, MPFR @ 181 bits *)
    In[5] := Accuracy[%%]
    Out[5] = 32.0235

    In[6] := -29037852093587905730945.2903487509345783209457398453749803489530945034950
    In[7] := Precision[%]
    Out[7] = 71.6451              (* MPFR @ 238 bits *)

The reported `Precision[]` differs from Mathematica's value by less than
0.2 digits because `Precision[]` returns `bits / log2(10)` with bits
quantised to integers; Mathematica appears to store the precision as a
continuous real. `Accuracy[]` follows the same offset because
`Accuracy = Precision − log10(|x|)`. End-to-end ordering (which side of
MachinePrecision a literal falls on, and which MPFR bit count it gets)
is identical.

**Always machine precision (never auto-promoted)** — preserves
existing semantics for code that relies on machine doubles:
- pure integer literals (`123`, `99999999999999999999`) — still
  `EXPR_INTEGER` / `EXPR_BIGINT`;
- real literals without a `.` (`1e10`, `5e-3`);
- zero literals regardless of trailing zeros (`0.0`, `0.000`,
  `0.0000000000000000000`);
- low-mantissa-precision scientific / scaled-scientific (`1.0e22`,
  `1.0*^22`).

**Backwards compatibility** — explicit Mathematica-style precision
suffixes still override the implicit decision. `3.14`50`,
`3.14``49`, and `3``50` all behave exactly as before.

**Implementation** — `src/parse.c` `parse_number()` real branch:
the literal is scanned once into a mantissa span and a full-literal
span, the implied precision is computed from the mantissa portion
only, and the result is built either via `expr_new_real(strtod(...))`
or `expr_new_mpfr_from_str(..., bits)`. The change is entirely local
to the literal-construction step; the existing precision-suffix
handler and `*^`-scaling code at the end of `parse_number()` are
unchanged.

**Tests** — new `tests/test_parser_precision.c` (23 test functions
across 13 categories) covers: basic machine/MPFR paths, negative
literals, threshold boundary, the three user-provided examples,
scientific and scaled notation, zero handling, integer pass-through,
backtick-suffix backwards compatibility, `Precision[]`/`Accuracy[]`
integration, MPFR-value round-trip (parser feeds the literal text to
`mpfr_set_str` directly, not via a double), 100-digit literals, and
fractions without integer parts.

---

## RealExponent (2026-05-23)

New built-in `RealExponent[x]` / `RealExponent[x, b]` -- the base-10 (or
base-`b`) real exponent of a real number, `Log[b, |x|]`.  The 1-argument
form defaults to base 10.

- Implementation: added in `src/real.c` (+ `src/real.h`), reusing the
  numeric classifier `rd_classify` and the rational-bigint detector
  `rd_is_rational_bigint` from the existing `RealDigits` /
  `MantissaExponent` machinery.  Registered in `real_init()` with
  `Protected | Listable` attributes.  Symbol `SYM_RealExponent`
  interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`; docstring added in `src/info.c`.
- Accepted numeric kinds: `Integer`, `BigInt`, `Rational`, `Real`, and
  (under `USE_MPFR`) `MPFR`.  Symbolic numeric leaves (`Pi`, `E`,
  `EulerGamma`, `Catalan`, `GoldenRatio`, `Degree`) and numeric-valued
  composites such as `Pi^Pi` or `1/Pi` route through `numericalize` at
  the combined working precision, then take the same path as a numeric
  literal.  Plain symbols with no numeric value are left unevaluated
  with no diagnostic.
- Output kind contagion -- only the **original** inputs (pre-
  numericalize) drive the choice:
  - Either `x` or `b` is MPFR  ->  result is MPFR at the higher of the
    input precisions.
  - Neither is MPFR  ->  result is a machine `Real`.
  This avoids spuriously promoting `RealExponent[Pi^Pi]` to MPFR just
  because the internal numericalize step uses MPFR at 64 working bits.
- Sign of `x` is discarded (`RealExponent[-x] == RealExponent[x]`).
- Zero handling follows Mathilda's `Accuracy` convention (every zero
  has `Accuracy = Infinity`, so `-Accuracy[0] = -Infinity`):
  - `RealExponent[0]`     -> `-Infinity`
  - `RealExponent[0.]`    -> `-Infinity`
  - `RealExponent[0``p]`  -> `-Infinity`
  This is a documented divergence from Mathematica's
  `RealExponent[0.] = -307.65...`; matching that requires changing
  `Accuracy[0.]` in `src/precision.c` first and is deferred.
- Base validation: the base must be a real number `> 1`.  Integer 1, 0,
  negative integers, `Rational` `<= 1`, `Real` `<= 1`, MPFR `<= 1`, and
  complex bases all emit `RealExponent::ibase` and leave the call
  unevaluated.
- Diagnostics (stderr; call is then left unevaluated):
  - `RealExponent::argt: RealExponent called with N argument(s); 1 or 2
    arguments are expected.` -- argc outside `[1, 2]`.
  - `RealExponent::realx: The value <x> is not a real number.` --
    `Complex[re, im]` with non-zero imaginary part at position 1.
  - `RealExponent::ibase: Base <b> is not a real number greater than 1.`
    -- base `<= 1`, non-positive, or complex.
- Computation path (USE_MPFR build):
  1. Numericalize symbolic inputs at working precision = `max(64,
     prec(x) + 32, prec(b) + 32)`.
  2. Convert `|x|` and `b` to MPFR via `mpfr_set_si` / `mpfr_set_z` /
     `mpfr_set_d` / `mpfr_set_q` / `mpfr_set` as appropriate.
  3. Compute `log(|x|) / log(b)` at working precision + 32 guard bits.
  4. Round to output precision (machine `Real` via `mpfr_get_d`, or
     MPFR via `expr_new_mpfr_move`).
- Tests: `tests/test_real_exponent.c` -- integer / bigint / rational /
  machine-real / MPFR coverage, base 2 / 3 / 5 / 7 / 10 / 16 / `E`,
  identities `RealExponent[xy] == RealExponent[x] + RealExponent[y]`
  and `RealExponent[b^p] == p * RealExponent[b]`, listable threading,
  symbolic constants (`Pi`, `Pi^Pi`, `Pi` with base `E`), every zero
  edge case, all error paths (argt / realx / ibase across multiple
  invalid bases), the symbolic-leave-unevaluated path, attributes /
  docstring / interned symbol introspection, and a memory-safety stress
  loop.  41 tests, all passing.

## MantissaExponent (2026-05-23)

New built-in `MantissaExponent[x]` / `MantissaExponent[x, b]` -- canonical
mantissa-exponent decomposition of a real number, such that `x = m * b^e`
with the mantissa in `1/b <= |m| < 1` (or `{0, 0}` when `x` is zero).
The 1-argument form defaults to base 10.

- Implementation: added in `src/real.c` (+ `src/real.h`), sharing the
  rational-natural-exponent helper `rd_rational_natural_exp` and numeric
  classifier `rd_classify` with `RealDigits`.  Registered in `real_init()`
  with `Protected | Listable` attributes.  Symbol `SYM_MantissaExponent`
  interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`; docstring added in `src/info.c`.
- Exact path (`Integer`, `BigInt`, `Rational`): the mantissa is built as
  an exact `Rational[num, den * b^e]` via pure GMP / mpq arithmetic, then
  canonicalized so common factors with `b^e` are reduced.  Sign of `x`
  carries through to the mantissa's numerator.
- Machine `Real` path: natural exponent via `floor(log(|x|) / log(b)) + 1`
  with an off-by-one correction for the rare double-rounding boundary
  case; mantissa via direct division by `pow(b, e)`.
- MPFR path: natural exponent via `mpfr_log` at +64 bits of guard
  precision, mantissa via `mpfr_pow_si` + division at the input
  precision.  Same off-by-one correction relative to the `1/b <= |m| < 1`
  band.  Mantissa Expr is built via `expr_new_mpfr_copy` so the result's
  precision exactly matches the input.
- `0` and `0.` are returned as `{0, 0}` and `{0.0, 0}` respectively; MPFR
  zero returns an MPFR zero at the same precision.
- Diagnostics (stderr; call is then left unevaluated):
  - `MantissaExponent::argt: MantissaExponent called with N argument(s);
    1 or 2 arguments are expected.` -- argc outside `[1, 2]`.
  - `MantissaExponent::realx: The value <x> is not a real number.` --
    `Complex[re, im]` with non-zero imaginary part.
  - `MantissaExponent::ibase: Base <b> is not an integer greater than 1.`
    -- integer base `< 2`, or base larger than `ULONG_MAX`.
- Non-integer bases (`Real`, `Rational`, symbolic `E`) currently leave
  the call unevaluated silently rather than diagnosing -- supporting them
  is a follow-up that requires symbolic / inexact base arithmetic for
  mantissa construction.
- Symbolic (non-numeric) arguments are left unevaluated with no
  diagnostic, matching Mathematica's `MantissaExponent[x]` behaviour.
- Tests: `tests/test_mantissa_exponent.c` -- integer / bigint / rational
  / machine-real / MPFR coverage, base 2 / 10 / 16 / 256, zero edge cases
  in every numeric kind, the fundamental identity `m * b^e == x` for both
  exact and MPFR inputs, listable threading, all four error paths, the
  symbolic-leave-unevaluated path, attributes / docstring / interned
  symbol introspection, and a memory-safety stress loop.  Valgrind clean
  against the same macOS-startup baseline as `real_digits_tests`.

## IntegerString (2026-05-23)

New built-in `IntegerString[n]` / `IntegerString[n, b]` /
`IntegerString[n, b, len]` -- decimal-digit (or base-`b`) string rendering
of an integer.  The 1-argument form defaults to base 10; the 2-argument
form supports `2 <= b <= 36` with digit values `10`-`35` rendered as
lowercase `a`-`z`; the 3-argument form left-pads with `'0'` to length `len`
(or, when `len` is smaller than the natural digit count, returns the `len`
least-significant digits).  Matches Mathematica's surface semantics
verbatim.

- Implementation: extends `src/int.c` (+ `src/int.h`).  Registered in
  `int_init()` alongside `IntegerDigits` / `IntegerLength` / `DigitCount` /
  `FromDigits` / `IntegerExponent`.  Attributes `Protected | Listable`
  applied in `int_init()`.  Symbol `SYM_IntegerString` interned in
  `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.  Docstring registered in `src/info.c`.
- Digit rendering routes through GMP's `mpz_get_str`, which converts an
  arbitrary-precision integer to a base-`b` digit string in one library
  call (for positive bases `2..36` it emits `0..9`,`a..z` exactly matching
  Mathematica's convention).  The padding / truncation pass is a single
  `memcpy` / `memset` over the resulting buffer.  Result is therefore
  essentially free even for inputs like `100!` or `2^100`.
- Sign of `n` is discarded.  `IntegerString[0]` is `"0"`;
  `IntegerString[n, b, 0]` is `""`.
- Diagnostics (stderr; call is then left unevaluated):
  - `IntegerString::argb: IntegerString called with N argument(s); between
    1 and 3 arguments are expected.` -- argc outside `[1, 3]`.
  - `IntegerString::int: Integer expected at position <pos> in <call>.` --
    concrete non-integer numeric (Real, Rational, Complex) at position 1
    or 3.  Pure symbolic args flow through silently.
  - `IntegerString::basf: <b> is not a valid base for IntegerString in
    <call>; the base must be an integer between 2 and 36.` -- non-integer
    or out-of-range base (covers `0`, `1`, negative, fractional / Real /
    Complex, and integers `>= 37`).
  - `IntegerString::intnn: Non-negative machine-sized integer expected at
    position 3.` -- negative or bignum `len`.
- Test suite: `tests/test_integer_string.c` (53 cases, registered in
  `tests/CMakeLists.txt` as `integer_string_tests`).  Covers documented
  examples verbatim (`17651` in base 2 -> `"100010011110011"`, `50!` in
  base 16 and base 36), every base from 2 / 3 / 7 / 8 / 10 / 11..15 / 16 /
  25 / 36 (boundary) with single-digit and multi-digit inputs, the
  pad-with-leading-zeros and len-less-than-digits cases on machine ints
  and bignums (including `2^100` in binary / hex and `100!` in decimal),
  the listable threading axis (on `n`, on `b`, on both, nested, and
  combined with padding), round-trip identities
  `FromDigits[IntegerString[n, b], b] == n` and
  `StringLength[IntegerString[n, b]] == IntegerLength[n, b]`, sign-discard
  on negative bignums, every error path
  (0 args / 4 args / Real / Rational / Complex `n` / base 0 / 1 / -3 /
  37 / 50 / 2.5 / negative `len` / real `len`), symbolic-args
  silent-unevaluated, attribute / docstring / interned-symbol
  introspection, and a 50-iteration repeated-evaluation stress loop for
  valgrind.  All tests pass cleanly; valgrind reports only system-library
  leaks (libobjc / libdyld on Darwin) unrelated to Mathilda.

## RealDigits (2026-05-23)

New built-in `RealDigits[x]` / `RealDigits[x, b]` / `RealDigits[x, b, len]`
/ `RealDigits[x, b, len, n]` -- positional-notation digit expansion of an
approximate or exact real number. Result is `{digits, exp}` with the first
digit being the coefficient of `b^(exp - 1)`. Sign of `x` is discarded.

- Implementation: new files `src/real.c` (+ `src/real.h`); registered in
  `core_init()` between `int_init()` and `attr_init()`. Attributes
  `Protected | Listable` applied in `real_init()`. Symbol `SYM_RealDigits`
  interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`. Docstring registered in `src/info.c`.
- Numeric kinds handled uniformly: `Integer`, `BigInt`, `Rational`,
  machine `Real`, and `EXPR_MPFR` (under `USE_MPFR`). Symbolic numeric
  constants such as `Pi`, `E`, and `GoldenRatio` are numericalized via
  `numericalize` to enough MPFR bits to satisfy the requested base/length
  when an explicit `len` is given.
- Algorithm:
  - Exact (Integer / Rational) with no explicit `len`: remainder-tracked
    long division detects terminating vs recurring expansions. Recurring
    rationals return a nested-list block, e.g.
    `RealDigits[19/7] == {{2, {7, 1, 4, 2, 8, 5}}, 1}`.
  - General path (explicit `len` and/or `n`, or inexact `x`): scale
    `|x|` by `base^(-low)` where `low = start_pos - len + 1`, floor to an
    mpz, and read off base-`b` digits LSD-first. Pure mpz / mpq arithmetic
    for exact inputs guarantees bit-exact answers regardless of `low`.
  - Inexact path: `mpfr_get_str(.., MPFR_RNDN, avail)` produces the
    canonical round-to-nearest digits at the value's actual precision
    (`53` bits for machine doubles, `mpfr_get_prec` for MPFR). This
    yields the "shortest round-trip" decimal form Mathematica uses --
    `RealDigits[123.55555]` returns the literal `1,2,3,5,5,5,5,5,0,...`
    instead of the IEEE binary tail.
  - Available precision in base `b` is `Round[Precision[x]/Log10[b]]`.
    Requested positions below that are filled with `Indeterminate`;
    positions above the natural exponent are filled with `0`.
  - Zero special case: `RealDigits[0] -> {{0}, 0}`,
    `RealDigits[0.] -> {{0}, -Floor[Accuracy[0.]]}`. For machine doubles
    `Accuracy[0.] = 15.95` so the result is `{{0}, -15}`.
- Restrictions: bases must be integers `>= 2` and fit in `unsigned long`.
  Non-integer bases (e.g. `GoldenRatio`) trip `RealDigits::ibase` and
  leave the call unevaluated; supporting them requires MPFR floor
  iteration and has been deferred.
- Diagnostics (stderr; call is then left unevaluated):
  - `RealDigits::argb` -- argc outside `[1, 4]`.
  - `RealDigits::realx` -- concrete non-real numeric (Complex with
    non-zero imaginary part).
  - `RealDigits::ibase` -- base not an integer `>= 2` (covers `0`, `1`,
    negative, non-integer, and bignum bases > ULONG_MAX).
  - `RealDigits::intnn` -- non-negative integer expected at position 3
    (`len`).
  - `RealDigits::int` -- integer expected at position 4 (`n`).
  - `RealDigits::ovfl` -- requested `len` exceeds `REAL_MAX_LEN`
    (1_000_000 digits).
- Test suite: `tests/test_real_digits.c` (49 cases, registered in
  `tests/CMakeLists.txt` as `real_digits_tests`). Covers documented
  Mathematica examples verbatim (`58127`, `123.55555`, `Pi @ 25 digits`,
  `19/7` with and without explicit `len`, `Pi @ 20 digits starting at
  10^-5` / `10^5`, `1.234` in base 2 to 15 digits, `5.635` with
  Indeterminate fill and offset start), exact rationals (terminating
  and recurring: `1/3, 1/6, 1/7, 1/8`), MPFR inputs via `N[Pi, 50]` and
  `N[Pi, 100]`, sign discard, bignum integers (`2^100` in base 2 = 101
  digits), listable threading, zero special cases, every error path,
  attribute / docstring / interned-symbol introspection, and a 30-iteration
  repeated-evaluation stress loop for valgrind. All tests pass cleanly
  under `valgrind --leak-check=full` (system-library leaks from libobjc
  / libdyld are unrelated to Mathilda).

## IntegerExponent (2026-05-23)

New built-in `IntegerExponent[n]` / `IntegerExponent[n, b]` -- highest
power of `b` dividing `n`, equivalently the number of trailing zeros in
the base-`b` digits of `|n|`. The 1-argument form defaults to base 10,
matching Mathematica's surface semantics.

- Implementation: extends `src/int.c` (+ `src/int.h`). Registered in
  `int_init()` alongside `IntegerDigits` / `IntegerLength` / `DigitCount` /
  `FromDigits`. Attributes `Protected | Listable` applied in
  `int_init()`. Symbol `SYM_IntegerExponent` interned in
  `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- Base 2 fast path uses GMP's `mpz_scan1` (O(log n / wordsize)) — the
  position of the lowest set bit is exactly the 2-adic valuation; sign of
  `n` does not need to be stripped because GMP's two's-complement view
  preserves trailing zeros for both signs. General bases use
  `mpz_remove`, a single library call that divides `|n|` by `b` as many
  times as possible and returns that count.
- Sign of `n` is discarded. `IntegerExponent[0, b] -> Infinity` for any
  base (every power of `b` divides 0). Works uniformly for machine
  integers, bignum `n`, and bignum bases (e.g. `IntegerExponent[
  (10^18 + 1)^3, 10^18 + 1] == 3`).
- Diagnostics (stderr; call is then left unevaluated):
  - `IntegerExponent::argt: IntegerExponent called with N argument(s);
    1 or 2 arguments are expected.` -- fires for `argc == 0` or
    `argc >= 3`.
  - `IntegerExponent::int: Integer expected at position <pos> in
    <call>.` -- concrete non-integer numeric (Real, Rational, Complex)
    at position 1 or 2. Pure symbolic args flow through silently.
  - `IntegerExponent::ibase: Base argument must be an integer >= 2.` --
    fires for an integer base `<= 1`.
- Test suite: `tests/test_integer_exponent.c` (50 cases, registered in
  `tests/CMakeLists.txt` as `integer_exponent_tests`). Covers documented
  examples verbatim (`1230000 -> 4`, `2^10 + 2^7` in base 2 `-> 7`,
  `144` in base 2 `-> 4` -- spec's `2^^10010000` syntax is not parsed
  by Mathilda, so the equivalent decimal `144` is used), Legendre's-formula
  identities on
  `100!` (`IntegerExponent[100!, 2] == 97`, `IntegerExponent[100!, 5] ==
  24`), the `2^100 * 3^50` mixed product across bases 2, 3, 6, bignum
  bases (`(10^18 + 1)^k`), zero-as-Infinity in every base, the
  divisibility property `Mod[n, b^IntegerExponent[n,b]] == 0 &&
  Mod[n, b^(IntegerExponent[n,b]+1)] != 0`, listable threading on `n`,
  on `b`, on both, and nested, every error path, and a 50-iteration
  repeated-evaluation stress loop for valgrind. Docstring registered in
  `src/info.c`.

## FromDigits (2026-05-23)

New built-in `FromDigits[list]` / `FromDigits[list, b]` /
`FromDigits["string"]` / `FromDigits["string", b]` -- the inverse of
`IntegerDigits` / `IntegerString`. Reconstructs a number from its
most-significant-first digit list (or character string) in a chosen
base, matching Mathematica's surface semantics.

- Implementation: extends `src/int.c` (+ `src/int.h`). Registered in
  `int_init()` alongside `IntegerDigits` / `IntegerLength` /
  `DigitCount`. Attribute `Protected` (intentionally **not**
  `Listable` -- the first argument *is* a list) declared in
  `src/attr.c` and re-applied in `int_init()`. Symbol
  `SYM_FromDigits` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- The all-integer fast path (every list digit AND the base are
  integer-like) is computed via Horner in GMP and demoted to
  `EXPR_INTEGER` when the result fits in `int64`, else returned as
  an `EXPR_BIGINT`. Empty list -> 0. Digits in the list need not be
  smaller than the base; they are "carried" through the Horner
  accumulation (matching Mathematica:
  `FromDigits[{7, 11, 0, 0, 0, 122}] == 810122`). Negative digits
  are also handled correctly.
- The symbolic / non-integer path (any Real, Rational, Complex, or
  symbolic digit OR base) builds the explicit Horner sum
  `Plus[Times[d[0], Power[b, n-1]], ..., d[n-1]]` and hands it back
  to the evaluator. Single code path covers symbolic base
  (`FromDigits[{1, 2, 3}, b] == 3 + 2 b + b^2`), mixed digits
  (`FromDigits[{1, a, 3}, 10] == 103 + 10 a`), full symbolic
  (`FromDigits[{a, b, c, d, e}, x] == e + d x + c x^2 + b x^3 + a x^4`),
  Real / Rational base (`FromDigits[{2, 3, 4}, 2.5] == 24.0`,
  `FromDigits[{1, 2, 3}, 1/2] == 17/4`).
- The string form decodes each character against the `[0-9a-zA-Z]`
  alphabet (`0`-`9` -> `0`-`9`, `a`-`z` / `A`-`Z` -> `10`-`35`)
  case-insensitively. Characters greater than the base are still
  decoded and carried (matching `FromDigits["1A3C"] == 2042`). Empty
  string -> 0. Base over a string is required to be an
  integer >= 2; a symbolic base over a string leaves the call
  unevaluated silently.
- Round-trip property `FromDigits[IntegerDigits[n]] == Abs[n]`
  (sign-discarding form) is asserted across machine-int, bignum, and
  bases 2-256 in the test suite, including `FromDigits[IntegerDigits[100!]]
  == 100!`.
- Diagnostics (stderr; call is then left unevaluated):
  - `FromDigits::argb: FromDigits called with N argument(s); 1 or 2
    arguments are expected.` -- fires for `argc == 0` or `argc >= 3`.
  - `FromDigits::nlst: Argument <arg> at position 1 in <call> should
    be a list or a string.` -- concrete-but-not-list-or-string first
    arg (Integer, Real, Rational, Complex). Pure symbolic first args
    flow through silently.
  - `FromDigits::ibase: Base argument must be an integer >= 2.` --
    fires for an integer base `<= 1` (or any integer base over the
    string form that is `<= 1`).
  - `FromDigits::char: Invalid digit character <c> in string at
    position <pos> in <call>.` -- character outside `[0-9a-zA-Z]` in
    a string input.
- Test suite: `tests/test_from_digits.c` (46 cases, registered in
  `tests/CMakeLists.txt` as `from_digits_tests`). Covers all
  documented examples verbatim, the inverse-of-`IntegerDigits`
  round trip, bignum results (`2^100`, `10^30 + 12345`, `100!`),
  carrying with digits `>=` base, negative digits, symbolic / mixed
  / Real / Rational base, hex strings with mixed case, base 36
  ("Z" -> 35), 50-digit bignum strings, edge cases (empty list,
  empty string, leading zeros, single-digit lists), and every error
  path including silent unevaluated symbolic forms. A 50-iteration
  repeated-evaluation stress loop catches double-frees and mpz
  leaks under valgrind. Verified leak-free on the per-digit
  `expr_to_mpz` (which `mpz_init_set_*`s its output, so the loop
  pairs each call with `mpz_clear`).

## DigitCount (2026-05-23)

New built-in `DigitCount[n]` / `DigitCount[n, b]` / `DigitCount[n, b, d]`
— per-digit histogram and scalar digit-count over the base-`b` expansion
of `|n|`, matching Mathematica's surface semantics.

- Implementation: extends `src/int.c` (+ `src/int.h`). Registered in
  `int_init()` alongside `IntegerDigits` / `IntegerLength`. Attribute
  `Protected` (intentionally **not** `Listable` -- the natural output is
  itself a list) declared in `src/attr.c` and re-applied in
  `int_init()`. Symbol `SYM_DigitCount` interned in
  `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- List form (1/2-arg) returns `{c(1), c(2), ..., c(b-1), c(0)}` in that
  order -- digit 0 is the LAST entry, matching Mathematica. Sized
  `base` entries, so an internal cap of `2^20` rejects pathological
  bases with a `DigitCount::ovfl` diagnostic; the 3-arg scalar form has
  no such cap.
- Histogram fast path uses GMP's `mpz_tdiv_q_ui` which returns the
  divisor remainder directly when the base fits in an `unsigned long`
  -- roughly 2x faster than the full `mpz_tdiv_qr` path for small
  bases. The 3-arg scalar path branches on `mpz_fits_ulong_p` for both
  base AND target so that small `b` with a bignum digit (or vice
  versa) still pays the fast remainder cost where it can.
- `DigitCount[0]` returns a list of zeros of length `b` (zero has no
  significant digits, matching `IntegerLength[0] == 0`). Sign of `n`
  is discarded everywhere.
- Diagnostics (stderr; call is then left unevaluated):
  - `DigitCount::argb: DigitCount called with N argument(s); between
    1 and 3 arguments are expected.` -- fires for `argc == 0` or
    `argc >= 4`.
  - `DigitCount::int: Integer expected at position 1 in <call>.` --
    concrete-but-non-integer numeric `n` (Real, Rational, Complex).
    Pure symbolic `n` flows through silently (returning `NULL`).
  - `DigitCount::base: The base <b> at position 2 of <call> should be
    an integer greater than 1.` -- fires for non-integer base
    (`5/2`, `2.5`, ...) AND for integer base `< 2` (`0`, `1`, `-2`).
    Matches Mathematica's verbatim diagnostic.
  - `DigitCount::digit: The digit <d> at position 3 of <call> should
    be a non-negative integer less than the base.` -- non-integer
    digit, or integer digit out of `[0, base)`.
  - `DigitCount::ovfl: Base too large for the list-returning form in
    <call>; use DigitCount[n, b, d] for a single digit instead.` --
    fires when the 1/2-arg form is invoked with `base > 2^20`.
- Definitional property `DigitCount[n, b, d] == Count[IntegerDigits[n,
  b], d]` is asserted on several small inputs in the test suite.
  Histogram-sum invariant `Total[DigitCount[n, b]] == IntegerLength[n,
  b]` is property-tested over `n = 1..30, b in {2, 7, 10}`.
- Docstring (three usage forms) registered in `src/info.c`; spec entry
  under `docs/spec/builtins/arithmetic-and-algebra.md` includes the
  three documented Mathematica examples.
- Tests: `tests/test_digit_count.c` (~50 cases) -- documented
  Mathematica examples (`DigitCount[2147, 2, 1] == 5`, `DigitCount[2147,
  2] == {5, 7}`, `DigitCount[100!] == {15, 19, 10, 10, 14, 19, 7, 14,
  20, 30}`), small decimal cases, zero in all forms, negative inputs,
  bignum (10^30, 2^100, 100!, int64-overflow boundary at `2^63`),
  bignum base via `b = 10^18 + 1` (forces the slow-path `mpz_tdiv_qr`
  loop), bignum digit, histogram-sum invariant, definitional
  `Count`-equivalence cross-check, every error path (`::argb`, `::int`,
  `::base`, `::digit`, `::ovfl`), three flavours of symbolic-arg
  silence, attribute-set check (`Protected && !Listable`), docstring
  presence, interned-symbol pointer reachability, and a 50-iteration
  stress loop touching every code branch to expose double-frees or
  mishandled `mpz_t`s. The `eval_capturing_stderr` helper was hardened
  to save/restore stderr via `dup`/`dup2` (previously used
  `freopen("/dev/tty", ...)` which silently breaks stderr under shell
  redirection, hiding subsequent FAIL output).

## IntegerLength (2026-05-23)

New built-in `IntegerLength[n]` / `IntegerLength[n, b]` — counts the
positional digits of `|n|`, matching Mathematica's surface semantics.

- Implementation: extends `src/int.c` (+ `src/int.h`). Registered in
  `int_init()` alongside `IntegerDigits`. Attributes `Protected |
  Listable` set both in `src/attr.c` (static base table) and applied
  through `symtab_get_def("IntegerLength")->attributes` in `int_init()`.
  Symbol `SYM_IntegerLength` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- Fast path uses GMP's `mpz_sizeinbase` for bases `2..62`. Power-of-two
  bases yield an exact result directly; non-power-of-two bases use one
  `mpz_ui_pow_ui` + `mpz_cmp` to disambiguate the documented
  "exact-or-one-too-big" return of `mpz_sizeinbase`. Bases `>= 63`
  (arbitrary-precision bases) fall back to a repeated-division loop.
  Net effect: O(log n) for typical small bases, regardless of how many
  digits `n` has.
- `IntegerLength[0]` is `0` in any base (zero has no significant
  digits). Sign of `n` is discarded.
- Listable: `IntegerLength[{1, 10, 100}]` threads element-wise; same for
  the base argument or both arguments together.
- Diagnostics (stderr; the call is then left unevaluated):
  - `IntegerLength::argt: IntegerLength called with N argument(s);
    1 or 2 arguments are expected.` — fires for `argc == 0` or
    `argc >= 3`. The unevaluated result echoes the call exactly, so
    `IntegerLength[]` returns `IntegerLength[]` and
    `IntegerLength[1, 2, 3, 4]` returns `IntegerLength[1, 2, 3, 4]`,
    matching Mathematica's surface output. Covered by
    `test_zero_args_argt`, `test_three_args_argt`,
    `test_four_args_argt`, `test_five_args_argt`.
  - `IntegerLength::int: Integer expected at position <p> in <call>.`
    — fires when a concrete-but-non-integer numeric (Real, Rational,
    Complex) is supplied at position 1 (n) or 2 (b). The call is then
    echoed back exactly, so `IntegerLength[1.1234]` returns
    `IntegerLength[1.1234]`, matching Mathematica. Pure symbolic
    arguments flow through silently (returning `NULL`).
  - `IntegerLength::ibase: Base argument must be an integer >= 2.` —
    integer base of 1, 0, or negative.
- Docstring (terse, two usage forms) registered in `src/info.c`; spec
  entry under `docs/spec/builtins/arithmetic-and-algebra.md`.
- Tests: `tests/test_integer_length.c` (~40 cases) — decimal, base 2 /
  3 / 8 / 16 / 62 / 100 / 256, zero, negatives, bignum
  (10^30, 2^100, 100!, including `IntegerLength[100!, 2] == 525` and
  the documented base-2..20 table for 100!), int64-overflow boundary,
  arbitrary-precision base (10^18 + 1), Listable threading on `n` /
  `b` / both / nested, the `Floor[Log[b, n]] + 1` property, error
  paths (`::argt`, `::int`, `::ibase`, symbolic args), attribute /
  docstring / symbol-pointer introspection, and a repeated-evaluation
  stress loop to expose double-frees under valgrind.

## IntegerDigits (2026-05-23)

New built-in `IntegerDigits[n]` / `IntegerDigits[n, b]` /
`IntegerDigits[n, b, len]` — decomposes an integer into its positional
base-`b` digit list, MSB-first, matching Mathematica's surface semantics.

- Implementation: `src/int.c` (+ `src/int.h`), registered via the new
  `int_init()` hook in `core_init()` (`src/core.c`). Attributes
  `Protected | Listable` set both in `src/attr.c` (the static base table)
  and applied through `symtab_get_def("IntegerDigits")->attributes` in
  `int_init()`. Symbol `SYM_IntegerDigits` interned in
  `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- All arithmetic is done in GMP (`mpz_tdiv_qr`), so the same code path
  handles both machine `int64_t` inputs and arbitrary-precision bignums.
  Individual digits are demoted to `EXPR_INTEGER` whenever
  `mpz_fits_slong_p` is true, so common results contain no transient
  bigints.
- Sign of `n` is discarded; `IntegerDigits[0]` returns `{0}` (one zero
  digit); `IntegerDigits[0, b, len]` returns a list of `len` zeros.
- Listable: `IntegerDigits[{6, 7, 2}, 2]` threads as
  `{IntegerDigits[6, 2], IntegerDigits[7, 2], IntegerDigits[2, 2]}`;
  `IntegerDigits[7, {2, 3, 4}]` threads the base argument; the optional
  `len` is a scalar that propagates to every threaded call.
- Truncation rule: when `len` is shorter than the natural digit count,
  the `len` *least-significant* digits are returned (Wolfram-compatible),
  computed by walking `mpz_tdiv_qr` only `len` times' worth of buckets
  before stopping — though for simplicity the current implementation
  decomposes the full integer and slices afterwards.
- Diagnostics (Mathematica-compatible surface text, all printed to
  stderr; the call is then left unevaluated):
  - `IntegerDigits::argb: IntegerDigits called with N argument(s);
    between 1 and 3 arguments are expected.` — fires for `argc == 0`
    or `argc > 3`.
  - `IntegerDigits::int: Integer expected at position <p> in <call>.`
    — fires when a concrete-but-non-integer numeric (Real, Rational,
    Complex, BigInt-of-non-integer-shape) is supplied at position 1
    (n), 2 (b), or 3 (len). Pure symbolic args still flow through
    silently (returning `NULL`) so downstream rewrites can fix them.
  - `IntegerDigits::ibase: Base argument must be an integer >= 2.` —
    integer base of 1, 0, or negative.
  - `IntegerDigits::intnn: Non-negative machine-sized integer
    expected at position 3.` — negative length, or a length that
    overflows `size_t`.
- Docstring (terse, three usage forms) registered in `src/info.c`; spec
  entry under `docs/spec/builtins/arithmetic-and-algebra.md`.
- Tests: `tests/test_integer_digits.c` (~30 cases) — decimal, base 2 /
  16 / 256, zero, negatives, padding short / long / truncating,
  bignum (10^30 and beyond), Listable threading on `n` / `b` / both,
  `IntegerDigits[Range[0, 7], 2, 3]`, error paths (bad base, bad length,
  symbolic args), attribute/docstring/symbol-pointer introspection, and
  a repeated-evaluation stress loop to expose double-frees under
  valgrind.

## Normalize (2026-05-22)

New built-in `Normalize[v]` / `Normalize[z]` / `Normalize[expr, f]` —
returns the unit-norm form of a scalar, vector, or general tensor,
matching Mathematica's surface semantics.

- Implementation: `src/linalg/normalize.c`, registered via
  `linalg_init()` in `src/linalg/linalg.c` (Protected, not Listable —
  the call operates on the whole vector, not element-wise).  Symbol
  `SYM_Normalize` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- Strategy: build `Times[expr, Power[f[expr], -1]]` and feed it to the
  evaluator.  `Times` is `Listable`, so a single call distributes the
  scalar reciprocal across every leaf of a vector / matrix / tensor
  input.  Default `f` is `Norm` (which itself folds to `Abs` for
  scalars), giving `Normalize[z] == z / Abs[z]` for free.
- Zero short-circuit: if the evaluated norm is a literal numeric zero
  (Integer 0, Real `0.0`, BigInt 0, or MPFR 0) we return `expr_copy(expr)`
  unchanged, matching Wolfram's documented "zero vectors are returned
  unchanged" rule.  Symbolic norms that *happen* to be zero are not
  short-circuited — the user keeps the symbolic division they wrote.
- Diagnostics: `argc` not in `{1, 2}` emits `Normalize::argt`
  (Mathematica-compatible text) to stderr and leaves the call
  unevaluated.
- Docstring registered in `src/info.c`; spec entry under
  `docs/spec/builtins/linear-algebra.md`.
- Tests: `tests/test_normalize.c` covering exact rational / radical
  / complex vectors, scalar (real / complex / imaginary) inputs,
  zero short-circuit on integer / real / empty list / zero matrix,
  symbolic vectors with default and custom norm functions, machine-
  precision floats via `N[]`, idempotence (`Norm[Normalize[v]] == 1`),
  a Listable-guard regression check, arity diagnostics, attribute /
  docstring / `SYM_Normalize` interning, and a repeated-evaluation
  stress loop for valgrind sanity.

## NegativeDefiniteMatrixQ (2026-05-22)

New predicate `NegativeDefiniteMatrixQ[m]` returns `True` iff
`Re[Conjugate[x] . m . x] < 0` for every nonzero vector `x`,
equivalently iff `-m` is positive definite, i.e. the negated Hermitian
part `-(m + ConjugateTranspose[m]) / 2` admits a Cholesky factorisation
with a real positive diagonal.

- Implementation: `src/linalg/negdef_q.c`, registered via
  `linalg_init()` in `src/linalg/linalg.c` (Protected, not Listable).
  Symbol `SYM_NegativeDefiniteMatrixQ` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- Numeric dispatch: loads `-m` into a column-major double buffer
  (real or interleaved complex), builds its Hermitian part in place,
  then reuses the LAPACK `dpotrf` / `zpotrf` wrappers
  (`mat_lapack_dpotrf` / `mat_lapack_zpotrf` in `src/linalg/lapack.{h,c}`)
  introduced for `PositiveDefiniteMatrixQ`.  Cholesky's `info` is the
  predicate (0 = m is negative definite).  When `USE_LAPACK` is
  unavailable, falls back to an in-house Cholesky in the same
  translation unit.
- Symbolic / non-coercible entries: returns `False` (conservative;
  matches Mathematica's "explicitly" qualifier for predicates that
  cannot symbolically prove the property).
- Shape rejections that return `False`: non-list input, empty list,
  ragged or non-square shape, 3-D tensors.
- Diagnostics: 0 or `>= 2` args emit `NegativeDefiniteMatrixQ::argx`
  (Mathematica-compatible text) to stderr and leave the call
  unevaluated, mirroring `PositiveDefiniteMatrixQ` / `SquareMatrixQ`.
- Tests: `tests/test_negative_definite_matrix_q.c` covering small
  symmetric / asymmetric real matrices, Hermitian and complex
  non-Hermitian, diagonal and zero matrices, BigInt / Rational / Real
  / Complex mixtures, negated Hilbert matrices (n up to 8),
  Cholesky-built `-m . m^T` matrices, symbolic-returns-False, shape
  and arity rejections, a `NegativeDefiniteMatrixQ[m] ==
  PositiveDefiniteMatrixQ[-m]` cross-check battery, plus attribute /
  docstring / sym-intern checks and a repeated-evaluation loop for
  valgrind sanity.

## PositiveDefiniteMatrixQ (2026-05-22)

New predicate `PositiveDefiniteMatrixQ[m]` returns `True` iff
`Re[Conjugate[x] . m . x] > 0` for every nonzero vector `x`, i.e. the
Hermitian part `(m + ConjugateTranspose[m]) / 2` admits a Cholesky
factorisation with a real positive diagonal.

- Implementation: `src/linalg/posdef_q.c`, registered via
  `linalg_init()` in `src/linalg/linalg.c` (Protected, not Listable).
  Symbol `SYM_PositiveDefiniteMatrixQ` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- Numeric dispatch: loads the matrix into a column-major double buffer
  (real or interleaved complex), builds the Hermitian part in place,
  then calls LAPACK `dpotrf` / `zpotrf` via new wrappers
  `mat_lapack_dpotrf` / `mat_lapack_zpotrf` in `src/linalg/lapack.{h,c}`.
  Cholesky's `info` is the predicate (0 = positive definite).  When
  `USE_LAPACK` is unavailable, falls back to an in-house Cholesky in the
  same translation unit.
- Symbolic / non-coercible entries: returns `False` (conservative;
  matches Mathematica's "explicitly" qualifier for predicates that
  cannot symbolically prove the property).
- Shape rejections that return `False`: non-list input, empty list,
  ragged or non-square shape, 3-D tensors.
- Diagnostics: 0 or `>= 2` args emit `PositiveDefiniteMatrixQ::argx`
  (Mathematica-compatible text) to stderr and leave the call
  unevaluated, mirroring `SquareMatrixQ`.
- Tests: `tests/test_positive_definite_matrix_q.c` (30 cases) covering
  small symmetric / asymmetric real, Hermitian and complex-symmetric,
  diagonal and zero matrices, BigInt / Rational / Real / Complex
  mixtures, Hilbert matrices (n up to 8), Cholesky-built `m . m^T`
  matrices, symbolic-returns-False, shape and arity rejections, plus
  attribute / docstring / sym-intern checks and a repeated-evaluation
  loop for valgrind sanity.

## Re / Im fold real-valued heads (2026-05-22)

`Re` and `Im` now collapse nested calls whose argument is real-valued by
construction.  For `f` in `{Re, Im, Abs, Arg}`:

- `Re[f[z]]` -> `f[z]`
- `Im[f[z]]` -> `0`
- `ReIm[f[z]]` -> `{f[z], 0}`

This matches the existing `Conjugate[f[..]] -> f[..]` rule (same set of
real-valued heads) and applies even when the inner argument is purely
symbolic and does not numericalize.

## UpperTriangularMatrixQ (2026-05-22)

New predicate `UpperTriangularMatrixQ` with two surface arities:

- `UpperTriangularMatrixQ[m]` returns `True` iff every entry strictly
  below the main diagonal of `m` is zero, `False` otherwise.
- `UpperTriangularMatrixQ[m, k]` returns `True` iff every entry
  `m[[i, j]]` with `j - i < k` is zero.  Positive `k` selects a
  superdiagonal above the main diagonal (the test gets stricter --
  even the main diagonal must vanish); negative `k` selects a
  subdiagonal below it (the first `|k|` subdiagonals are allowed to be
  nonzero).  Works on rectangular as well as square matrices.

An option `Tolerance -> t` relaxes the zero test to `Abs[e] <= t`,
mirroring `DiagonalMatrixQ` / `HermitianMatrixQ` / `SymmetricMatrixQ`.
`Tolerance -> Automatic` falls through to the structural (exact-zero)
test.  Without a tolerance the predicate is conservative: only literal
numeric zeros (`Integer 0`, `Real 0.0`, `BigInt 0`) count as zero, so a
symbolic sub-diagonal entry causes the matrix to be rejected.

Shape handling:
- Non-list, scalar, vector, ragged, and rank-3+ inputs return `False`.
- The empty list `{}` is not a matrix and returns `False`.
- An `n`-by-`0` matrix (e.g. `{{}, {}}`) has no entries and is vacuously
  upper triangular -- returns `True`.

Diagnostics (matching Wolfram's surface text):

- 0 args ->
  ```
  UpperTriangularMatrixQ::argt: UpperTriangularMatrixQ called with 0 arguments; 1 or 2 arguments are expected.
  ```

- Any non-`Rule` junk beyond position 2 (3rd positional arg or later) ->
  ```
  UpperTriangularMatrixQ::nonopt: Options expected (instead of <expr>) beyond position 2 in UpperTriangularMatrixQ[...]. An option must be a rule or a list of rules.
  ```

Both diagnostics go to `stderr` and leave the call unevaluated.

Wiring:
- `SYM_UpperTriangularMatrixQ` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`
  (alphabetical between `UpTo` and `Verbatim`).
- `builtin_upper_triangular_matrix_q` in `src/list.c` (sits next to
  `DiagonalMatrixQ` / `SquareMatrixQ` / `SymmetricMatrixQ` /
  `HermitianMatrixQ`).  Reuses `diag_entry_is_exact_zero` and
  `diag_entry_under_tolerance` from `DiagonalMatrixQ`.
- Registered with attribute `Protected` and a docstring in
  `src/info.c`.

Tests: `tests/test_upper_triangular_matrix_q.c` covers upper /
non-upper / 1x1 / symbolic / real / complex / exact / arbitrary-precision
matrices, the docstring's super- and sub-diagonal examples for
`k = 1, 2, -1, -2`, rectangular cases (2x3 and 3x2 upper / non-upper /
out-of-range `k`), `Tolerance` (including `Automatic` and too-tight
tolerance), shape rejections (scalar / vector / `{}` / ragged / 3-D
tensor), `n x 0` matrices, the argt / nonopt diagnostics, attribute and
docstring introspection, `DiagonalMatrix` / `IdentityMatrix`
cross-property checks, and a 50-iteration repeated-evaluation stress
loop for valgrind sanity.


## DiagonalMatrixQ (2026-05-22)

New predicate `DiagonalMatrixQ` with two surface arities:

- `DiagonalMatrixQ[m]` returns `True` iff every off-(main-diagonal) entry
  of `m` is zero, `False` otherwise.
- `DiagonalMatrixQ[m, k]` returns `True` iff every entry off the `k`-th
  diagonal (entries with `j - i != k`) is zero.  Positive `k` walks the
  superdiagonals above the main diagonal; negative `k` walks the
  subdiagonals below it.  Works on rectangular as well as square
  matrices.

An option `Tolerance -> t` relaxes the zero test to `Abs[e] <= t`,
mirroring the surface API of `HermitianMatrixQ` / `SymmetricMatrixQ`.
`Tolerance -> Automatic` falls through to the structural (exact-zero)
test.  Without a tolerance the predicate is conservative: only literal
numeric zeros (`Integer 0`, `Real 0.0`, `BigInt 0`) count as zero, so a
symbolic off-diagonal entry causes the matrix to be rejected.

Shape handling:
- Non-list, scalar, vector, ragged, and rank-3+ inputs return `False`.
- The empty list `{}` is not a matrix and returns `False`.
- An `n`-by-`0` matrix (e.g. `{{}, {}}`) has no entries and is vacuously
  diagonal -- returns `True`.

Diagnostics (matching Wolfram's surface text):

- 0 args ->
  ```
  DiagonalMatrixQ::argt: DiagonalMatrixQ called with 0 arguments; 1 or 2 arguments are expected.
  ```

- Any non-`Rule` junk beyond position 2 (3rd positional arg or later) ->
  ```
  DiagonalMatrixQ::nonopt: Options expected (instead of <expr>) beyond position 2 in DiagonalMatrixQ[...]. An option must be a rule or a list of rules.
  ```

Both diagnostics go to `stderr` and leave the call unevaluated so the
user can see their typo.

Wiring:
- `SYM_DiagonalMatrixQ` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}` (alphabetical
  between `Derivative` and `Direct`).
- `builtin_diagonal_matrix_q` in `src/list.c` (sits next to
  `SquareMatrixQ` / `SymmetricMatrixQ` / `HermitianMatrixQ`).
- Registered with attribute `Protected` and a docstring in
  `src/info.c`.

Tests: `tests/test_diagonal_matrix_q.c` (44 cases) covers diagonal /
non-diagonal / 1x1 / symbolic / real / complex matrices, the
docstring's super- and sub-diagonal examples for `k = 1, 2, -1, -2`,
rectangular cases (2x3 and 3x2 diagonal, off-diagonal nonzero,
out-of-range `k`), `Tolerance` (including `Automatic` and too-tight
tolerance), shape rejections (scalar / vector / `{}` / ragged / 3-D
tensor), `n x 0` matrices, the argt / nonopt diagnostics, attribute and
docstring introspection, `DiagonalMatrix` round-trip, and a
50-iteration repeated-evaluation stress loop for valgrind sanity.
Valgrind on the new binary reports identical `definitely / indirectly /
possibly lost` totals to the baseline `square_matrix_q_tests`; the
`still reachable` delta (~461 bytes) is the one-time
`intern_symbol("DiagonalMatrixQ")` plus the new docstring storage.


## Conjugate: auto-simplify on real-valued and involutive subexpressions (2026-05-22)

`Conjugate` now reduces a small family of obvious cases that previously
returned the input unchanged:

```
Conjugate[Conjugate[z]]  ->  z          (involution)
Conjugate[Re[z]]         ->  Re[z]
Conjugate[Im[z]]         ->  Im[z]
Conjugate[Abs[z]]        ->  Abs[z]
Conjugate[Arg[z]]        ->  Arg[z]
```

`Re`, `Im`, `Abs`, and `Arg` are real-valued by construction, so they
are Conjugate-fixed irrespective of whether their argument numericalises
to a machine real. This complements the existing `is_numeric_real`
fast-path, which only catches symbolic *constants* that reduce under
`N[]` (e.g. `Pi`, `Sqrt[2]`, `3/Sqrt[11]`).

The involution case also collapses arbitrary stacks: an odd number of
nested `Conjugate`s reduces to a single `Conjugate`, an even number to
the bare argument.

`builtin_conjugate` (`src/complex.c`): two structural checks added at the
top of the function, before the existing numeric / complex-literal
paths. The involution path uses the standard NULL-out-before-free
pattern to hand the inner expression to the evaluator without a copy.

Wrong-arg-count diagnostics: `Conjugate[]` and `Conjugate[a, b, ...]`
now print a Mathematica-compatible

```
Conjugate::argx: Conjugate called with N arguments; 1 argument is expected.
```

to `stderr` and leave the call unevaluated.  Pluralisation of
`argument(s)` matches Wolfram's surface text.

## SquareMatrixQ (2026-05-22)

New predicate `SquareMatrixQ[m]` that returns `True` iff `m` is a
square matrix (`Dimensions[m] == {n, n}` for some `n >= 1`) and `False`
otherwise.  Pure shape test: no element predicate or option is
consulted, so it does the absolute minimum work needed to classify the
input.

Behaviour:
- Non-list, scalar, string, vector, empty (`{}`, `{{}}`), ragged,
  rectangular, and higher-rank tensor inputs all return `False`.
- Symbolic matrices (`{{a, b}, {c, d}}`) are accepted just like numeric
  ones -- the test is structural, not numerical.
- Exactly one argument is accepted.  Any other count emits a
  Mathematica-compatible

  ```
  SquareMatrixQ::argx: SquareMatrixQ called with N arguments; 1 argument is expected.
  ```

  to `stderr` and leaves the call unevaluated, mirroring the
  diagnostic style already used by `builtin_conjugate` and matching the
  surface behaviour observed in Wolfram Language.

Wiring:
- `SYM_SquareMatrixQ` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- `builtin_square_matrix_q` in `src/list.c` (sits next to
  `SymmetricMatrixQ` / `HermitianMatrixQ`).
- Registered with attribute `Protected` and a docstring in `src/info.c`.

Tests: `tests/test_square_matrix_q.c` covers numeric / symbolic /
identity squares, every rejection axis (scalar, vector, empty, ragged,
rectangular, 3-D tensor, mixed-list entries), the `MatrixQ`
implication direction, a `Dimensions == {n, n}` cross-check battery,
the argx wrong-arity diagnostic, attribute and docstring
introspection, and a 50-iteration valgrind-friendly stress loop.

## HermitianMatrixQ (2026-05-22)

New predicate `HermitianMatrixQ[m]` that returns `True` iff `m` is
explicitly Hermitian (`m == ConjugateTranspose[m]`), and `False`
otherwise.  Diagonal entries must be self-conjugate.

The default test is structural and handles symbolic `Conjugate[...]`
pairs directly so it does not have to rely on `Conjugate[Conjugate[x]]`
folding (although as of 2026-05-22 that fold is now an automatic
simplification -- see the Conjugate note above).  Specifically, the
pair test accepts any of:

  1. `a == Conjugate[c]` structurally and `c == b` (covers (Conjugate[a], a));
  2. `b == Conjugate[c]` structurally and `c == a` (covers (a, Conjugate[a]));
  3. `Conjugate[b]` evaluates to a structurally-equal expression of `a`.

Two options are supported, matching Mathematica's surface API:

- `SameTest -> f`: pairs are accepted iff `f[m[i,j], Conjugate[m[j,i]]]`
  evaluates to `True`.  `SameTest -> Automatic` falls through to the
  structural test.
- `Tolerance -> t`: pairs are accepted iff
  `Abs[m[i,j] - Conjugate[m[j,i]]] <= t`.  `Tolerance -> Automatic`
  falls through to the structural test.

Non-matrix, non-square, ragged, empty, and rank-3+ tensor inputs
return `False`.  Unknown options or non-`Rule` trailing arguments
leave the call unevaluated.

Wiring:
- `SYM_HermitianMatrixQ` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- `builtin_hermitian_matrix_q` in `src/list.c` (sits next to `MatrixQ`).
- Registered with attribute `Protected` and a docstring in `src/info.c`.

Tests: `tests/test_hermitian_matrix_q.c` (32 cases) covers real /
complex / symbolic Hermitian matrices, the documented rejections,
shape edge cases, `SameTest` and `Tolerance` options (including
`Automatic`), error-handling for bad options, equivalence against
`SameQ[m, ConjugateTranspose[m]]`, attribute and docstring
introspection, and 50-iteration repeated-evaluation runs for
ownership/leak sanity.  Valgrind on the new binary reports no leaks
attributable to Mathilda code (the residual macOS dyld/libobjc
allocations are identical to the baseline `conjugate_transpose_tests`
binary).

## SymmetricMatrixQ (2026-05-22)

New predicate `SymmetricMatrixQ[m]` that returns `True` iff
`m == Transpose[m]` (the complex-symmetric notion — no conjugation),
and `False` otherwise.  Mirrors the coding style of `HermitianMatrixQ`
but uses structural equality `expr_eq` for off-diagonal pairs and
exempts the diagonal (trivially equal to itself).

Two options are supported with the same surface API as
`HermitianMatrixQ`:

- `SameTest -> f`: pairs `(m[i,j], m[j,i])` are accepted iff
  `f[m[i,j], m[j,i]]` evaluates to `True`.  `SameTest -> Automatic`
  falls through to the structural test.
- `Tolerance -> t`: pairs are accepted iff
  `Abs[m[i,j] - m[j,i]] <= t`.  `Tolerance -> Automatic` falls
  through to the structural test.

Non-matrix, non-square, ragged, empty, and rank-3+ tensor inputs
return `False`.  Unknown options or non-`Rule` trailing arguments
leave the call unevaluated.

Cross-property notes: a real symmetric matrix is always Hermitian; a
complex symmetric matrix need not be (e.g.
`{{1+I, 2+2 I}, {2+2 I, 3+3 I}}` is symmetric but not Hermitian).

Wiring:
- `SYM_SymmetricMatrixQ` interned in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.
- `builtin_symmetric_matrix_q` in `src/list.c` (sits next to
  `builtin_hermitian_matrix_q`).
- Registered with attribute `Protected` and a docstring in
  `src/info.c`.

Tests: `tests/test_symmetric_matrix_q.c` (34 cases) covers real /
complex / symbolic symmetric matrices, the documented rejections,
shape edge cases, `SameTest` and `Tolerance` options (including
`Automatic` and the `Log[x^2]` / `2 Log[x]` example with a
`Simplify`-based predicate), error-handling for bad options, the
cross-property checks against `HermitianMatrixQ`, equivalence against
`SameQ[m, Transpose[m]]`, attribute and docstring introspection, and
50-iteration repeated-evaluation runs for ownership/leak sanity.
Valgrind on the new binary differs from the baseline
`hermitian_matrix_q_tests` by 48 bytes / 1 block — the one-time
`intern_symbol("SymmetricMatrixQ")` allocation.  No per-call leaks
attributable to `builtin_symmetric_matrix_q`.

## LUDecomposition: Hager-Higham MPFR condition estimator (2026-05-22)

The MPFR kernel now uses the Hager-Higham one-norm estimator (the
algorithm LAPACK's `*lacn2` uses inside `*gecon`) for the condition
number of real matrices.  The estimator runs the iteration

```
x = (1/n) e
loop:
    y = A^{-T} x
    gamma = ||y||_1
    xi = sign(y)
    z = A^{-1} xi
    if convergence test passes, return gamma
    x = e_{argmax |z|}
```

with `A^{-T}` and `A^{-1}` applied via the existing LU factorisation
