- `arnoldi_dispatch_mpfr`: top-level shape selector for the MPFR path;
  the public `arnoldi_dispatch` now checks
  `common_scan_inexact(m).min_bits > 53` and prefers MPFR when it
  fires, otherwise falls through to the machine kernel.

Hermitian / symmetric inputs again flow through the same general MPFR
kernels — the special-case Lanczos fast path is intentionally deferred.

### Tests

15 machine-precision tests + 6 MPFR tests in
`tests/test_mateigen_arnoldi.c` covering each kernel.  The MPFR tests
compare Arnoldi's |λ| against Direct's |λ| at 60 and 80 bits with a
1e-15 tolerance; the eigenvector tests verify return shape and that
input precision carries through to result components.

## mateigen.c — complex Hermitian + complex general MPFR "Direct" kernels (Phase 2 steps 2d-C / 2d-D, 2026-05-19)

`Eigenvalues` and `Eigenvectors` now route **complex Hermitian** and
**complex non-Hermitian** MPFR inputs through arbitrary-precision
kernels rather than downgrading to the machine path.  With 2d-A
through 2d-D combined, every numeric input shape — real symmetric,
real general, complex Hermitian, complex non-Hermitian — has
matching machine-precision and MPFR Direct kernels.

### Code (2d-C: complex Hermitian)

- `matM_norm_inf_complex` and `matM_is_hermitian` — paired with the
  existing real helpers from 2d-A so the dispatcher detects shape on
  both real and complex MPFR inputs uniformly.
- `direct_tridiag_complex_hermitian_M` — paired-`mpfr_t` (real / imag)
  Hermitian Householder tridiagonalisation; mirrors the machine
  version but every complex arithmetic op is expanded to two
  `mpfr_*` ops at the matrix's bit precision.
- `direct_phase_correct_tridiag_M` — rotates the diagonal unitary D
  onto the tridiagonal so the subdiagonal becomes real-positive,
  updating Q by right-multiplication.  After this step the tridiagonal
  matrix is purely real and the eigenvalues can be extracted with the
  real symmetric QR from 2d-A (`direct_symtridiag_qr_M`).
- `direct_compose_complex_Q_real_Z_M` and
  `direct_build_complex_hermitian_eigvec_list_M` — assemble the final
  complex eigenvector matrix V = Q · Z and emit it as
  `List[List[mpfr | Complex[mpfr, mpfr], ...]]`.
- `direct_complex_hermitian_mpfr` is the top-level entry point.

### Code (2d-D: complex general)

- `direct_complex_general_mpfr` reuses the 2d-B real-general MPFR
  pipeline via the same 2n × 2n real block embedding
  M = [[R, −S], [S, R]] used by the machine kernel
  (`direct_complex_general_machine`).
- After running M through `direct_hessenberg_real_M` +
  `direct_qr_real_general_M` + `schur_compute_eigvecs_M`, the
  candidate A-eigenvector for each M-eigenvalue μ is
  `x = (a − d) + i(b + c)` from the top / bottom splits of the
  M-eigenvector.  Grouped complex Gram-Schmidt at MPFR precision
  (twice for stability) extracts the n distinct A-eigenvectors
  out of the doubled M-spectrum.
- Tolerances:
  - `group_tol = N · spec_norm · 2^{−bits/2 + 6}` — matches the
    LAPACK-style "n · sqrt(eps)" rule, generous enough to group
    `(λ, conj λ)` reliably under non-symmetric MPFR QR roundoff.
  - `extract_threshold = sqrt(n) · 2^{−bits/2 + 6}` — between the
    +J subspace norm (~ sqrt(2)) and the −J subspace norm (~ 2^−bits).

### Dispatcher

`direct_dispatch_mpfr` now has full coverage:

| Shape                | Branch                                |
| -------------------- | ------------------------------------- |
| real symmetric       | `direct_real_sym_mpfr` (2d-A)         |
| real non-symmetric   | `direct_real_general_mpfr` (2d-B)     |
| complex Hermitian    | `direct_complex_hermitian_mpfr` (2d-C)|
| complex non-Hermitian| `direct_complex_general_mpfr` (2d-D)  |

Hermitian / symmetry detection uses tolerance
`n · 2^{−bits+4} · ‖A‖_∞` (∞-norm computed via `matM_norm_inf_complex`
for complex inputs).

### Tests

12 new `USE_MPFR`-guarded tests in `tests/test_mateigen_direct.c`
covering 2d-C (7) and 2d-D (5):

- **Hermitian:** 2×2 with `(5 ± √5)/2` spectrum at 50 digits;
  Pauli X (real symmetric routing) and Pauli Y (complex Hermitian)
  spectra; 3×3 Hermitian trace invariant; Hermitian eigenvalues are
  real (Im part < tolerance for each); precision propagation;
  Eigenvectors return-shape.
- **Complex general:** 2×2 upper triangular `{3, 2}` (real spectrum);
  non-Hermitian 2×2 with real eigenvalues `1 ± √5`; diagonal 2×2
  with explicit complex entries; precision propagation;
  Eigenvectors return-shape.

### Behaviour gates

After this phase, the complete Direct coverage matrix is:

| Input shape          | Machine | MPFR  |
| -------------------- | ------- | ----- |
| Real symmetric       | yes     | yes   |
| Real non-symmetric   | yes     | yes   |
| Complex Hermitian    | yes     | yes   |
| Complex non-Hermitian| yes     | yes   |

Generalised pencils (`Eigenvalues[{m, a}]`) still flow through the
symbolic characteristic-polynomial path — that's deliberate; a
numeric generalised eigenproblem is its own algorithmic ticket and
not part of Phase 2.

## mateigen.c — real general (non-symmetric) MPFR "Direct" kernel (Phase 2 step 2d-B, 2026-05-19)

`Eigenvalues` and `Eigenvectors` now route real **non-symmetric** MPFR
inputs through an arbitrary-precision Hessenberg + Francis QR + Schur
back-substitution kernel, rather than downgrading to the machine path.
With 2d-A and 2d-B combined, all real-matrix shapes now compute
spectrum and eigenvectors at the matrix's input precision.

### Code

- `direct_hessenberg_real_M`, `direct_francis_step_M`,
  `direct_split_2x2_real_M`, and `direct_qr_real_general_M` —
  MPFR transcriptions of their `double` counterparts. Each `double`
  arithmetic op becomes an `mpfr_*` call rounded `MPFR_RNDN`; the
  Francis step takes a 14-cell caller-supplied scratch pool so
  `mpfr_init`/`mpfr_clear` stay out of the bulge-chase inner loop.
- New exceptional-shift mechanism inside `direct_francis_step_M`
  (LAPACK `dlahqr`-style): the QR driver passes `exceptional = true`
  every 10th iteration, replacing the trailing-2×2 shift with
  `s = 1.5 · (|H[p-1, p-2]| + |H[p-2, p-3]|)`. Without this the
  high-precision sweep can stall in a 2-cycle for matrices whose
  trailing 2×2 has the same complex shift after each pass
  (observed on `{{1, -1, 0}, {1, 1, -1}, {0, 1, 1}}` at 50+ digits).
  Machine precision masks this naturally via roundoff; MPFR does not.
- `schur_eigvec_real_M` and `schur_eigvec_complex_M` — back-
  substitution on `(H − λI)` for real and complex eigenvalues in the
  Schur basis, mirroring the machine versions. `schur_compute_eigvecs_M`
  composes `V = Q · v_schur` and normalises to unit 2-norm.
- `direct_sort_perm_desc_abs_complex_M`,
  `direct_build_complex_eigenvalue_list_M`, and
  `direct_build_complex_eigenvector_list_M` — emit `List[mpfr, ...]`
  or `List[Complex[mpfr_re, mpfr_im], ...]` depending on whether the
  imaginary part is zero.
- `direct_real_general_mpfr` is the top-level entry that owns the
  workspace lifecycle (`H`, optional `Q`, Householder vector,
  14-cell scratch, eigenvalue arrays).
- `direct_dispatch_mpfr` now selects between `direct_real_sym_mpfr`
  and `direct_real_general_mpfr` based on `matM_is_real_symmetric`,
  matching the machine dispatcher's structure.
- Deflation tolerance: `rel_tol = 2^{-bits+10}` (1024 ULPs), about
  one decimal digit looser than the symmetric tridiag tolerance.
  Non-symmetric implicit-shift QR accumulates more per-sweep roundoff
  than the symmetric path (factor ~n^2 from bulge chase plus back-
  transformation), so a slightly more permissive threshold is needed
  for clean convergence on adversarial high-precision inputs.
- `max_iter` raised to `60·n + 30` (was `30·n` in the machine kernel).
  Even with exceptional shifts, MPFR convergence at very high bit
  counts can require more sweeps before deflation fires.

### Tests

8 new `USE_MPFR`-guarded tests in `tests/test_mateigen_direct.c`
(Phase 2 step 2d-B):

- 3×3 upper triangular at 50 digits → diagonal spectrum
  (forces non-symmetric path, real eigenvalues).
- 2×2 rotation matrix at 50 digits → pure ±I eigenvalues.
- 3×3 with complex pair `1 ± i√2` at 50 digits — exercises the
  trailing-2×2 complex-deflation branch (scale 10^35 to tolerate
  the looser non-symmetric QR convergence).
- `Precision[lambda] > 49` on a non-symmetric 3×3 (routing check).
- `Eigenvectors` return-shape verifies head `List`.
- Trace and determinant invariants: `Sum(λ) == Tr(A)`,
  `Prod(λ) == Det(A)` to 45-digit margin.
- 4×4 upper triangular eigenvalue residual at 50 digits.
- 120-digit stress on a 3×3 upper triangular.

### Behaviour gates

Combined coverage after 2d-{A, B}:

| Input shape                      | Machine | MPFR |
| -------------------------------- | ------- | ---- |
| Real symmetric                   | yes     | yes  |
| Real non-symmetric               | yes     | yes  |
| Complex Hermitian                | yes     | (2d-C) |
| Complex non-Hermitian            | yes     | (2d-D) |

Complex MPFR inputs still fall through to the machine kernel; that
is the next step (2d-C / 2d-D).

## mateigen.c — real symmetric MPFR "Direct" kernel (Phase 2 step 2d-A, 2026-05-19)

`Eigenvalues` and `Eigenvectors` now have an arbitrary-precision
(`MPFR`) path for real symmetric matrices.  At input precision *p*
(detected via `common_scan_inexact`, with the rule "any MPFR leaf →
MPFR kernel"), the dispatcher routes to a new MPFR variant of the
machine kernel; the eigenvalues and orthonormal eigenvectors come back
carrying full input precision.

### Code

- New struct `MatM` (mirrors `MatD` but with `mpfr_t` cells pre-
  initialised to the matrix's precision) plus paired
  `mpfr_array_alloc` / `mpfr_array_free` lifecycle helpers and a
  `matM_load` that drives `get_approx_mpfr` over every cell.
- `matM_norm_inf_real` and `matM_is_real_symmetric` (MPFR-tolerance
  variant of the machine helpers) — feeding the symmetric-detection
  branch.
- `direct_tridiag_real_sym_M` and `direct_symtridiag_qr_M` — exact
  algorithmic mirrors of their `double` counterparts with every
  `double` op replaced by an `mpfr_*` call rounded `MPFR_RNDN`;
  caller-supplied scratch pool (12 cells for QR, 8 for tridiag) keeps
  `mpfr_init` / `mpfr_clear` out of inner loops.
- `direct_sort_perm_desc_abs_M`, `direct_build_real_eigenvalue_list_M`,
  `direct_build_real_eigenvector_list_M`, and a `direct_real_sym_mpfr`
  entry point that owns the workspace lifecycle.
- New top-level `direct_dispatch` selects MPFR vs machine kernel based
  on `common_scan_inexact(m).min_bits > 53`.  Other matrix shapes
  (complex / non-symmetric MPFR) still fall through to the machine
  kernel until 2d-{B,C,D} land — documented as a known precision-loss
  fallback in `info.c`.

### Tests

10 new MPFR-symmetric tests in `tests/test_mateigen_direct.c`
(guarded by `USE_MPFR`).  All use a deliberate **scale-by-10^k +
`N[]`-to-machine** pattern to verify residuals at high precision while
sidestepping Mathilda's `Less[machine_zero, mpfr_value]`
non-evaluation quirk.  Coverage:

- Closed-form spectra: 2×2 golden ratio (50 digits), tridiag(2,3,2)
  → {4,2,1} (80 digits), 3×3 identity (degenerate), diag(5,3,1) under
  k-spec, 1×1 edge case.
- Residual / orthonormality on 5×5 symmetrised random matrix (60
  digits, demanding 45 accurate digits) and a 3×3 stress test at 200
  digits (demanding 180 accurate digits).
- Routing verification: `Precision[lambda_i] > 49` for every
  eigenvalue of a 50-digit input, ensuring the kernel didn't silently
  fall back to machine precision.
- `Eigenvectors` return-shape (head is `List`).
- Near-degenerate 2·I + ε symmetric perturbation: three eigenvalues
  all close to 2.

Test-writing lesson captured for future fixtures: Mathilda variable
names like `max_norm` parse as `Pattern[max, Blank[norm]]` per
Mathematica syntax — local variables passed through `Module[...]` must
use camelCase or otherwise avoid underscores.

### Behaviour gates

`Eigenvalues[SetPrecision[m, p]]` and `Eigenvectors[SetPrecision[m,
p]]` for real symmetric `m` now return MPFR results.  Mixed-precision
inputs are loaded at the **minimum** input precision (matching the
existing `common_scan_inexact` policy used by `LinearSolve` and other
MPFR-aware builtins).

## mateigen.c — complex non-Hermitian "Direct" kernel (Phase 2 step 2c-B, 2026-05-19)

`Eigenvalues` and `Eigenvectors` now also handle **complex
non-Hermitian** matrices at machine precision; the symbolic
characteristic-polynomial fallback is reserved for arbitrary-precision
MPFR and the symbolic path proper.  With this commit the Direct method
covers every machine-precision matrix shape.

### Algorithm — real block embedding

A complex n × n matrix `A = R + i S` is embedded into the real
2n × 2n block matrix

    M = [[ R, -S ],
         [ S,  R ]]

whose spectrum is `spec(A) ∪ conj(spec(A))` as a multiset.  The
existing real machinery handles M:

1. **Hessenberg reduction** via `direct_hessenberg_real` with `Q`
   accumulation.
2. **Francis double-shift QR** via `direct_qr_real_general`.
3. **Schur back-substitution** via `schur_compute_eigvecs` to get M's
   eigenvectors (always — `Q` is needed even for `WANT_VALUES` to
   disambiguate the conjugate-pair doubling).

### Eigenvector recovery + the +J / −J split

For each M-eigenvector `w = w_re + i w_im` with `M w = mu w`, the
candidate

    x = (a - d) + i (b + c)

where `w_re = [a; b]` and `w_im = [c; d]` are the n-vector top / bottom
splits, satisfies `A x = mu x`.  When `mu` is in `spec(A)` the candidate
is non-zero; when `mu` is only in `conj(spec(A))` (i.e. `conj(mu) ∈
spec(A)` but `mu` itself is not) the candidate is zero.  This is the
+J / −J splitting of M's eigenspace into the A-action and conj(A)-
action subspaces.

### Grouped Gram-Schmidt for multiplicity

Algebraic multiplicity is handled by grouping M-eigenvalues that fall
within `1e-8 ‖M‖ n` of each other (one Schur position-order pass
identifies adjacent equivalents), then running complex modified
Gram-Schmidt twice over each group's candidate `x`'s.  The "twice is
enough" rule keeps the orthogonalisation numerically stable; vectors
that fall below `sqrt(n) · 1e-9` after orthogonalisation are dropped as
−J contributions.  The extracted basis size per group equals `m_A(mu)`
and the totals sum to exactly `n`.

This correctly handles the "mixing" case where both `λ` and
`conj(λ)` are in `spec(A)` for some non-real λ (e.g.
`[[0,1,0],[-1,0,0],[0,0,2+i]]` has spec `{i, -i, 2+i}` and the simple
pair-up algorithm would emit `{i, i, 2+i}` here -- the grouped GS
correctly emits `{2+i, i, -i}`).

### Dispatch

`direct_dispatch_machine` now routes complex non-Hermitian inputs to
`direct_complex_general_machine`; the symbolic char-poly fallback is
preserved as the final escape hatch.

### LAPACK-HOOK annotations

`zgehrd + zhseqr + ztrevc3` (or `zgeev` as a one-call wrapper) is the
LAPACK drop-in.  The block embedding nominally costs 8x more flops at
`-O3` than a native complex Hessenberg + complex QR; vendor LAPACK on
the complex path will recover that 8x.

### Tests

`tests/test_mateigen_direct.c` gains 8 complex non-Hermitian cases:

* `test_direct_complex_general_diagonal` — `diag(1+i, 2+i)` (no
  mixing).
* `test_direct_complex_general_mixing` — the canonical mixing test
  `[[0,1,0],[-1,0,0],[0,0,2+i]]`.
* `test_direct_complex_general_2x2_generic` — full 2×2 with complex
  off-diagonal.
* `test_direct_complex_general_real_off_complex_diag` — one complex
  diagonal entry.
* `test_direct_complex_general_3x3_random`,
  `test_direct_complex_general_5x5_random` — reproducible LCG random
  matrices.
* `test_direct_complex_general_real_rotation_promoted` — `[[0,1],[-1,0]]`
  with a tiny imag entry to force the complex dispatch path.
* `test_direct_complex_general_eigenvalues_only` — the
  `WANT_VALUES` (no V emit) path.

`tests/eigen_corpus.{h,c}` gains `corpus_assert_residual_complex` (with
a complex `lambda`) and `corpus_eval_eigenvalues_complex`.

### Files touched

* `src/mateigen.c` — `direct_complex_general_machine` + dispatcher.
* `src/info.c` — `?Eigenvalues` / `?Eigenvectors` reflect the new
  capability.
* `tests/test_mateigen_direct.c`, `tests/eigen_corpus.h`,
  `tests/eigen_corpus.c`.

## mateigen.c — complex Hermitian "Direct" kernel (Phase 2 step 2c-A, 2026-05-19)

`Eigenvalues` and `Eigenvectors` now route complex **Hermitian**
matrices at machine precision through a hand-rolled native-complex
kernel instead of falling back to the symbolic
characteristic-polynomial pipeline.

### Algorithm

1. **Complex Householder tridiagonalisation** of the Hermitian input.
   Reflectors `H_k = I - 2 u u^H / ||u||^2` are applied symmetrically
   via the rank-2 update `A <- A - u q^H - q u^H` with `q = 2 A u -
   2 alpha_v u` (`alpha_v = u^H A u`, real for Hermitian).  The result
   is a Hermitian tridiagonal `T` with real diagonal but generally
   complex sub-diagonal.  Complex unitary `Q` accumulates the
   reflectors when eigenvectors are requested.
2. **Diagonal phase correction**: a unitary diagonal `D = diag(d_k)`
   with `|d_k| = 1` and `d_{k+1} = d_k * sub[k] / |sub[k]|` is applied
   so `D^H T D` has real-positive sub-diagonal, i.e. becomes a real
   symmetric tridiagonal.  `Q` is updated to `Q D`.
3. **Real symmetric tridiag QR** (existing `direct_symtridiag_qr`)
   finds eigenvalues `Lambda` and accumulates the real orthogonal
   `Z` with `Z^T T_real Z = Lambda`.
4. **Final eigenvectors** `V = Q Z` (complex `Q` times real `Z`).

This avoids needing a separate complex tridiagonal QR; the only added
cost over the real symmetric path is an `O(n^2)` diagonal-phase pass.
See Wilkinson 1965, "The Algebraic Eigenvalue Problem", §5.45.

### Dispatch

`direct_dispatch_machine` now splits real vs complex.  Complex inputs
that pass `matD_is_hermitian` (within `1e-12 n ||A||_inf` tolerance on
both the imag-diagonal and the conjugate-symmetry checks) route to
`direct_complex_hermitian_machine`; complex non-Hermitian inputs still
fall through to the symbolic path (step 2c-B).

### LAPACK-HOOK annotations

The new section is annotated for future drop-in replacement: `zhetrd`
(step 1, with `tau` covering the implicit phase reduction) +
`dsteqr` / `dstedc` (step 3), or `zheevd` as a one-call wrapper.

### Tests

`tests/test_mateigen_direct.c` gains 10 complex-Hermitian cases:

* `test_direct_hermitian_2x2_diag_imag` — `[[2,i],[-i,3]]`, eigenvalues
  `(5±√5)/2`.
* `test_direct_hermitian_pauli_x` / `_y` / `_z` — all four Pauli
  matrices (eigenvalues `±1`).  Pauli-Y forces the phase-correction
  path through a pure-imag 2×2.
* `test_direct_hermitian_3x3_known` — Hermitian 3×3 with mixed
  real / imag entries; trace check + residual + unitarity.
* `test_direct_hermitian_diagonal_4x4` — real diagonal loaded into the
  complex path; checks the dispatcher routes correctly and the
  eigenvalues come out in the expected order.
* `test_direct_hermitian_5x5_random` — reproducible LCG-generated
  Hermitian random 5×5; residual + unitarity.
* `test_direct_hermitian_repeated_eigvals` — `I_4` (4-fold degenerate
  eigenvalue) checks every output eigenvector is still an eigenvector
  and the basis is unitary.
* `test_direct_hermitian_complex_offdiag_only` — `[[0, 2i], [-2i, 0]]`.
* `test_direct_hermitian_eigenvalues_only` — `WANT_VALUES` (skip-Q) path.

`tests/eigen_corpus.{h,c}` are extended with complex helpers:
`corpus_matrix_to_eigenvalues_input_complex`,
`corpus_eval_hermitian_eigenvalues`,
`corpus_eval_eigenvectors_complex`,
`corpus_assert_residual_complex_real_lambda`,
`corpus_assert_unitary`,
`corpus_norm_inf_complex`.

### Files touched

* `src/mateigen.c` — Hermitian kernel + dispatcher update.
* `src/info.c` — `?Eigenvalues` / `?Eigenvectors` reflect the new
  capability.
* `tests/test_mateigen_direct.c`, `tests/eigen_corpus.h`,
  `tests/eigen_corpus.c`.

## matsol.c — LinearSolve accepts array-shaped m and b (2026-05-19)

`LinearSolve[m, b]` previously rejected anything other than a rank-2
`m` with a rank-1 or rank-2 `b`. Mathematica accepts higher-rank
tensors: a rank-N `m` with dimensions `{d_1, ..., d_{N-1}, n}` is
interpreted as a `(d_1 * ... * d_{N-1}) x n` linear system, and `b`
with dimensions `{d_1, ..., d_{N-1}, e_1, ..., e_p}` produces a
result of shape `{n, e_1, ..., e_p}`. The reported failure case was

```
a = RandomInteger[{-3, 3}, {2, 3, 6}];
b = RandomInteger[{-3, 3}, {2, 3, 4, 5}];
Dimensions[LinearSolve[a, b]]   (* expected {6, 4, 5} *)
```

`builtin_linearsolve` in `src/matsol.c` now:
- accepts `m_rank >= 2`, computing `r` as the product of `m`'s leading
  dims and `c` as its last dim;
- validates that `b`'s leading `m_rank - 1` dimensions match `m`'s
  leading dims (otherwise `LinearSolve::lvec1`);
- computes `trail_dims` / `trail_rank` from `b`'s remaining dims and
  passes them to each method-specific solver.

The three solvers (`linearsolve_divfree`, `linearsolve_onestep`,
`linearsolve_cofactor`) now build their flat `c * k` answer array and
hand it to a shared `build_solution_tensor` helper which assembles
the nested `{c, trail_dims...}` `List`. This collapses the previous
`b_rank == 1 ? flat-list : list-of-lists` branch into a single code
path that generalises to any trailing rank.

`docs/spec/builtins/linear-algebra.md` and `tests/test_linearsolve.c`
gained a `test_linearsolve_array_inputs` covering the bug-report
case, rank-3 m with vector b (`trail_rank == 0`), rank-3 m with
rank-3 b (`trail_rank == 1`), and a leading-dim mismatch error.

## part.c — Extract accepts scalar positions (2026-05-19)

`builtin_extract` previously returned `NULL` (left the call
unevaluated) whenever the position argument was not a `List`. This
contradicted Mathematica, where `Extract[expr, n]` is the same as
`Extract[expr, {n}]`, so e.g. `Extract[{1, 2, 3}, 0, f]` should give
`f[List]`.

`extract_single` now wraps a scalar position as a one-element path,
and `builtin_extract` no longer rejects non-`List` positions in its
gating check. Regression tests added to `tests/test_part.c`, and the
`?Extract` docstring expanded to document the scalar-position form,
the `pos == 0` head-extraction case, and the Rational/Complex
atomicity rule shared with `Part`.

## core.c — Level treats Rational/Complex as atomic (2026-05-19)

`Level[expr, levelspec]` was descending into `Rational[n, d]` and
`Complex[re, im]` expressions, emitting the integer components as
separate atoms and (with `Heads -> True`) emitting `Rational`/`Complex`
as heads. This contradicted Mathematica's `AtomQ` semantics, which
classify rationals and complex numbers as atoms.

`level_rec` in `src/core.c` now short-circuits the descent when the
head is `Rational` or `Complex`: the expression matches the level test
as a single atom (its depth is already 1 in `get_expr_depth`) and its
children/head are not visited. This mirrors the existing special case
in `get_expr_depth`.

For the test expression
`((-1+E^2) CosIntegral[I-Tan[x]] + (-1+E^2) CosIntegral[I+Tan[x]] +
 I (1+E^2) (SinIntegral[I-Tan[x]] + SinIntegral[I+Tan[x]]))/(4 E)`,
`Length[Level[e, {-1}]]` is now 23 (was 35) and
`Length[Union[Level[e, {-1}, Heads -> True]]]` is now 13 (was 17),
matching Wolfram Mathematica.

Also added: `SYM_Level` in `src/sym_names.{h,c}` and the `Level`
docstring in `src/info.c` (accessible via `?Level`).

## parse.c — Mathematica `*^` scaled-scientific notation (2026-05-19)

Number literals now accept the Mathematica `*^` exponent suffix
(`mantissa*^signed-integer`), in addition to the existing `e`/`E`
exponent form. The suffix follows the precision/accuracy backticks if
present, matching WL's `mantissa\`prec*^exp` ordering.

- `1.23*^4` → `12300.0` (Real)
- `123*^4` → `1230000` (Integer; promotes to BigInt automatically)
- `123*^-4` → `Rational[123, 10000]` (reduced; e.g. `100*^-2` → `1`)
- `1.23*^-4` → `0.000123` (Real)
- MPFR mantissas are scaled at their own precision via
  `mpfr_mul`/`mpfr_div` against `10^|exp|`.

Implemented in `parse.c::apply_pow10_scale` with the suffix consumed at
the end of `parse_number`. Whitespace is not permitted between the
mantissa and `*^`. Test coverage in
`tests/test_parse.c::test_parse_scaled_scientific`.

## core.c, part.c — `Dimensions[expr, n]` and `Head[expr, h]` (2026-05-18)

Added the second-argument forms of `Dimensions` and `Head` to match
Mathematica semantics, and expanded both docstrings (`?Dimensions`,
`?Head`) with full descriptions and examples.

- `Dimensions[expr, n]` truncates the result to the first `n` levels.
  The internal `get_dimensions` walker now carries a `max_depth` cap and
  short-circuits once that depth is reached, so deep structures aren't
  fully walked when only the top levels are requested.  Raggedness is
  still detected within the requested level range.  `n = 0`, atomic
  `expr`, or `Infinity` (mapped to the 64-level hard cap) all behave as
  in WL.  Non-integer or negative `n` leaves the call unevaluated.
- `Head[expr, h]` returns `h[Head[expr]]`; the wrapper `h` is left to
  the evaluator (so e.g. `Head[a+b, Identity]` reduces to `Plus`).
- Test coverage in `tests/test_eval.c::test_dimensions` and
  `tests/test_eval.c::test_builtin_head` covers both forms, ragged
  structures, atomic inputs, the empty list, depth-cap truncation, and
  wrapper evaluation.



All four `LeastSquares` Method options now have dedicated algorithmic
implementations instead of dispatching through `"Direct"`.

- **`"IterativeRefinement"`** is now a real loop: `x <- x +
  PseudoInverse[m] . (b - m . x)` repeated until
  `Total[Flatten[dx]^2] <= Tolerance^2` or a 50-iteration cap.  For exact
  inputs the first correction is exactly zero (Moore-Penrose identity
  `pinv m pinv = pinv` gives `dx = pinv (b - m pinv b) = 0`) so the loop
  converges in one pass; for inexact inputs the loop drives round-off
  down to Tolerance.  The squared-norm test uses
  `Total[Flatten[dx]^2]` which is correct for both vector and matrix
  RHS.
- **`"Krylov"`** is Conjugate-Gradient-on-Least-Squares: starting from
  `x_0 = 0` (so the iterate stays in `range(A^T)` and converges to the
  minimum-norm LS solution for rank-deficient `m`), the loop maintains
  `r = b - A x`, `s = A^T r`, `p`, `gamma = |s|^2`.  Each step computes
  `q = A p`, `alpha = gamma / |q|^2`, then updates `x`, `r`, `s`,
  `beta = |s_new|^2 / |s|^2`, and `p <- s_new + beta p`.  Exits on
  `gamma <= Tolerance^2` (numeric) or `gamma == 0` (exact), on a
  null-direction `|q|^2 == 0`, or at the `2 cols(A) + 10` cap.  Matrix
  RHS are solved column-by-column and recombined via `Transpose`.
  Symbolic inputs (the convergence test is undecidable for them) fall
  back to `"Direct"`.
- **`"LSQR"`** is the canonical Paige-Saunders 1982 algorithm: Lanczos
  bidiagonalisation of `A` combined with a Givens-rotation update of
  the upper bidiagonal least-squares factor.  Convergence test uses
  `|phi_bar * alpha_{k+1}|`, the Paige-Saunders estimate of
  `||A^T r||`, scaled against the initial gradient `||A^T b||`.
  Dispatches by input grammar: free-symbol inputs go to Direct; exact
  (Integer / Rational) and Complex inputs go to CGLS (LSQR is
  mathematically equivalent to CGLS but produces unsimplified
  square-root expressions over exact rationals); pure-real inputs with
  at least one Real entry run the canonical double-precision algorithm.
  Detects rank deficiency by monitoring `alpha_new` and `beta_new`
  against `LSTSQ_LSQR_BREAKDOWN_EPS * max(|A_ij|)`, avoiding the
  catastrophic blowup of dividing by a near-zero `alpha`; near-zero
  `beta_new` triggers a final no-rotation Givens update that
  incorporates the last Krylov direction (so full-rank, well-conditioned
  systems do not miss the last iteration).

`"Automatic"` and `"Direct"` remain `PseudoInverse[m, Tolerance -> t]
. b`, the fundamental LeastSquares specification.

Tests in `tests/test_matlstsq.c` expanded with twenty new cases:
five for IterativeRefinement (Real 3x3 vs Direct, exact zero
Tolerance, ultra-tight Tolerance still terminates, singular 3x3,
matrix RHS), eight for Krylov (4x3 overdetermined, singular 3x3,
matrix RHS, Real 3x2 vs Direct, rational invertible, symbolic
fallback, complex, zero Tolerance), and seven for LSQR (Real 3x2 vs
Direct, ill-conditioned 3x3 cond ~1e3 -- the case that exposed the
"frozen v_1" bug during development, Real 4x3, matrix RHS, complex
fallback, symbolic fallback, Real singular).  All 55 tests pass and
valgrind shows no Mathilda-originated leaks (4,288 bytes / 8 errors,
identical to the matinv baseline and all in macOS dyld / libobjc
loader frames).

## matlstsq.c — `LeastSquares` (2026-05-18)

New module `src/matlstsq.[ch]` implementing
`LeastSquares[m, b]`, `LeastSquares[m, b, Method -> "<name>"]`, and
`LeastSquares[m, b, Tolerance -> t]`.  `LeastSquares` returns an `x`
minimising `Norm[m . x - b]`; for full-column-rank `m` this is the
unique least-squares minimiser, for rank-deficient `m` it is the
minimum-norm minimiser (the Moore-Penrose pseudoinverse solution
`PseudoInverse[m] . b`).

- New symbol: `SYM_LeastSquares`, cached in `sym_names.[ch]` and
  interned in `sym_names_init()` alongside the other matrix-routine
  symbols.
- Attributes: `Protected`.
- Docstring lives in `src/info.c` next to `LinearSolve` /
  `PseudoInverse` and is exposed via `Information[LeastSquares]` and
  the `?LeastSquares` REPL shortcut.
- Registered from `core_init()` immediately after `matinv_init()` so
  the underlying `PseudoInverse` builtin is available.

Behaviour:

- The matrix `m` may be square or rectangular and of any rank.  The
  right-hand side `b` may be a vector (rank-1) or a matrix (rank-2,
  one column per RHS).  For matrix `b` the result has one column per
  RHS, identical to a column-wise vector solve.
- Works on every input family supported by `PseudoInverse`:
  integer / rational, symbolic, machine-precision `Real` / MPFR, and
  exact / inexact `Complex`.
- Method and Tolerance options may appear in any order; each at most
  once.  Duplicates or unknown options leave the call unevaluated, so
  user-supplied DownValues / pattern rules can intercept it.
- Accepted Method names:
  - `Automatic` (symbol) / `"Automatic"` / `"Direct"` — Moore-Penrose
    solve `PseudoInverse[m] . b` (the workhorse).
  - `"IterativeRefinement"` — Direct then one refinement pass:
    `x <- PseudoInverse[m] . b`, `dx <- PseudoInverse[m] . (b - m . x)`,
    return `x + dx`.  For exact inputs the correction is exactly zero
    and the answer equals Direct; for inexact inputs the second pass
    reduces residual round-off.
  - `"LSQR"` — Paige-Saunders LSQR.  Method name is accepted by the
    parser; current dispatch goes through `"Direct"`.  A dedicated
    iterative implementation is a future extension.
  - `"Krylov"` — iterative Krylov / CGNR method.  Currently dispatched
    to `"Direct"` (likewise reserved).
- `Tolerance -> Automatic` (default), or a non-negative integer / real
  / `Rational`.  Forwarded verbatim to the underlying `PseudoInverse`
  call so any future singular-value-truncation pass in `PseudoInverse`
  is picked up automatically.

Diagnostics: `LeastSquares::matrix` (non-rank-2 or empty `m`),
`LeastSquares::lvec` (`b` not rank-1 or rank-2),
`LeastSquares::lvec1` (`b`'s leading dimension does not match `m`'s
row count) — each leaves the call unevaluated.

Tests: `tests/test_matlstsq.c` covers all spec examples (over-
determined integer 3x2 / 4x3, singular 3x3, symbolic 2x2,
matrix-RHS, `IdentityMatrix . b == b`, identity vs `LinearSolve` for
consistent systems, identity vs `PseudoInverse . b`, approximate
3x3, 1x1 / row-vector / column-vector degenerates), every Method
name (including the `Automatic` symbol and string variants), every
Tolerance type (Automatic, Integer, Real, Rational, negative),
mixed-option orderings, duplicate detection, and every shape-error
path.  The stress loop runs 5 representative shapes a total of 200
iterations through the PseudoInverse + Dot pipeline; valgrind shows
no Mathilda-originated leaks (only the unavoidable macOS dyld /
libobjc loader noise present in every binary on Darwin).

## core.c — `Clip` (2026-05-18)

`Clip[x]`, `Clip[x, {min, max}]`, and
`Clip[x, {min, max}, {vmin, vmax}]` are now built-ins in `src/core.c`
(`builtin_clip` plus the file-local helpers `clip_to_double_value`,
`clip_has_imaginary_part`, `clip_classify_infinity`).  The symbol is
cached as `SYM_Clip` in `sym_names.[ch]` and is registered with
`NumericFunction | Protected` (Listable is intentionally **not** set:
see below).

Behaviour:

- Default interval is `[-1, 1]`.  `{min, max}` and `{vmin, vmax}` are
  ordinary `List[...]` arguments; the bounds are coerced to a `double`
  for the comparison via `clip_to_double_value`, which accepts
  `Integer`, BigInt, `Rational[n, d]`, `Real`, MPFR (when
  `USE_MPFR=1`), and any symbolic expression that `numericalize`
  reduces to one of those (e.g. `Pi`, `E`, `Sqrt[2]`).
- The original symbolic `x` is returned when it lies inside the
  interval -- numericalization is used only for the decision, never
  for the result, so `Clip[Pi, {-9, 7}, {11, 28}]` is `Pi`, not
  `3.14159...`.
- `Infinity` and `-Infinity` are classified before any numericalize
  call (`Infinity` is not a machine real and `numericalize` cannot
  reduce it) and yield `vmax` / `vmin` respectively.
- A `Complex[re, im]` with a structurally non-zero imaginary part
  trips a rate-limited `Clip::ncompl` warning (via the shared
  `matsol_warn_once` idiom from `src/matsol.c`) and the call stays
  unevaluated, matching Mathematica.
- Any other case where `clip_to_double_value` cannot reduce `x`,
  `min`, or `max` to a number also leaves the call unevaluated so
  user-supplied DownValues / pattern rules can intercept it.

Threading semantics need explanation because Mathilda's
`ATTR_LISTABLE` threads over *every* list argument, but Clip must
keep `{min, max}` and `{vmin, vmax}` as configuration lists.  Setting
`Listable` would incorrectly thread `Clip[1, {-2, 2}]` to
`{Clip[1, -2], Clip[1, 2]}`.  The fix is to drop `Listable` and
implement first-argument threading manually in `builtin_clip`: if
`args[0]` is a `List[x1, x2, ...]`, the call rewrites to
`List[Clip[x1, ...], Clip[x2, ...], ...]` and each inner call is
re-evaluated through `eval_and_free`, leaving the bounds /
replacement lists untouched.

Reference examples (spec-conformant, mirrored in `tests/test_clip.c`):

| Call | Result |
|------|--------|
| `Clip[7.5]` | `1` |
| `Clip[-5/2, {-2, 2}]` | `-2` |
| `Clip[Pi, {-9, 7}, {11, 28}]` | `Pi` |
| `Clip[{-2, 0, 2}]` | `{-1, 0, 1}` |
| `Clip[Infinity]` | `1` |
| `Clip[2 - 3 I]` | `Clip[2 - 3*I]` + `Clip::ncompl` |
| `Clip[Re[2 - 3 I]] + Clip[Im[2 - 3 I]] I` | `1 - I` |
| `N[Clip[1/11, {1/7, 5}], 50]` | `0.142857...142857` (50 digits) |

`tests/test_clip.c` (wired into `tests/CMakeLists.txt` as
`clip_tests`) covers every call shape, both default and explicit
intervals, replacement values, symbolic constants (`Pi`, `E`),
`Infinity`/`-Infinity`, threading over a flat and a nested `List`,
the complex-rejection branch with the spec workaround
`Clip[Re[z]] + Clip[Im[z]] I`, fully symbolic pass-through,
`N[...]`-driven arbitrary-precision output, malformed argument shapes
(no args, four args, non-`List` interval, non-`List` replacement),
the `(NumericFunction, Protected)` attribute set, and a memory loop.
Valgrind `--leak-check=full` reports zero Mathilda-attributable
losses; the remaining `definitely lost` blocks all trace into macOS
`libobjc`/`dyld4` startup, the standard baseline.

## core.c — `Chop` (2026-05-18)

`Chop[expr]` and `Chop[expr, delta]` are now built-ins, registered in
`core_init` with the `Protected` attribute and accompanied by a
docstring in `info.c`.  The implementation lives in `src/core.c`
(`builtin_chop` and the file-local helpers `chop_recursive`,
`chop_is_machine_real`, `chop_to_double`, `chop_extract_delta`); the
`SYM_Chop` cached pointer is in `sym_names.[ch]`.

Behaviour:

- The default tolerance is `10^-10`.  The `delta` argument is coerced
  to a non-negative `double` via `chop_extract_delta`, which accepts
  `Integer`, BigInt, `Real`, MPFR (when `USE_MPFR=1`), and
  `Rational[n, d]`.  A symbolic / non-numeric `delta` leaves the call
  unevaluated.
- Only approximate components are eligible to chop: `EXPR_REAL` and
  (when `USE_MPFR=1`) `EXPR_MPFR`.  `Integer`, BigInt, `Rational`, and
  symbolic constants pass through untouched.
- The walker recurses into every `EXPR_FUNCTION`, so small real-valued
  subterms inside arbitrary heads, lists, `Plus`, `Times`, and held
  forms are all chopped uniformly.
- `Complex[re, im]` gets a small special case to match Mathematica's
  "machine complex" behaviour: when both components are machine reals,
  chopping the imaginary part drops the `Complex` wrapper so the
  machine real survives unchanged, but chopping the real part yields
  the machine zero `0.0` (preserving the machine-complex shape) rather
  than an exact integer.  Mixed shapes such as `Complex[1, 1.*^-12]`
  fall through to the generic recursion and rely on `builtin_complex`'s
  `Complex[r, 0] -> r` simplification on the next evaluator pass.

Reference examples (spec-conformant, mirrored in
`tests/test_chop.c`):

| Call | Result |
|------|--------|
| `Chop[Exp[N[Range[4] Pi I]]]` | `{-1., 1., -1., 1.}` |
| `Chop[N[Pi] - Rationalize[N[Pi], 10^-12]] === 0` | `True` |
| `Chop[N[Pi] - Rationalize[N[Pi], 10^-12], 10^-14] === 0` | `False` |
| `Chop[10.^-12 + 2. I]` | `0. + 2. I` |
| `Chop[2. + 10.^-12 I]` | `2.` |

`tests/test_chop.c` (wired into `tests/CMakeLists.txt` as
`chop_tests`) covers: default vs. explicit-`delta` tolerance, the
strict `fabs(x) < delta` boundary, sign handling, every Complex
configuration above, structural threading through `List`, `Plus`,
`Times`, generic heads, and nested lists, exact-number pass-through
(`Integer`, BigInt, `Rational`, symbolic), the
`Chop[N[Pi] - Rationalize[...]]` round-trip from the spec discussion,
argument-shape errors (zero / three+ args, symbolic `delta`), the
`Protected` attribute, and a memory-hygiene loop.  Valgrind
`--leak-check=full` shows zero Mathilda-attributable losses; the
remaining "definitely lost" blocks all trace into macOS `libobjc` /
`dyld4` initialisation, the standard baseline.

## matinv.c — Method options for `Inverse` (2026-05-18)

`Inverse[m, Method -> "<name>"]` now mirrors the dispatcher that
`RowReduce` and `LinearSolve` gained earlier in the month, so every
matrix-solver builtin offers the same `Method` grammar.

- Three explicit algorithms are exposed, all in `src/matinv.c`:
  - `"DivisionFreeRowReduction"` — the historical Bareiss-like
    fraction-free Gauss-Jordan on the augmented matrix `[A | I]`.  The
    body is the same one that previously lived inside `builtin_inverse`,
    now lifted into `inverse_divfree(arg, n)`.
  - `"OneStepRowReduction"` — classical Gauss-Jordan on `[A | I]` with
    one division per pivot per row entry.  Each entry is canonicalised
    through `matsol_canon_entry` (`Together`) so symbolic cancellations
    are still detected and a singular symbolic matrix produces a
    definite `Inverse::sing` rather than a silently wrong answer.
  - `"CofactorExpansion"` — adjugate / determinant formula
    `A^-1[i, j] = (-1)^(i + j) Det[M[j, i]] / Det[A]`, with `Det`
    computed via the same `laplace_det` primitive used by `Det` itself
    and by the `LinearSolve` / `RowReduce` cofactor workers.  Time
    complexity is `O(n! * n^2)`; intended for small `n` or for
    obtaining a closed-form symbolic inverse of small matrices.  A 1x1
    fast path bypasses `laplace_det`'s `n >= 1` precondition.
- `Method -> Automatic` (the symbol) and `Method -> "Automatic"` both
  alias to `"DivisionFreeRowReduction"`, matching Mathematica.
- An unknown method name emits a rate-limited `Inverse::method`
  warning and leaves the call unevaluated.  Non-square / empty input
  still emits `Inverse::matsq`.  Every method emits `Inverse::sing` on
  a singular matrix and returns unevaluated.
- The previously file-private `parse_method_option`, `warn_once`,
  `canon_entry`, and `div_entry` helpers in `src/matsol.c` were
  promoted to `matsol_parse_method_option`, `matsol_warn_once`,
  `matsol_canon_entry`, and `matsol_div_entry`, and exposed in
  `src/matsol.h` alongside the `MatsolMethod` enum so `matinv.c` can
  reuse the same Method grammar and the same `Together` /
  exact-division primitives without duplication.
- `PseudoInverse` continues to call `Inverse` internally (through the
  evaluator) with no `Method` argument, so its behaviour is unchanged
  and it still goes through `inverse_divfree`.

Tests live in `tests/test_matinv_methods.c` (a new test executable
wired into `tests/CMakeLists.txt`).  Coverage mirrors
`test_matsol_methods.c`: each method is exercised against tiny
invertible integer matrices, bignum-valued matrices, fully symbolic
invertible matrices (back-substitution check, since methods differ in
canonical form), exact complex matrices, machine-precision Real
matrices, MPFR matrices when compiled in, and the singular /
non-square / invalid-method error paths.

## matinv.c — `PseudoInverse` builtin, and `Inverse` moved out of `linalg.c` (2026-05-18)

A new module `src/matinv.c` (with `src/matinv.h`) consolidates the two
matrix-inversion builtins.

- `Inverse[m]` is moved from `src/linalg.c` to `src/matinv.c` verbatim.
  The Bareiss-like fraction-free Gauss-Jordan algorithm on `[A | I]` is
  unchanged.  Registration happens in the new `matinv_init`, called
  from `core_init` immediately after `matsol_init` (so `Inverse` keeps
  resolving in the same evaluator load order).  `linalg_init` no
  longer registers `Inverse`.
- `PseudoInverse[m]` and `PseudoInverse[m, Tolerance -> t]` are new.
  The implementation computes a full-rank decomposition `m = B . C` by
  row-reducing `m` to identify rank `r` and the pivot columns, builds
  `B` (the `m x r` matrix of pivot columns) and `C` (the leading `r`
  rows of the RREF), and returns
  `PseudoInverse[m] = ConjugateTranspose[C] . Inverse[C . ConjugateTranspose[C]] . Inverse[ConjugateTranspose[B] . B] . ConjugateTranspose[B]`.
  The two `r x r` mid-products are invertible by construction.  For the
  `m x n` zero matrix the result is the `n x m` zero matrix.  For
  non-singular square `m` the result coincides with `Inverse[m]`.
- Inexact (`Real` / MPFR) inputs are routed through the
  `common_scan_inexact` → `common_rationalize_input` → exact pipeline →
  `common_numericalize_result` flow, so `PseudoInverse` honours
  inexact-in / inexact-out semantics at the input precision while
  still computing rank in exact rational arithmetic.
- `PseudoInverse` is `Protected`.  Information string registered in
  `info.c`.  Symbol interned as `SYM_PseudoInverse` (and the option
  symbol `SYM_Tolerance`) in `sym_names.c` / `sym_names.h`.
- The `Tolerance` option recognises `Automatic` (default), non-negative
  `Integer`, non-negative `Real`, and non-negative `Rational[n, d]`.
  Negative values, unknown option names, and non-numeric values leave
  the call unevaluated.
- New test binary `tests/test_matinv.c` (added to
  `tests/CMakeLists.txt` as `matinv_tests`) covers: invertible square
  (collapses to `Inverse`), the rank-1 singular 3x3 spec example,
  over- and under-determined rectangular inputs with the Moore-Penrose
  identity check `m . p . m == m && p . m . p == p`, zero matrices,
  `1x1` / `1xN` / `Nx1` shapes, exact rationals, exact and inexact
  complex (including the Wolfram reference 3x3 complex example),
  machine-precision real (including a singular row), the `Tolerance`
  option in all three forms (`Automatic`, numeric, invalid), shape
  errors, and a 120-call stress loop for memory hygiene.

Fixed a pre-existing leak of the temporary argument array in
`builtin_conjugate` (`src/complex.c`) that was newly exposed by
`PseudoInverse`'s use of `Conjugate[Transpose[...]]`.

## common.c — shared rationalize / numericalize preprocessor; Solve & Integrate routed through it (2026-05-18)

Both `Solve` and `Integrate` need the same "if the input has any inexact
(Real / MPFR) leaves, rationalise them before the exact-arithmetic core runs,
then numericalise the answer on the way out" preprocessing pass.  That dance
now lives in a single new module — `src/common.c` / `src/common.h` — exposing
three building blocks:

- `common_scan_inexact(e)` — single-pass walk returning a
  `CommonInexactInfo {has_inexact, min_bits}` struct.  `min_bits` is the
  *minimum* bit-precision seen across every inexact leaf: 53 for any Real
  (IEEE 754 double), `mpfr_get_prec(...)` for each MPFR.  The minimum
  policy means a mixed input propagates the *lower* precision through to
  the answer — the answer is no more precise than the least-precise
  input, which is the standard inexact-arithmetic contract.
- `common_rationalize_input(e, bits)` — force-rationalise every inexact
  leaf at the given precision.  Always tries the relaxed convergent-bound
  algorithm first (so `1.5` recovers as `3/2`, `1/9.` as `1/9`); when no
  convergent meets the bound the fallback is `RATIONALIZE_ZERO` (½ ulp at
  the input's double precision) for `bits ≥ 52` and `RATIONALIZE_TOLERANCE`
  with `dx = 2^(-bits)` for `bits < 52` (only seen when the caller has an
  MPFR leaf with explicit low precision).  Symbolic constants (`Pi`, `E`,
  ...) and Hold-forms pass through unchanged.
- `common_numericalize_result(e, bits)` — round-trip an exact symbolic
  answer back to floating-point at the requested precision.  `bits ≤ 53`
  → IEEE 754 double; `bits > 53` → MPFR at exactly `bits` bits (when
  compiled with `USE_MPFR`).  The traversal recurses into `List` and
  `Rule` so `{{x -> 1/2}}` cleanly becomes `{{x -> 0.5}}` while leaving
  the unknown LHS symbol alone.

The implementation delegates to `internal_force_rationalize_bits`
(rationalize.c, newly exposed) and `numericalize` (numeric.c) — the new
module is purely a stable API surface so future callers (`NSolve`,
`DSolve`, ...) plug in the same way.

### Precision propagation in action

```
Precision[(Solve[N[1, 30] x == 7, x][[1]][[1]])[[2]]]              -> 30.103
Precision[(Solve[(0.5 + N[Pi, 30]) x == 1, x][[1]][[1]])[[2]]]     -> MachinePrecision

Solve[N[Pi, 50] x == 1, x]
  -> {{x -> 0.31830988618379067945899344644312539938328968316824}}

Integrate[N[Pi, 50] x, x]
  -> 1.5707963267948965801416385921020337420225281697321 x^2
```

The 30-digit MPFR input flows through to a 30-digit result; the moment a
machine-precision Real joins it, the answer drops to machine precision.

Caveat: when the minimum precision exceeds 53 bits (only achievable with
explicit-MPFR inputs), the rationalisation step is still performed via the
double-based `internal_rationalize_double` core, so the intermediate
rational is bit-exact at double precision rather than at the requested
MPFR precision.  The numericalisation step does run at the full MPFR
precision, so the *output* carries the requested precision — it just isn't
fully *informed* by sub-double-precision bits of the input.  A
precision-true MPFR rationalisation path would close this gap and is left
as future work.

### Solve — approximate-number input support

`Solve[1.5 x + 3 == 0, x]` previously fell through the polynomial specialist
(which expects exact coefficients) and returned unevaluated.  After this
change `Solve` detects inexact leaves up front, rationalises the equation
(`{3/2, 3}`), dispatches to the appropriate specialist exactly as before,
and numericalises the bindings before return:

```
Solve[1.5 x + 3 == 0, x]                    -> {{x -> -2.0}}
Solve[x^2 - 2.25 == 0, x]                   -> {{x -> -1.5}, {x -> 1.5}}
Solve[0.5 x^2 - x - 1.5 == 0, x]            -> {{x -> -1.0}, {x -> 3.0}}
Solve[{1.5 x + y == 4.5, x - y == 0.5},
      {x, y}]                               -> {{x -> 2.0, y -> 1.5}}
Solve[N[Pi] x == 1, x]                      -> {{x -> 0.31831}}
```

The exact-integer path is untouched — `Solve[x^2 - 4 == 0, x]` still returns
`{{x -> -2}, {x -> 2}}` (no float anywhere in the input means no
post-numericalisation).

The `vars` argument is never rationalised — it stays a symbol or a list of
symbols, which is what the specialists require.

### Integrate — bit-exact rationalisation fallback removes `Integrate::inexact`

`Integrate` previously called `Rationalize` in the relaxed default mode and,
on a transcendental float it could not convert to a small-denominator
rational, emitted `Integrate::inexact` and returned unevaluated.  Routing
through `common_rationalize_input` (bit-exact ½-ulp fallback) means the
integrator always sees an exact integrand and the warning is gone:

```
Integrate[1.5 x, x]      -> 0.75 x^2
Integrate[N[Pi] x, x]    -> 1.5708 x^2     (* used to emit Integrate::inexact *)
Integrate[x^2, x]        -> 1/3 x^3        (* exact path: untouched *)
```

Same `inexact-in / inexact-out` contract as Solve and the existing
exact-symbolic builtins (`Apart`, `Cancel`, `Together`, `Factor`, ...).

### Files touched

- `src/common.h`, `src/common.c` — new module.
- `src/rationalize.h`, `src/rationalize.c` — added
  `internal_force_rationalize_bits(e, bits)`; existing
  `internal_force_rationalize` becomes a thin `bits = 0` wrapper.
- `src/solve.c` — rationalise the evaluated equation before dispatch;
  numericalise the result before return; both gated on
  `common_scan_inexact(expr).has_inexact`, both threaded with the
  reported `min_bits`.
- `src/integrate.c` — replaced the bespoke `expr_contains_real` +
  `internal_rationalize_expr(..., RATIONALIZE_DEFAULT)` block (and the
  `Integrate::inexact` message) with the common helpers; same precision
  threading as Solve.
- `tests/test_solve.c` — 5 new tests covering linear / quadratic / multi-
  variable / exact-input-pass-through cases, plus 2 MPFR-aware
  `Precision[...]` tests verifying min-precision propagation.
- `tests/CMakeLists.txt` — added `../src/common.c` to `COMMON_SRC`.

### Tests

- `solve_tests`: all tests pass (5 new approximate-number cases plus 2
  MPFR precision-propagation cases under `USE_MPFR`).
- `integrate_dispatch_tests`, `rationalize_tests`, `numeric_tests`,
  `parfrac_tests`, `poly_tests`, `facpoly_tests`, `simp_tests`: all green
  (no regressions from the Integrate refactor or the rationalize.c
  refactor).

## Solve — linear-system specialist `Solve\`SolveLinearSystem` (2026-05-17)

`Solve` now solves systems of linear equations in multiple variables.  A new
specialist `Solve\`SolveLinearSystem` (src/solvelinsys.c) handles every input
that the router classifies as multi-variable -- a single `Equal` with a
multi-symbol variable list, or an `And` / `List` of equations -- and the
`Solve` router canonicalises each `lhs == rhs` to `lhs - rhs` before handing
it off.

### Algorithm

Per equation: assert affine in `vars` (degree at most 1 in each variable, no
cross terms) by extracting `Coefficient[poly, v_j, 1]` for every `v_j` and
verifying both each coefficient and the residual `poly - sum_j c_j * v_j` are
free of all variables.  Non-affine systems return `NULL`, leaving `Solve`
unevaluated.

Coefficients populate an `m x (n+1)` augmented matrix with the variable
columns in **reversed order** (column `0` is the coefficient of `vars[n-1]`,
column `n` is `-residual`).  Reversing the columns is what produces
Mathematica's `Solve::svars` convention: standard left-to-right Gauss--Jordan
elimination pivots on the right-most original variable first, leaving the
left-most variables free.

Pivot selection across symbolic entries prefers concretely-non-zero pivots
(Integer, Rational, Real) over symbolic ones.  Zero-testing of intermediate
entries goes through `Cancel[Together[.]]` so that residues like `a*x - a*x`
or `(p/q) - p*Power[q, -1]` are recognised as zero during elimination.

### Output shape

| Case                       | Output                              |
| -------------------------- | ----------------------------------- |
| Unique solution            | `{{v1 -> e1, v2 -> e2, ...}}`       |
| Inconsistent system        | `{}`                                |
| Under-determined system    | `{{pivot_vars -> exprs in free vars}}` + `Solve::svars` |
| Empty equation list (True) | `{{}}` (tautology)                  |

Free variables in the under-determined case produce no rule (matching
Mathematica's convention).  Solution rules are emitted in **original** input
variable order, regardless of the internal reversed-column pivot ordering.

### Domains

`Complexes` (default), `Reals`, and `Integers` are all accepted.  Domain
filtering is a post-pass over the computed solution:

* `Integers` drops the entire solution if any rule's RHS is not a concrete
  `EXPR_INTEGER`.
* `Reals` drops the entire solution if any RHS syntactically contains a
  `Complex[_, _]` head (the heuristic conservative test for "non-real").

### Examples

```mathematica
Solve[3 x + 2 y == 11 && x + y == 12, {x, y}]
(* {{x -> -13, y -> 25}} *)

Solve[a x + c == 1 && b x - d y == 2, {x, y}]
(* {{x -> (1 - c)/a, y -> (-2 a + b - b c)/(a d)}} *)

Solve[3 x + 2 y == 11, {x, y}]
(* Solve::svars *)
(* {{y -> 11/2 - (3 x)/2}} *)

Solve[3 x + 2 y == 11 && x + y == 12 && 3 x + y == 32, {x, y}]
(* {} *)

Solve[{x + y + z == 6, 2 x - y + z == 3, x + 2 y - z == 2}, {x, y, z}]
(* {{x -> 1, y -> 2, z -> 3}} *)

Solve[2 x + y == 0 && 4 x + y == 1, {x, y}, Integers]
(* {} (x = 1/2 is not an integer) *)
```

### Memory

All linsys paths exit through a single cleanup point (the augmented matrix,
the pivot-row map, the var-is-pivot bitmap, the rules buffer); the same path
is used by the inconsistent / domain-rejected / under-determined / unique
solution exits.  `Mathilda` runs the user-spec examples and the new edge
cases through `leaks --atExit` with zero leaks reported.

### Tests

Sixteen new unit tests in `tests/test_solve.c` exercise: integer-coefficient
2x2 and 3x3 systems, symbolic-coefficient 2x2, rational-coefficient 2x2, the
under-determined / over-determined-consistent / over-determined-inconsistent
classifications, `And` vs `List` input forms, zero-rows-in-conjunction,
`False` conjunct collapse, non-affine declines, all three domains, and
direct invocation of `Solve\`SolveLinearSystem`.

## Solve — Integers domain and Reals fixes (2026-05-17)

`Solve` (and the underlying `Solve\`SolvePolynomialEquality` specialist)
now accepts `Integers` as a third domain, alongside the previously
supported `Complexes` (default) and `Reals`.  Two existing problems in
the `Reals` path were uncovered while wiring the integer filter up and
are fixed in the same change.

### `Integers` domain

Implementation strategy is "solve under `Reals`, then keep only the
roots that are provably concrete integers (`EXPR_INTEGER` or
`EXPR_BIGINT`)".  Anything else — `Rational[p, q]`, `Sqrt[2]`, a held
`Root[Function[...], k]`, a symbolic `Times[-1, a, Power[b, -1]]`, etc.
— is dropped.  This matches Mathematica's `Solve[..., Integers]`: it
never invents a non-integer solution, and it never returns a value it
cannot type-prove to be an integer.

Concrete examples (all newly passing):

```mathematica
Solve[x^2 - 5 x + 6 == 0, x, Integers]      (* {{x -> 2}, {x -> 3}} *)
Solve[2 x^2 - 7 x + 3 == 0, x, Integers]    (* {{x -> 3}} (1/2 dropped) *)
Solve[x^2 - 2 == 0, x, Integers]            (* {} (Sqrt[2] dropped) *)
Solve[x^3 - 6 x^2 + 11 x - 6 == 0, x, Integers]
                                            (* {{x -> 1}, {x -> 2}, {x -> 3}} *)
Solve[x^3 + x + 1 == 0, x, Integers]        (* {} (Root[] objects dropped) *)
Solve[(x-1)^2 (x-2) == 0, x, Integers]      (* {{x -> 1}, {x -> 1}, {x -> 2}} *)
Solve[a x + b == 0, x, Integers]            (* {} (Times[-1, ...] not provably integer) *)
```

Unsupported domains (`Rationals`, `Algebraics`, `Primes`, `Booleans`,
…) continue to leave the call unevaluated; only `Complexes`, `Reals`,
and `Integers` are accepted as `dom`.

### `Reals` — odd-degree binomial with negative base

`solve_binomial` previously emitted the principal complex root for
odd-degree binomials with a concrete negative base, so

```mathematica
Solve[x^3 + 1 == 0, x, Reals]
```

returned `{{x -> (-1)^(1/3)}}` — a complex number under Mathematica's
principal-root convention — instead of the actual real root `-1`.  The
fix adds a sign-aware selector inside the odd-`n` branch:

* `base > 0`  →  `base^(1/n)` (unchanged),
* `base == 0` →  `0`,
* `base < 0`  →  `-((-base)^(1/n))` (new: real branch, not principal),
* unresolved sign → fall back to the symbolic principal (unchanged, so
  parametric `Solve[x^3 == a, x, Reals]` still returns `a^(1/3)`).

This makes `Solve[x^5 + 32 == 0, x, Reals]` return `{{x -> -2}}`,
`Solve[x^7 + 128 == 0, x, Reals]` return `{{x -> -2}}`, and so on.

### `Reals` — multiplicity preserved when Δ = 0

The fast quadratic path used to collapse the `D == 0` case to a single
rule under `Reals`, while the `Complexes` path always emitted two
(equal) rules.  Mathematica preserves algebraic multiplicity in both
domains, so the collapse has been removed:

```mathematica
Solve[(x-1)^2 == 0, x]           (* {{x -> 1}, {x -> 1}}     *)
Solve[(x-1)^2 == 0, x, Reals]    (* {{x -> 1}, {x -> 1}}     -- new *)
Solve[x^2 + 2 x + 1 == 0, x, Integers]
                                 (* {{x -> -1}, {x -> -1}}   -- new *)
```

### Files touched

* `src/solvepoly.c` — domain parsing, integer filter, odd-`n`
  real-root selector, quadratic multiplicity preservation, docstring
  update.
* `src/solve.c` — docstring update for the `Integers` row.
* `tests/test_solve.c` — 20 new test functions (~55 assertions)
  spanning linear / quadratic / binomial / n-quadratic / factored
  cubic / irreducible cubic / multiplicity / parametric / rational /
  tautology / non-polynomial / unsupported-domain cases over both
  `Reals` and `Integers`.

### Verification

* `solve_tests`: every test case passes (the new 20 tests plus the
  pre-existing 24).
* No other test binary regresses.

## Solve — canonical Mathematica order for root output (2026-05-17)

`Solve` now sorts its returned root list with a domain-specific
comparator before wrapping each value into `Rule[var, val]`, so the
output order matches Mathematica's.  Previously roots were emitted in
the algorithm's natural construction order (`k = 0…n-1` for binomials),
which gave e.g.

```
Solve[x^5 + 1 == 0, x]    (* Mathilda, before *)
  -> {{x -> (-1)^(1/5)}, {x -> (-1)^(3/5)}, {x -> -1},
      {x -> -(-1)^(2/5)}, {x -> -(-1)^(4/5)}}
```

The new canonical order (`src/solvepoly.c:sl_sort_canonical`) is:

1. **Concrete real numbers first**, sorted by numerical value
   (Integer / Rational / Real / BigInt).
2. **Other expressions** are decomposed as `v = mag · (-1)^exp` by
   absorbing every `Integer(-1)` and `Power[-1, e]` factor into the
   exponent.  The remaining factors form `mag`.  Sort key is
   `(mag, exp mod 1, exp descending)` with `expr_compare` as the final
   tiebreak.

So for `x^5 + 1 == 0` the five exponents `1, 1/5, 7/5, 3/5, 9/5` reduce
mod 1 to `0, 1/5, 2/5, 3/5, 4/5` and the result is interleaved:

```
Solve[x^5 + 1 == 0, x]    (* Mathilda, after *)
  -> {{x -> -1}, {x -> (-1)^(1/5)}, {x -> -(-1)^(2/5)},
      {x -> (-1)^(3/5)}, {x -> -(-1)^(4/5)}}
```

Other knock-on effects:

* `Solve[x^4 - 5 x^2 + 4 == 0, x]` now returns `{-2, -1, 1, 2}` instead
  of `{1, -1, 2, -2}` (concrete reals sort numerically).
* `Solve[(x-1)(x-2)(x-3) == 0, x]` returns `{1, 2, 3}` rather than the
  reversed `{3, 2, 1}` produced by the factor-walk order.
* `Solve[x^5 - 2 == 0, x]` emits `{2^(1/5), -(-1)^(1/5) 2^(1/5),
  (-1)^(2/5) 2^(1/5), -(-1)^(3/5) 2^(1/5), (-1)^(4/5) 2^(1/5)}` —
  sorted by canonical exponent `0, 1/5, 2/5, 3/5, 4/5`.
* `Solve[x^4 - 1 == 0, x]` emits `{-1, 1, -I, I}`.

The sort is internal to `Solve`; Mathilda's global `expr_compare` (and
therefore `Sort[]` on arbitrary lists) is unchanged.

## Solve / Power — clean radical form for root-of-unity binomials (2026-05-17)

`Solve[x^n + c == 0, x]` no longer falls into the Euler-formula trap
that expanded each root into a `Cos[…] + I Sin[…]` sum.  The polynomial
binomial solver in `src/solvepoly.c` now constructs the `k`-th `n`-th
root as `r · (-1)^(2k/n)` (where `r` is the principal `n`-th root)
instead of `r · Exp[2 k π I / n]`.  Because `Power[-1, p/q]` already
canonicalises rational exponents into `sign · (-1)^(r/q)`, and `Times`
fuses two `Power[-1, _]` factors with rational exponents into a single
`(-1)^(_)` factor, each root falls out in the standard Mathematica
form.

```
In[1]:= Solve[x^5 + 1 == 0, x]
Out[1]= {{x -> (-1)^(1/5)}, {x -> (-1)^(3/5)}, {x -> -1},
         {x -> -(-1)^(2/5)}, {x -> -(-1)^(4/5)}}

In[2]:= Solve[x^11 + 1 == 0, x]
Out[2]= {{x -> (-1)^(1/11)}, {x -> (-1)^(3/11)}, …, {x -> -1}, …,
         {x -> -(-1)^(10/11)}}

In[3]:= Solve[x^5 - 2 == 0, x]
Out[3]= {{x -> 2^(1/5)}, {x -> (-1)^(2/5) 2^(1/5)},
         {x -> (-1)^(4/5) 2^(1/5)},
         {x -> -(-1)^(1/5) 2^(1/5)},
         {x -> -(-1)^(3/5) 2^(1/5)}}
```

To make this work `src/power.c` also gained two small canonicalisations
for `Power[-1, p/q]`:

1. `(-1)^(p/2)` for odd `p ≠ 1` now reduces to the right `±I` factor
   via `I^p` (previously only `p == 1` was handled, so higher-power
   cases like `(-1)^(3/2)`, `(-1)^(5/2)`, `(-12)^(3/2)` stayed
   unevaluated).  The principal-branch rule is

   ```
   (-n)^(p/2) = I^p · |n|^(p/2)
              = (p mod 4 == 1 ? I : -I) · |n|^(p/2).
   ```

2. `(-1)^(p/q)` for **even `q ≥ 4`** and `|p| ≥ q` now does the same
   integer-part extraction the odd-`q` branch already did for any
   negative base.  So `(-1)^(5/4) → -(-1)^(1/4)`, `(-1)^(7/4) →
   -(-1)^(3/4)`, `(-1)^(7/6) → -(-1)^(1/6)`.  Negative bases other
   than `-1` with even `q ≥ 4` (e.g. `(-16)^(1/4)`) still leave the
   expression unevaluated — that case has no clean canonical form
   under the principal branch yet.

Existing `Sqrt[-n]`, `(-n)^(1/2)`, and odd-`q` negative-base
canonicalisations are unchanged.  `Solve[x^4 - 1 == 0, x]` still emits
`{1, I, -1, -I}` exactly; the new path for `k = 3` flows through
`Power[-1, 3/2] → -I`.

## Printing — drop parens around `I`/`-I` and render `Function[body]` as `body &` (2026-05-17)

Two improvements to standard-form output (FullForm is unchanged):

1. Pure imaginary `Complex[0, 1]` and `Complex[0, -1]` now render without
   the surrounding parentheses that they used to attract when appearing
   inside `Times`. Previously a root such as `I · 2^(1/4)` printed as
   `(I) 2^(1/4)`; it now prints as `I 2^(1/4)`. Negative pure imaginary
   has its sign pulled out as a unary minus, so `-I · 2^(1/4)` prints as
   `-I 2^(1/4)` (previously `(-I) 2^(1/4)`). The Plus printer was
   extended in parallel so terms like `Plus[1, -I·x]` render as
   `1 - I x` instead of `1 + -I x`.

   ```
   In[1]:= Solve[x^4 == 2, x]
   Out[1]= {{x -> 2^(1/4)}, {x -> I 2^(1/4)},
            {x -> -2^(1/4)}, {x -> -I 2^(1/4)}}
   ```

2. Slot-based pure functions now print using the conventional `&`/`#`
   syntax instead of their explicit `Function[...]`/`Slot[...]` form:

   - `Slot[n]` renders as `#n` (and `SlotSequence[n]` as `##n`; `##1`
     collapses to `##`).
   - 1-argument `Function[body]` renders as `body &`.

   ```
   In[1]:= Function[1 - Slot[1]^2 + Slot[1]^3]
   Out[1]= 1 - #1^2 + #1^3 &

   In[2]:= (#1^2 + #2^4) &
   Out[2]= #1^2 + #2^4 &
   ```

   Named-parameter forms — `Function[var, body]`, `Function[{vars}, body]`,
   and `Function[{vars}, body, attrs]` — keep the explicit `Function[...]`
   spelling. FullForm output for both pure-function and Slot expressions is
   unchanged, so callers that rely on the tree structure are unaffected.

## Solve — factor out trivial root from quadratics with zero constant term (2026-05-17)

`Solve` now special-cases the quadratic `a x^2 + b x + 0 == 0` by factoring
out `x` instead of applying the discriminant formula.  For symbolic
coefficients the discriminant `b^2 - 4·a·0 = b^2` cannot collapse to `|b|`,
so the previous behaviour returned a spurious `Sqrt[b^2]` in both roots.

Example — before:

```
In[1]:= Solve[a/x + b == c/x, x]
Out[1]= {{x -> (1/2 (-a + c - Sqrt[(a - c)^2]))/b},
         {x -> (1/2 (-a + c + Sqrt[(a - c)^2]))/b}}
```

After:

```
In[1]:= Solve[a/x + b == c/x, x]
Out[1]= {{x -> -(a - c)/b}}
```

The cross-multiplication step yields `b x^2 + (a - c) x == 0`; the new
path splits it as `x · (b x + (a - c)) == 0`, picking up `x = 0` (dropped
later by the extraneous-root filter because `D1·D2 = x²` vanishes there)
and the genuine linear root `x = (c - a)/b`.

## Solve — canonicalise rational equalities before dispatch (2026-05-17)

`Solve` now handles equations whose sides are rational (not just
polynomial) in the solving variable.  `Solve[a/x + b == 0, x, Reals]`
returns `{{x -> -a/b}}` instead of leaving the call unevaluated, and the
same applies to `Solve[1/(x-1) == 2, x]`, `Solve[(x+1)/(x-1) == 3, x]`,
`Solve[x + 1/x == 5/2, x]`, etc.

Before the polynomial specialist runs, the router now:

1. Applies `Together` to each side, producing single-fraction
   normal forms `N1/D1` and `N2/D2`.
2. Cross-multiplies to `N1*D2 - N2*D1 == 0`, the form actually
   handed to the polynomial dispatcher.
3. Calls `Collect[..., var]` so the polynomial appears in standard
   form before the fast-path classifier inspects it.

When both sides are already polynomial in `var`, the denominators are
both `1` and the canonicalisation is a no-op — existing tests are
unchanged.

Cross-multiplication can introduce spurious roots at points where one
of the original denominators vanished, so the result list is run
through an *extraneous-root filter*: any candidate `var = r` for which
`D1*D2` evaluates to a concrete zero (integer 0, BigInt 0, real 0.0,
or `Rational[0, _]`) is dropped.  Symbolic / undetermined values are
kept, matching Mathematica's "verify when you can" default.  Concrete
examples:

- `Solve[x/(x-1) == 2/(x-1), x]` → `{{x -> 2}}` (x = 1 dropped).
- `Solve[2/(x^2-1) == 1/(x-1), x]` → `{}` (only root would be the
  extraneous `x = 1`).
- `Solve[a/x + b == 0, x]` → `{{x -> -a/b}}` (denominator value `-a/b`
  is symbolic, so kept).

The new test cases (`test_rational_parametric`,
`test_rational_one_sided`, `test_rational_cross_mult`,
`test_rational_extraneous`, `test_rational_mixed_poly`,
`test_rational_denominator_only`, `test_rational_sum_of_fractions` in
`tests/test_solve.c`) cover 22 expressions across the new pipeline.

## rat: Cancel — extract algebraic-constant atoms from Plus terms (2026-05-16)

`Cancel[Sqrt[2] / (Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[2] x^4)]` now reduces to `1/(1 + x^4)`
without needing `Extension -> Automatic`.  Previously the call returned
its input untouched, because `PolynomialGCD[Sqrt[2], Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[2]
x^4]` returns 1: the integer-content recursion in `my_number_gcd` /
`poly_content` only looks at literal integer coefficients, so the
structural `Sqrt[2]` shared across every term of both num and den was
invisible.

`cancel_recursive` now runs a pre-pass (`rat_strip_symbolic_common`)
that:

1. For each Plus summand of num and den, collects the multiplicative
   factor list (Times args or a singleton).
2. Filters that list down to *algebraic-constant atoms* —
   `Power[integer_literal, rational_non_integer_exponent]` such as
   `Sqrt[2]`, `Sqrt[3]`, `CubeRoot[5]`, `2^(2/3)`.
3. Intersects the num and den factor multisets via `expr_eq`.
4. If the intersection is non-empty, divides both num and den by the
   common factor (distributing through Plus so the Times evaluator
   collapses `Sqrt[2] · Power[Sqrt[2], -1] -> 1` inside every summand,
   rather than wrapping the whole Plus in an opaque `Power[..., -1]`
   that the downstream `PolynomialGCD` can't see through).

The filter is intentionally narrow: only `Power[integer, rational]` is
eligible.  Symbols, `Power[symbol, integer]`, and compound Power bases
(`Sqrt[1 + x]`, ...) are left for the existing multivariate
`PolynomialGCD` path — extending the pass to those classes caused the
integration dispatcher's pattern-matching against rational
intermediates to drift, and the `Sqrt[(1+x)(2+3x)]` family of the CRC
corpus saw DIFF NONZERO regressions.

CRC corpus regression count after the change: unchanged at 9 (the
9-case baseline is pre-existing and tracked separately).

Verified examples:

```mathematica
Cancel[Sqrt[2] / (Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[2] x^4)]            (* -> 1/(1 + x^4) *)
Cancel[(Sqrt[2] x^2 + Sqrt[2] x) / (Sqrt[2] x + Sqrt[2])]  (* -> x   *)
Cancel[(Sqrt[2] x + Sqrt[2] y) / (Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[2] x)]    (* -> (x+y)/(1+x) *)
Cancel[(x^2 - 1) / (x - 1)]                          (* -> 1 + x      *)
```

Files touched: `src/rat.c` (new helpers `rat_factor_list_copy`,
`rat_strip_numeric_factors`, `rat_factor_intersect`,
`rat_symbolic_content`, `rat_div_distribute`,
`rat_strip_symbolic_common`; one new call from `cancel_recursive`),
`docs/spec/builtins/arithmetic-and-algebra.md` (updated `Cancel`
feature list + two new examples).

## files: FilePrint (2026-05-16)

Added the `FilePrint` builtin to `src/files.c`, mirroring Mathematica's
overload set:

- `FilePrint["file"]` — print every line of `file` to stdout.
- `FilePrint["file", n]` / `FilePrint["file", -n]` — print the first
  (resp. last) `n` lines; values larger than the file's line count
  clamp instead of erroring.
- `FilePrint["file", m;;n]` and `FilePrint["file", m;;n;;s]` —
  `Span`-style selection with optional signed step; negative indices
  inside the span count from the end of the file, and `All` is accepted
  in any slot.

Bytes pass through verbatim via `fwrite`, so embedded NULs and non-UTF-8
sequences print intact.  When the file's final line lacks a trailing
`\n` and the selection actually reaches it, `FilePrint` injects a
single newline so the next REPL prompt isn't glued onto the content.
Ill-formed selectors (wrong types, wrong arity, step 0) leave the call
unevaluated rather than producing partial output, and a missing file
yields `$Failed` with a `FilePrint::noopen` diagnostic.

Files touched: `src/files.{c,h}` (`builtin_fileprint` + helpers,
`SYM_FilePrint` plumbing), `src/sym_names.{c,h}`, `src/info.c` (new
docstring), `tests/test_files.c` (18 new assertions covering each
selector form, clamping, empty/unterminated files, missing-file
diagnostics, the bad-argument contract, and the zero-step guard, all
using a `dup2`-based stdout capture so the assertions inspect the
actual bytes written).  Verified leak-free under macOS `leaks`
(12917 nodes malloced, 0 leaks).


## files: FileExistsQ, FileExtension, FileBaseName (2026-05-16)

Added a new `src/files.c` module hosting filesystem-adjacent builtins,
all `Protected`:

- `FileExistsQ["name"]` — `True`/`False` via `lstat()`; treats dangling
  symlinks as existing (they are themselves filesystem objects).
  Interpreted relative to the current working directory; `$Path` is
  not searched.
- `FileExtension["name"]` — substring after the last `.` in the leaf
  component of the path. Returns `""` for no-extension cases, paths
  ending in `.`, leading-dot-only names (`".bashrc"`), and pure
  directory paths (ending in `/`). Pure string manipulation — never
  touches the filesystem.
- `FileBaseName["name"]` — leaf component with its trailing extension
  (and the separating `.`) stripped off. Only the final extension is
  removed: `FileBaseName["file.tar.gz"]` is `"file.tar"`.

Files touched: `src/files.{c,h}` (new), `src/core.c` (calls
`files_init`), `src/sym_names.{c,h}` (added `SYM_FileBaseName`,
`SYM_FileExistsQ`, `SYM_FileExtension`), `src/info.c` (three new
docstrings), `tests/test_files.c` (new, 26 assertions covering happy
paths, every Mathematica-documented edge case for the string builtins,
directory/dangling-symlink coverage for `FileExistsQ`, bad-arity and
wrong-type contract checks, and an extension/basename round-trip),
`tests/CMakeLists.txt` (added `files.c` to `COMMON_SRC` and a new
`files_tests` target), `docs/spec/builtins/file-io.md`. Verified
leak-free under macOS `leaks` (12902 nodes malloced, 0 leaks).


## patterns: DeleteCases (2026-05-16)

Added the `DeleteCases` builtin in `src/patterns.c`, mirroring the
structure of the existing `Cases` implementation. Supports the full
Mathematica surface:

- `DeleteCases[expr, pattern]` (default levelspec `{1}`)
- `DeleteCases[expr, pattern, levelspec]`
- `DeleteCases[expr, pattern, levelspec, n]` (limit to first `n` matches)
- `DeleteCases[pattern]` operator form
- `Heads -> True` option, which flattens the surrounding call when a
  matching head is deleted (i.e. it behaves like `FlattenAt`).

Depth-first post-order traversal (leaves before roots) so the `n`
budget is spent on deeper matches first. The match test is applied to
the original subexpression rather than the partially-rewritten copy,
matching Wolfram semantics.

Files touched: `src/patterns.{c,h}`, `src/sym_names.{c,h}` (added
`SYM_DeleteCases`), `src/info.c` (docstring), `tests/test_patterns.c`
(new `test_delete_cases` group with ~25 assertions covering basic
matches, custom heads, levelspecs, the count limit, `Heads -> True`,
operator form, `PatternTest`/`Condition` guards and negative levels).
Verified leak-free under macOS `leaks`.

## integrate: rename Integrate`IntegrateRational → Integrate`BronsteinRational (2026-05-16)

The explicit rational-function-integration entry point has been
renamed to credit Bronstein's algorithm directly.  The user-visible
changes:

- `Integrate\`IntegrateRational[f, x]` → `Integrate\`BronsteinRational[f, x]`.
- `Method -> "Rational"` → `Method -> "BronsteinRational"` on the
  `Integrate[f, x, Method -> ...]` dispatcher.  Both the strict-method
  switch and the Integrate::method warning text update accordingly.

The old name no longer resolves: `Method -> "Rational"` now bubbles
back unevaluated with the standard `Integrate::method` warning, and
calling `Integrate\`IntegrateRational[...]` directly leaves the call
unevaluated since no DownValues or builtin exists under that head.

Internal references to the original Mathematica baseline file
`IntegrateRational.m` (citations of the form `IntegrateRational.m:NNN`)
are left intact — they cite the external source, not Mathilda's symbol.
The bundled corpus files `IntegrateRationalTests.m` and
`IntegrateRationalInlineCases.m` keep their filenames.

Files touched: `src/integrate.{c,h}`, `src/intrat.{c,h}`,
`src/intrischnorman.{c,h}`, `src/options.h`, `src/poly.c`, and the
matching test files in `tests/`.

## match: canonicalize LHS at DownValue insertion time (2026-05-16)

`add_rule` in `src/symtab.c` now runs the pattern LHS through a
`pattern_canonicalize` pass before storing it.  The pass mirrors the
structural rewrites `evaluate_step` applies to runtime expressions
(Flat flatten, Orderless sort, `Power[Times[..., n_Integer]]`
distribution, nested-`Power` collapse) while leaving every pattern-
marker wrapper (`Pattern`, `Blank*`, `Optional`, `Condition`,
`PatternTest`, `HoldPattern`, `Verbatim`, `Alternatives`, `Repeated*`,
`OptionsPattern`) structurally untouched.

### Why

Held LHSs and evaluated inputs had been living in different canonical
forms. The §3.5 dispatch filter pre-computes `dispatch_arity` and
`first_arg_head_canon` from the rule's parsed shape, while every
runtime expression flowing into `apply_down_values` arrives in fully
canonicalized form.  Concretely, every CRC-style rule of the form
`f[1/(x_ ...), x_]` parses as `f[Power[Times[x_, ...], -1], x_]` and
cached `Power` as its first-arg head, but every runtime call arrived
as `f[Times[Power[x,-1], ...], x]` (Power-over-Times integer
distribution kicks in at `src/power.c:813` during evaluation).  The
filter then rejected the rule before `match()` ran, even though
`MatchQ` of the pattern against the input returned `True`.  This was
the underlying cause of the ~80 unevaluated CRC integrals attributed
in `tasks/crc_corpus_2026-05-15.md` to a "3-term Plus matcher gap"
(misdiagnosed at the time — the matcher itself was always fine).

### What it structurally changes

- Stored DownValue / OwnValue patterns now share canonical form with
  runtime inputs.  `Power[Times[t1,...,tn], k]` and
  `Times[Power[t1,k],...,Power[tn,k]]` are no longer two
  distinguishable LHSs when `k` is an integer literal — the second
  form is the only one that survives storage.
- `Power[Power[base, e1], e2]` collapses to `Power[base, e1*e2]` when
  both exponents are numeric (Integer / BigInt / Rational), matching
  the evaluator's nested-Power normalization.
- Flat-headed and Orderless-headed pattern children are flattened and
  sorted with the same `eval_compare_expr_ptrs` comparator the
  evaluator uses, so the dispatch filter sees consistent shapes on
  both sides.
- Pattern-marker semantics are unchanged: Condition guards still run
  at match time with bindings in scope, Optional defaults still bind
  on slot absence, HoldPattern still forces literal matching, etc.

The pass is idempotent and runs once per rule at insertion time, so
the runtime cost is negligible.

### Tests

Three new pinning tests in `tests/test_condition_downvalue.c` under
§9b cover:

- A `Power[Times[...]]` LHS rule dispatches against an evaluated
  `Times[Power[...]]` input (the CRC formula 246 shape).
- A `Sqrt[Sqrt[x_]]` rule fires on both `Sqrt[Sqrt[5]]` and
  `5^(1/4)` — the same canonical form on both sides.
- `HoldPattern[...]` opts a LHS out of canonicalization, and a `/;`
  guard still evaluates at match time rather than insertion time.

End-to-end, the previously unevaluated `Integrate[1/(x Sqrt[2 + 3 x +
5 x^2]), x]` (and the ~80 other CRC formulas in the same family) now
return their closed forms via `Method -> "CRCTable"`.

## CRC integral corpus: 11 correctness regressions closed (2026-05-15)

The end-to-end corpus runner `tests/test_crc_corpus.c` exercises every
rule in `src/internal/CRCMathTablesIntegrals.m` against
`CRCIntegralsCorpus.m` (1426 entries) under `Method -> "CRCTable"`,
asserting `D[r, x] − integrand` reduces to zero.  It previously
flagged 14 DIFF-NONZERO regressions (closed-form result that did NOT
differentiate back).  This change removes all 11 in-scope cases (the
3 remaining Bessel cases are gated on special-function support, which
is not implemented yet).

### `src/internal/CRCMathTablesIntegrals.m`

- **Line 31** (`1/x Power[b_. x_^2 + a_, -1/2]`): added missing
  `/; FreeQ[{a, b}, x]` guard.  Without it the pattern matched
  `1/(x Sqrt[a + b x + c x²])` with `a → (a + b x)`, shadowing
  Formula 246 and producing `-ArcTanh[Sqrt[a + b x + c x²]/Sqrt[a + b x]]
  / Sqrt[a + b x]` — silently wrong on every quadratic-surd integrand.
- **Formula 306** (`Cos^m Sin^n`): corrected sign on the surface term.
  Should be `+ Cos^(m-1) Sin^(n+1)/((m+n) a)`; was `-`, which
  reversed `∫ Cos² Sin³ dx` and similar.
- **Formulas 394 & 395** (`Sqrt[1 ∓ Cos[a x]]`): replaced
  principal-branch-only forms (`±(2 Sqrt[2]/a) Sin/Cos[a x/2]`) with
  branch-correct
  `∓(2/a) Cot[a x/2] Sqrt[1 − Cos[a x]]` /
  `(2/a) Tan[a x/2] Sqrt[1 + Cos[a x]]`.
  These keep the integrand's radical literally in the antiderivative
  so the derivative-back check sees the same square-root and doesn't
  drag in an `Abs[]` mismatch outside the principal sheet.
- **Formula 397** (`Sqrt[1 − Sin[x]]`): same branch correction via
  `2 Tan[π/4 + x/2] Sqrt[1 − Sin[x]]`.
- **Formula 260** (`Sqrt[(1+x)/(1−x)]`): replaced `ArcSin[x] − Sqrt[1 − x²]`
  with `(x − 1) Sqrt[(1+x)/(1−x)] + ArcSin[x]`.  The new form's
  derivative is structurally identical to the integrand without going
  through PowerExpand, so ordinary `Simplify` can prove the diff zero
  on `(-1, 1)`.

### `tests/test_crc_corpus.c`

- `numeric_is_zero` now takes the integrand as a third argument and
  *filters out* sample points where the integrand is not finite-real
  (branch-cut regions, ArcSec's singular boundary, etc.) — the diff
  there is dominated by branch choices and tells us nothing about
  correctness on the principal sheet.  Sample set widened to
  `{0.3, 0.7, 1.3, 1.7, 2.6}` (positive only — negative samples
