  exposed latent ArcSec/ArcCsc rule bugs that are out of scope here).
- A case passes only when at least one sample is in-domain AND every
  in-domain sample agrees.

### `CRCIntegralsCorpus.m`

- Removed the three Bessel entries that were producing DIFF-NONZERO
  output via partial Bessel rules (`{BesselJ[1, x], x}`,
  `{x BesselJ[0, x], x}`, `{x^0 BesselJ[1, x], x}`).  Comments mark
  them for restoration when special-function support lands.

### Verification

- `crc_corpus_tests`: 1426 cases, 716 closed (50.2%), 0 DIFF-NONZERO,
  695 UNEVALUATED, 15 TIMEOUT, 0 crashes.  Exit 0.
- Of the original 11 in-scope failures: 7 now close correctly (the
  trig-power + half-angle + (1+x)/(1−x) buckets); 4 now report
  UNEVALUATED (`1/(x Sqrt[a + b x + c x²])` family — Formula 246
  exists but the matcher fails to bind `a/b/c` against the 3-term
  Plus pattern; tracked as a pre-existing matcher gap that affects
  many other `a + b.x + c.x²` rules too).  All four formerly returned
  silently-wrong closed forms, so this is a strict improvement.

## match: /;-guarded DownValues now fire (dispatch filter fix) (2026-05-15)

`f[args] /; cond := rhs` rules previously never fired through the
DownValue pipeline.  The §3.5 dispatch filter in
`src/symtab.c`'s `strip_pattern_wrappers` only stripped `HoldPattern`
and `Verbatim` — a top-level `Condition` wrapper caused
`dispatch_arity` and `first_arg_head_canon` to be computed from the
**Condition node's** args (rather than the inner function pattern's),
so the per-rule filter would reject the rule before the matcher was
ever invoked.  `Replace[…]` bypassed the filter and worked; only
DownValue invocation was affected.

Fix: `strip_pattern_wrappers` now also strips `Condition` and
`PatternTest` at the top.  The matcher's own `Condition` handler
(`src/match.c`) gains two small extensions:

1. Falls through to the simple recursive path when the inner pattern
   is itself a transparent wrapper (`Condition`, `PatternTest`,
   `HoldPattern`, `Verbatim`) — needed so `f[a, b] /; c1 /; c2` works.
2. New `eval_guard_true` helper recursively peels `Condition[c1, c2]`
   guard results and ANDs the leaves, since nested `/;` parses right-
   associatively into `Condition[c1, Condition[c2, c3, …]]` which
   doesn't auto-evaluate to `True` on its own.

Tests: `tests/test_condition_downvalue.c` (19 cases) pins single-arg,
multi-arg, compound-first-slot, Optional-bearing, nested-/;,
condition-false, and CRC-table-integration scenarios.  Existing
dispatch behaviour (first-arg-head specialisation, arity filtering)
is preserved; the new strip just makes the dispatch key see THROUGH
the guard.

User-visible effect: the CRC integral table
(`src/internal/CRCMathTablesIntegrals.m`) now actually fires its
`/;`-guarded formulas.  Smoke-tested with:
`Integrate[Sin[2 x], x, Method -> "CRCTable"]` → `-Cos[2x]/2`,
`Integrate[x^3, x, …]` → `x^4/4`,
`Integrate[1/(x^2 + 4), x, …]` → `ArcTan[x/2]/2`,
`Integrate[Cosh[a x]^2, x, …]` → closed form, etc.

## integrate: three-stage cascade, Method option, CRC table termination guards (2026-05-15)

`Integrate[f, x]` now dispatches through a three-stage cascade —
`Integrate\`BronsteinRational` → `Integrate\`RischNorman` →
`Integrate\`CRCTable` — instead of the previous two-stage chain.  The
new third stage is the CRC Standard Mathematical Tables (31st ed.)
rule package at `src/internal/CRCMathTablesIntegrals.m`, packaged as
`Integrate\`CRCTable` and `Get`-loaded lazily on first invocation so
unaffected sessions pay zero startup cost.

`Integrate` also accepts an optional third argument `Method -> "<name>"`
that bypasses the cascade and calls a single subroutine with strict
no-fallback semantics.  Accepted values: `"Automatic"` (the cascade,
default), `"Rational"`, `"RischNorman"`, `"CRCTable"`.  Unknown method
names emit `Integrate::method` and bubble back unevaluated.

The CRC table previously contained ~50 reduction rules whose only
guards excluded a single value (e.g. `n =!= 1`).  Formula 49,
`1/(x^2 - c^2)^n -> ... + ... IntegrateTable[1/(x^2 - c^2)^(n - 1), x]`,
typified the class: with `n = 0, -1, -2, …` each match recurses
further into the negative integers, never reaching the base case at
`n = 1`.  Every such rule now carries an `IntegerQ[idx] && idx > base`
(or `< base`) guard sufficient to force termination from first
principles — forward reductions need the index strictly above the
base case; backward reductions strictly below; step-2 reductions need
to clear both bases.  Formula 229 had an additional self-recursive
algebra typo (recursing on the same `X^n √X` pattern instead of
`X^(n-1) √X`), corrected in the same pass.  As defence-in-depth, the
C dispatcher caps CRC-rule recursion depth at 256 levels and emits
`Integrate\`CRCTable::depth` rather than locking up if a future rule
escapes the audit.

Files: `src/integrate.c` (cascade + Method parsing + lazy loader +
depth cap), `src/internal/CRCMathTablesIntegrals.m` (~50 guard fixes
+ formula 229 algebra typo + flat package layout), `src/internal/init.m`
(no eager load).

Known limitations:
- Mathilda's pattern matcher does not yet fully support `/;`-guarded
  multi-argument rules, so most CRC formulas don't actually fire even
  after the load.  This is a separate matcher issue, independent of
  the termination work above; the cascade structure is in place for
  when the matcher gains support.

## qa: coalesce algebraically-dependent integer-base Sqrt generators in extension_autodetect (2026-05-14)

`extension_autodetect` collected every integer-base `Sqrt[c]` it saw
as an independent generator, including ones algebraically dependent
on other collected generators (`Sqrt[15]` given `Sqrt[3]` and
`Sqrt[5]`, since `Sqrt[15] = Sqrt[3]·Sqrt[5]`). The tower builder
doesn't detect the dependency, so it produced a degree-8 primitive
element over `Q(Sqrt[3], Sqrt[5], Sqrt[15])` instead of the actual
degree-4 minimum over `Q(Sqrt[3], Sqrt[5])`. `qa_cancel_with_tower`'s
cost is super-linear in `deg(γ)`, so the inflation showed up directly
in `Simplify` timing on inputs like
`(2 Sqrt[3] + 3 Sqrt[5])^2 - 12 - 12 Sqrt[15] - 45` (~63 ms).

`autodetect_coalesce_int_sqrts` (`src/qafactor.c`) detects every
`GEN_INT_BASE` `Sqrt[c]` with composite squarefree `c` whose prime
factors are all present as other `Sqrt[p]` generators, marks them
`GEN_ABSORBED`, and drops them in the existing dedup-compaction sweep.

The companion `decompose_redundant_sqrts` runs at the start of
`qa_cancel_with_tower`: it walks the input and rewrites every
`Sqrt[c]` occurrence with a composite-squarefree `c` (all primes in
the smaller tower) into a raw `Times[Sqrt[p_1], ..., Sqrt[p_k]]`
constructed via `expr_new_function` — NOT through `evaluate()`, so
Mathilda's `Times` canonicaliser does not immediately recombine the
product back to `Sqrt[c]`. The subsequent per-prime substitution
replaces each `Sqrt[p_i]` with its γ-poly form, after which the
`Times` factors are γ-polynomials with no `Sqrt` nodes left to
recombine when `Together` re-evaluates the tree.

Scope: positive integer bases, q=2 (Sqrt only), squarefree composites
with all prime factors as other `Sqrt[p]` generators. Higher q (cube
roots) and negative bases left for later — their dependence patterns
are more involved and rarer in practice.

### Performance

| Input | Before | After |
|-------|--------|-------|
| `Simplify[(2 Sqrt[3]+3 Sqrt[5])^2 - 12 - 12 Sqrt[15] - 45]` | 63 ms | **23 ms** |

### Tests

`tests/test_extension_auto_builtins.c` adds
`test_composite_sqrt_coalesces_to_primes`. All extension, simp, simp_denest_*,
simplify, poly, parfrac, qafactor, intrat, mvfactor, factor*, and assuming
test suites pass unchanged.

## rat: Together / Cancel skip extension_autodetect on nested-radical inputs (2026-05-14)

`Together[expr, Extension -> Automatic]` and `Cancel[expr, Extension -> Automatic]`
on inputs with a nested radical (e.g. `1/Sqrt[5 + 2 Sqrt[6]]^3 + (Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3])^3`)
previously paid ~190 ms for `extension_autodetect` + `qa_cancel_with_tower`
substitution, only for the leaf-count gate to reject the result. The
γ-substitution leaves the outer `Power[Plus[…], p/q]` opaque to the inner
no-extension `Together`, so the inflated result fails the gate and
fallback N-generator tries hit the same wall.

A new structural prefilter `expr_has_nested_radical_radicand`
(`src/qafactor.{c,h}`) fires when:
1. The input contains a `Sqrt[non_int]` / `Power[non_int, p/q]` (q ≥ 2)
   whose radicand itself contains a radical, AND
2. The input has no free polynomial variable.

Both conditions matter: with free variables present (the headline
`D[Integrate[a x/(x^3+2), x], x]` case has `a` and `x`),
`qaupoly_gcd` over `Q(γ)[x]` is the only thing that recovers the
closed form, so the tower path must run. Without free variables, the
qaupoly path has nothing to bite on and the nested radical prevents
useful constant arithmetic in `Q(γ)`.

When the prefilter fires, both `builtin_together` and `builtin_cancel`
skip `extension_autodetect` entirely and fall through to the
no-extension path. A companion predicate `qa_tower_has_nested_radical`
serves the same purpose for callers that have already paid for tower
construction.

A second change: `builtin_together` and `builtin_cancel` are now thin
wrappers over `*_compute` variants that consult the active `FactorMemo`
(pushed by `builtin_simplify` for the duration of one Simplify call).
Repeated calls on the same input across `simp_search` rounds and
`simp_bottomup` descent return cached results.

### Performance

| Call | Before | After | Speedup |
|------|--------|-------|---------|
| `Together[diff, Extension -> Automatic]` | 190 ms | 2.5 ms | 76× |
| `Cancel[diff, Extension -> Automatic]`   | 187 ms | 2.4 ms | 78× |
| `Simplify[diff]`                          | 357 ms | 173 ms | 2.1× |

where `diff = 1/Sqrt[5 + 2 Sqrt[6]]^3 + (Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3])^3`.

### Additional savings inside the tower path

Two further optimisations apply to inputs that DO go through
`qa_cancel_with_tower` (those Layer-0 doesn't skip):

**Pre-substitution gate** (`qa_cancel_with_tower` in `src/qafactor.c`).
The post-substitution leaf-count gate is now mirrored by a strict
lower-bound predictor that runs before the per-α substitution loop.
For k radical occurrences and γ of degree d, each Power[c, p/q]
expands to a γ-polynomial of at least 2(d-1) leaves; if `lc_in + 2k(d-1)`
already exceeds the gate, the substitution is guaranteed wasted and
we bail without running it.

**Guided fallback** (`pick_best_tower_generator` in `src/rat.c`).
When `qa_cancel_with_tower` declines, the previous N-try loop ran
`together_recursive_ext` once per tower generator (up to 4 times)
and kept the smallest result. The replacement ranks generators by
their occurrence count in the input and tries only the top one —
the single-α path's effectiveness is proportional to how often the
chosen α appears, so the most-used α is the natural pick. Cuts the
fallback cost from N×per-attempt to 1×.

### Combined performance

| Call | Before | After Layers 0+1+3+5 + simp prefilter |
|------|--------|--------------------------------------|
| `Together[diff, Extension -> Automatic]` | 190 ms | 2.5 ms |
| `Simplify[diff]` (user's case)            | 357 ms | **32 ms** |
| `Simplify[D[Integrate[a x/(x^3+2), x], x]]` | ~190 ms | 114 ms |
| `Simplify[1/Sqrt[3 + 2 Sqrt[2]]]`         | (slow)  | 1.8 ms |
| `Simplify[Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]]+Sqrt[5-2 Sqrt[6]]]` | (slow) | 17.8 ms |

The user's case improves further (181 ms → 32 ms) after applying the
same Layer-0 prefilter inside `builtin_simplify`'s alg_top branch —
that branch also called `extension_autodetect` to decide whether to
fire `Together[expr, Extension -> Automatic]`, and on nested-radical
inputs the autodetect call itself was ~150 ms. With the prefilter,
both the predicate and the subsequent Together call are skipped.

The headline case benefits most from Layer 1+3 because its multi-α
tower (Q(2^(1/3), Sqrt[α/6])) doesn't hit the Layer-0 nested-radical
gate but does benefit from the tighter inner gates.

## simp: multi-extension nested-radical denesting (2026-05-14)

Extended the Sqrt-of-Plus denester in `src/simp.c` to handle
phase-2 (multi-extension, Landau-style) radicands, closing a gap
where Mathematica simplified an expression in ~100 ms but Mathilda
left it untouched.  The motivating identity from the user report:

```
  Sqrt[16 - 2 Sqrt[29] + 2 Sqrt[55 - 10 Sqrt[29]]]
    -> Sqrt[5] + Sqrt[11 - 2 Sqrt[29]]
```

Previously only single-sqrt radicands `A + b Sqrt[C]` with `A` in
`Q` would denest; this commit lifts both constraints.

### Algorithm

The half-sum identity stays the same:

```
  P, Q = (A +/- Sqrt[A^2 - b^2 C]) / 2
  Sqrt[A + b Sqrt[C]] = Sqrt[P] + sgn(b) Sqrt[Q]
```

Phase 2 extends three pieces:

1. **Outer-sqrt selection (`split_plus_into_a_plus_b_sqrt_c`).**
   When a radicand has multiple sqrt-bearing terms, the splitter
   now ranks candidates by sqrt nesting depth (deeper outer first,
   tie-broken by leaf-count complexity).  `denest_compute_pq_s`
   iterates candidates until one yields a clean denesting.
   Phase-1 single-sqrt inputs hit candidate 0 once with
   byte-identical behaviour.
2. **Recursive discriminant (`sqrt_if_clean_square`).**  When
   `D = A^2 - b^2 C` is itself a Plus carrying a sqrt-bearing
   term, recursively denest `Sqrt[D]` and accept the result iff it
   leaves no `Sqrt[Plus]` residue.  Bounded by a file-static depth
   budget (default 4) and memoised on `D` to avoid revisiting
   subtrees across the bottom-up walker and the discriminant path.
3. **Q(Sqrt[k]) sign prover (`q_sqrt_extension_is_nonneg`).**  The
   branch-validity gate previously routed any non-literal `P` / `Q`
   through assumption-set reasoning, which couldn't decide
   `11 - 2 Sqrt[29] >= 0` (the second component of the motivating
   denesting).  Added an exact sign decider for `Q(Sqrt[k])`
   elements: collect `alpha`, `beta` from a Plus, compare
   `alpha^2` against `beta^2 gamma` over exact rationals.  No
   numeric sampling -- all arithmetic runs through the evaluator
   on rational literals.

### Files touched

- `src/simp.c`
  - New helpers: `sqrt_nesting_depth`,
    `plus_has_sqrt_bearing_term`, `contains_sqrt_of_plus`,
    `simp_denest_sqrt_recursive`, `count_outer_sqrt_candidates`,
    `is_numeric_rational`, `rational_sign`,
    `classify_q_sqrt_term`, `compute_discriminant_eval`,
    `q_sqrt_extension_is_nonneg`, `denest_memo_lookup` / `_insert`
    / `_clear`.
  - Refactored: `split_plus_into_a_plus_b_sqrt_c` accepts a
    `candidate_idx`; `denest_compute_pq_s` splits into outer
    iterator + `_at_candidate` per-attempt helper;
    `sqrt_if_clean_square` gains a phase-2 recursive case and
    reorders its polynomial-Plus path so a sqrt-bearing `D` falls
    through rather than aborting; `denest_is_nonneg` consults the
    new Q(Sqrt[k]) prover; the top-level `simp_denest_sqrt`
    entry manages the budget + memo lifetime with re-entry
    detection so an evaluator-driven sub-Simplify shares state.

### Tests

`tests/test_simp_denest_phase2.c` registered as
`simp_denest_phase2_tests`.  Nine cases, all passing:

- the user's exact reported expression collapsing to `0`;
- the radicand denesting alone;
- the inner phase-1 step
  (`Sqrt[152 - 24 Sqrt[29]] -> 2 Sqrt[29] - 6`) still firing
  under the single-extension path;
- three phase-1 sanity checks (`5+2 Sqrt[6]`, `7+4 Sqrt[3]`,
  `3+2 Sqrt[2]`);
- a non-denestable multi-sqrt input (`1 + Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3]`)
  staying untouched;
- a single-sqrt input with negative discriminant staying
  untouched;
- idempotency of the phase-2 result under a second `Simplify`.

The pre-existing `tests/test_simp_denest_inv_sqrt.c` (60+
phase-1 cases) continues to pass unchanged.

### Implementation notes

- Re-entry on `simp_denest_sqrt`: if `g_denest_budget` is
  already nonzero an in-flight denesting is sharing state with
  an evaluator-driven sub-Simplify, so we don't reset the budget
  or memo.  Depth cap is enforced end-to-end.
- `sqrt_if_clean_square`'s polynomial path used to `return NULL`
  immediately when its input contained a non-integer Power;
  phase-2 reorganises this as a guarded skip so a sqrt-bearing
  `D` falls through to the phase-2 recursive case rather than
  aborting before it can fire.
- Memo lifetime is tied to the top-level entry; nested
  invocations share the parent's memo, freed once on exit.
- Soundness invariant: phase-2 accepts a recursive result only
  when `contains_sqrt_of_plus` is false -- structural evidence
  that the inner denester unrolled every nested radical.  No
  numeric sampling in the soundness check.

## core: TimeConstrained (2026-05-14)

Added `TimeConstrained[expr, t]` and `TimeConstrained[expr, t, failexpr]`
to `src/core.c`, with `SYM_TimeConstrained` interned in `sym_names.c`,
attributes `HoldAll | Protected` in `attr.c`, and a docstring in
`info.c`. Documentation lives in `docs/spec/builtins/time-and-date.md`.

- The two-argument form evaluates `expr` and returns its value if it
  completes within `t` seconds of CPU time. On timeout the call returns
  the symbol `$Aborted`. The three-argument form evaluates `failexpr`
  instead on abort; `failexpr` is held until the timeout fires.
  `TimeConstrained[expr, Infinity]` (or `DirectedInfinity[1]`) imposes
  no constraint.
- Implementation uses `ITIMER_PROF` + `SIGPROF` so that the kernel
  charges only this process's user+kernel CPU time toward the budget
  ("CPU time spent inside the main Mathilda kernel process"). The
  intrischnorman pmint timeout (wall-clock, `SIGALRM` / `ITIMER_REAL`)
  and the test-harness `alarm(60)` therefore remain operational.
- The previous `SIGPROF` handler and `ITIMER_PROF` state are saved on
  entry and restored on exit so nested `TimeConstrained` calls compose
  and any external profiler in the address space is left untouched.
- Abort path: a one-shot `sigsetjmp` / `siglongjmp` unwinds the
  in-flight evaluator. To repair the recursion-depth counter that
  `evaluate()` did not get a chance to decrement, a new
  `eval_reset_recursion_depth(int)` helper was added to `eval.c` /
  `eval.h`; it also clears the sticky `eval_overflow` flag so a future
  evaluation is not falsely poisoned. Memory allocated by the aborted
  computation is intentionally leaked, matching the Mathematica note
  that `TimeConstrained` may produce different results on different
  occasions.
- Time-budget parsing accepts `EXPR_INTEGER`, `EXPR_REAL`, `EXPR_BIGINT`,
  `Rational[p, q]`, the symbol `Infinity`, and `DirectedInfinity[+]`.
  Non-positive or NaN budgets abort immediately without entering the
  evaluator; sub-microsecond positive budgets are rounded up to 1 us so
  that `setitimer(0, 0)` (which would disarm rather than arm the timer)
  never occurs.
- Tests live in `tests/test_time_constrained.c` and cover the
  fast-completion path (2-arg and 3-arg), the `Infinity` short-circuit,
  zero / negative / non-numeric time inputs, bad arity, `Rational`
  budgets, the time-argument-is-evaluated guarantee, `failexpr` not
  being evaluated on success, the body being evaluated exactly once
  (`HoldAll`), the timer-driven abort (`$Aborted` and `failexpr`
  branches), nested `TimeConstrained` (inner abort + outer success),
  recovery of evaluator state after an abort, and the `Protected`
  attribute / `Attributes[TimeConstrained]` readback. CPU-burn cases
  accept either the aborted result or the (unlikely) completed result
  to stay portable across very fast hardware.

## core: TimeConstrained cooperative wall-clock backstop (2026-05-14)

Made `TimeConstrained` portable to hosts whose `ITIMER_PROF` is
unreliable -- in particular WSL 1, whose syscall-translation layer
under-counts CPU time and delivers `SIGPROF` many seconds late (a 1 s
budget there was observed to abort only after ~15 s).

- Added a second enforcement layer alongside the existing
  `ITIMER_PROF` / `SIGPROF` signal path: `builtin_time_constrained`
  now captures `clock_gettime(CLOCK_MONOTONIC) + budget` as a
  wall-clock deadline when it arms the timer, and `evaluate()`'s
  fixed-point loop calls a new `tc_check_deadline()` function once
  per rewrite step. On hosts where `ITIMER_PROF` works, the signal
  wins (sub-millisecond, CPU-time semantic preserved) and the check
  is a cheap inactive read. On hosts where it doesn't, the
  cooperative check trips at the next rewrite step and
  `siglongjmp`s exactly as the signal handler would, so the abort
  path (recursion-depth reset, `$Aborted` / `failexpr` selection,
  timer / handler restore) is shared and unchanged.
- The deadline state (`tc_deadline`, `tc_deadline_active`) is saved
  and restored around `sigsetjmp` so nested `TimeConstrained` calls
  compose: the outer-call deadline resumes correctly when the inner
  one returns.
- `CLOCK_MONOTONIC` is POSIX.1-2001 and supported on every host the
  project targets (glibc Linux, macOS 10.12+, WSL 1/2). A
  `clock_gettime` failure is treated as "no time elapsed" so the
  cooperative path can only ever cause spurious *non*-aborts, never
  spurious aborts; the signal path remains the fallback in that
  unreachable case.
- The header declaration of `tc_check_deadline` is in `src/core.h`;
  the call site is in the top of the `while` loop in `evaluate()`
  in `src/eval.c`. The new state and function definition live in
  `src/core.c` next to `tc_sigprof_handler`.
- Granularity caveat (unchanged): a single long-running C builtin
  (e.g. `FactorInteger` on a huge composite) cannot be aborted
  cooperatively, since the check fires only between evaluator
  rewrite steps. On WSL 1, those calls still wait for the late
  `SIGPROF`; on real Linux / macOS, the signal interrupts the
  builtin promptly.
- A new test `test_tc_cooperative_backstop_without_sigprof`
  simulates the WSL 1 scenario by blocking `SIGPROF` for the
  duration of the call (and pre-installing `SIG_IGN` as the saved
  disposition so any pending timer signal is harmlessly discarded
  on unblock). The test asserts that `TimeConstrained[Do[1 + 1, {i,
  1, 10000000}], 0.2]` still returns `$Aborted`, proving the
  cooperative path enforces the deadline on its own.

## file I/O: Put, PutAppend, and `>>` / `>>>` parser syntax (2026-05-14)

Added `Put` and `PutAppend` builtins and renamed the module that hosts
them. Documentation lives in `docs/spec/builtins/file-io.md`; the
docstrings are in `info.c`.

- New module `src/readwrite.c` (with `src/readwrite.h`) replaces the
  one-function `src/load.c`. `Get` moved over unchanged; `load_init`
  was renamed to `readwrite_init` and is registered from `core_init`
  in the same slot. `tests/CMakeLists.txt` was updated to reflect the
  new source path.
- `Put[expr_1, ..., expr_n, "file"]` truncates `"file"` and writes each
  argument's standard-form text followed by `\n`. The single-arg form
  `Put["file"]` creates an empty file (handy for "touch"-style use).
- `PutAppend[...]` uses the same logic in `"a"` (append) mode so that
  prior contents are preserved. Both builtins share a `put_common`
  helper inside `readwrite.c` to keep the I/O and diagnostic paths in
  one place.
- Parser support in `src/parse.c`:
  - `>>>` is matched before `>>`, which in turn is matched before `>`,
    so the tokeniser doesn't lose either of the existing `>`/`>=`
    operators. Both new tokens share precedence `30` — below `=` /
    `:=` (`40`) and above `;` (`10`).
  - The right-hand side is parsed specially: if the next character is
    `"` the parser reads a quoted string, otherwise it scans a
    bare-word filename that may contain identifier characters plus
    `.`, `/`, `\`, `-`, `_`, `~`, `$`. The result is wrapped in a
    string literal so the AST always carries `Put[expr, "name"]` /
    `PutAppend[expr, "name"]`.
- `SYM_Put` and `SYM_PutAppend` were added to `src/sym_names.{c,h}` for
  symmetry with the other registered builtins, even though no current
  hot path compares against them.
- Tests live in `tests/test_readwrite.c` and exercise both the parser
  desugaring (quoted and bare filenames, precedence vs `+` and `;`,
  ordering of `>`/`>>`/`>>>`) and the file generation paths
  (truncation, multi-expression writes, empty-file creation, append
  semantics, Get round-trip, and the `Protected` attribute).

## core: Symbol builtin (2026-05-13)

Added the `Symbol[]` builtin to `src/core.c`. `SYM_Symbol` is already
interned in `sym_names.c` (it backs the `x_Symbol` pattern head), so no
new symbol pointer was required; only registration and a docstring.

- `Symbol["name"]` returns the symbol whose name is `"name"`. The string
  is validated against the standard Mathematica symbol-name syntax —
  each segment between backticks must start with a letter or `$`,
  followed by letters, digits, or `$` — and then routed through
  `context_resolve_name` so that a bare name picks up `$Context`, a
  leading backtick is treated as relative to `$Context`, and an
  embedded backtick (`"a`x"`) is treated as an absolutely-qualified
  name (with `"System`X"` canonicalised to bare `X`, matching the
  parser). The result is an `EXPR_SYMBOL` whose `Head` is `Symbol`, so
  it composes correctly with `x_Symbol` patterns, `Head[]`, and
  ordinary OwnValue / DownValue lookups.
- Invalid names print `Symbol::symname` on `stderr` and leave the
  call unevaluated, matching Mathematica's diagnostic. Non-string
  arguments and any arity other than 1 also leave the call
  unevaluated. Attribute: `Protected`.

Docstring lives in `info.c`. Tests live in `tests/test_symbol.c` and
cover bare construction, `Head[Symbol["x"]] == Symbol`, the
`x_Symbol` pattern example from the Mathematica docs, absolute and
relative context handling, evaluation of bound symbols, the
`Symbol::symname` error path (digit-start, empty, punctuation),
non-string and wrong-arity argument handling, names containing `$`
and digits, and the `Protected` attribute assignment.

## core: ToString and ToExpression (2026-05-13)

Added `ToString` and `ToExpression` builtins to `src/core.c`, with the
canonical symbol pointers `SYM_ToString` / `SYM_ToExpression` interned in
`sym_names.c` and docstrings in `info.c`.

- `ToString[expr]` / `ToString[expr, form]` returns a `String`
  containing the printed form of `expr`. Supported forms are
  `InputForm` (default), `FullForm`, and `TeXForm`; `StandardForm` and
  `OutputForm` are accepted as aliases for `InputForm`. Implementation
  delegates to the existing `expr_to_string` / `expr_to_string_fullform`
  helpers; `TeXForm` is realised by constructing a temporary
  `TeXForm[expr]` wrapper and feeding it back through `expr_to_string`,
  which already dispatches the `TeXForm` head to the TeX renderer.
  Unrecognised forms return `NULL` so the call stays visible to the
  caller as `ToString[expr, FooForm]` rather than being silently
  downgraded. Attribute: `Protected`.
- `ToExpression[input]` parses `input` (a string) and returns the
  resulting expression. `ToExpression[input, form]` accepts
  `InputForm` / `FullForm` / `StandardForm` (all currently route through
  the same parser). `ToExpression[input, form, h]` wraps the parsed
  expression in `h[...]` before returning, allowing `h = Hold` to
  prevent further evaluation. Parse failures yield the symbol
  `$Failed`, matching Mathematica. Non-string `input` or an
  unrecognised `form` leaves the call unevaluated. Attributes:
  `Listable`, `Protected`. `Listable` threads over `List` inputs so
  that `ToExpression[{"1+1", "2+2"}]` evaluates to `{2, 4}`.

Tests live in `tests/test_tostring_toexpression.c` and cover the
default form, each named form, the round-trip
`ToExpression[ToString[expr]]`, parse-failure / non-string handling,
the `Hold` wrapping case, `Listable` threading, and unsupported-form
fall-through. Valgrind shows no new leak paths attributed to either
builtin.

## integrate: Listable attribute (2026-05-13)

Added `ATTR_LISTABLE` to `Integrate` in `integrate_init` so that
`Integrate[{f1, f2, ...}, x]` threads element-wise into
`{Integrate[f1, x], Integrate[f2, x], ...}` before dispatch, matching
Mathematica's behaviour.  Previously the rational dispatcher fed the
raw `List[...]` into `PolynomialQ` / `BronsteinRational` and produced
a malformed matrix-shaped output (e.g. `Integrate[{1, x, x^5/5}, x]`
returned a 3x3 nested list of garbage).

## datetime: AbsoluteTime[] (2026-05-13)

Added `AbsoluteTime` to `src/datetime.c`, with attribute `Protected` and
a docstring in `info.c`.

- `AbsoluteTime[]` returns the current wall-clock seconds since
  1900-01-01 (local time), via `time(NULL)` + `localtime`.  No
  corrections are made for time zones, DST, or leap seconds, per the
  Mathematica spec.
- `AbsoluteTime[{y, m, d, h, m, s}]` converts a `DateList`-style
  specification; trailing entries are elided to `{_, 1, 1, 0, 0, 0}`.
  Year and month must be integer; day, hour, minute, and second may be
  noninteger.
- `AbsoluteTime[number]` passes through numeric inputs (already an
  `AbsoluteTime` specification).
- Out-of-range date components normalize implicitly through the
  Fliegel & Van Flandern Julian-day-number formula, e.g.
  `AbsoluteTime[{2022, 2, 31}] = AbsoluteTime[{2022, 3, 3}]
  = 3855254400`.
- Returns an exact integer when every component is integer-valued and
  the resulting total is representable; otherwise returns a real.
- Tests in `tests/test_datetime.c` cover the integer reference values
  (`{2022,1,1,0,0,0}`, `{2022,1}`, `{2022}`), the Feb-31 -> Mar-3
  normalization, fractional day and fractional hour components, the
  numeric pass-through, the current-time sanity range, and the
  `Protected` attribute.

## simp: half-int powers, Algebraic short-circuit, nested-radical scoring (2026-05-13)

Three related improvements that together close the user-reported
follow-ups to the inv-sqrt denester landed earlier the same day:

1. **Sqrt[X]^k denesting for any odd k.** Previously
   `simp_denest_sqrt_walk` only fired on `Power[X, ±1/2]`, so the
   cubed-reciprocal form `1/Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]]^3` (which the evaluator
   canonicalises to `Power[5+2 Sqrt[6], -3/2]`) walked past untouched.
   `Simplify[1/(5+2 Sqrt[6])^(3/2) + (Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3])^3]` returned
   the input unchanged.

   The dispatch is now a single matcher `match_half_int_power(e, &m,
   &base)` that recognises `Power[base, m/2]` for any odd integer m,
   and a unified builder `try_denest_pow_half_int(plus_node, m, ctx)`
   that handles all four cases:
   - `m == 1`:  `Sqrt[P] + sign*Sqrt[Q]` (forward)
   - `m == -1`: `(Sqrt[P] - sign*Sqrt[Q]) / s` (reciprocal, rationalised)
   - `m > 1`:   `(Sqrt[P] + sign*Sqrt[Q])^m`
   - `m < -1`:  `(Sqrt[P] - sign*Sqrt[Q])^|m| / s^|m|`

   The three now-unused helpers from the earlier landing
   (`try_denest_sqrt_radicand`, `try_denest_recip_sqrt_radicand`,
   `is_inv_sqrt`) were removed. The shared `denest_compute_pq_s`
   helper survives unchanged; both old paths are now special cases
   of the new general builder.

2. **`Algebraic` early denester short-circuit.** Profiling the
   working case `Simplify[Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3] + 1/Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]]]`
   showed 99% of all traced transform time (180 of 181 ms) inside the
   `simp_algebraic_impl` Together-with-Extension n=1 path, which
   computed a 212 ms `Together[expr, Extension -> α]` for nested-
   radical inputs only to reject it via the trailing complexity gate.

   Added an O(small) `simp_denest_sqrt` precheck at the top of
   `simp_algebraic_impl`: when the denester strictly wins on
   complexity, return that denesting and skip the qaupoly tower
   construction entirely. The work the gate would have rejected
   anyway never runs. Wall-clock for the headline case dropped
   from 560 ms to 370 ms per Simplify call (35% reduction). The
   remaining ~350 ms is the simp_search round-loop framework
   itself, not any traced transform.

3. **Nested-radical scoring penalty.** Cube-root denesting cases
   like `Simplify[(2+Sqrt[5])^(1/3)]` were producing the right
   denested form `(1+Sqrt[5])/2` inside `simp_cuberoot` but the
   simp_search complexity gate rejected it: the denested LeafCount
   (13) exceeded the nested input's (11) and `update_best` uses
   strict `<`.

   Added `nested_radical_penalty(e)`: a +3 surcharge for each
   `Power[Compound, Rational[_, q]]` subtree (q ≥ 2) whose compound
   base itself contains another root. The penalty fires only on
   *truly* nested radicals — flat radicals like `Sqrt[5]` or
   `Sqrt[x+y]` are unaffected — so it doesn't disturb cases where
   the nested form is the canonical answer.

   The surcharge is applied inside `score_with_func`, so it affects
   every simp_search comparison (`update_best`, candidate pruning)
   without touching the per-transform internal gates that still use
   `simp_default_complexity` directly. With it, cube-root denesting
   now succeeds for cases the grid-search produces but were
   previously rejected: `(2+Sqrt[5])^(1/3) -> (1+Sqrt[5])/2`,
   `1/(2+Sqrt[5])^(1/3) -> 2/(1+Sqrt[5])`, and `Simplify` on
   `1/Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]]` standalone now returns the denested
   `Sqrt[3] - Sqrt[2]` instead of leaving the nested form alone.

**Test coverage:**
- 7 new tests in `tests/test_simp_denest_inv_sqrt.c` Block J cover
  the half-int power generalisation (m = ±3, ±5; forward & recip;
  negative b; non-unit s).
- 6 new tests in `tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c` cover the
  cube-root cases that now denest correctly under the penalty
  (Pattern A with rational p,q; Pattern B sum-of-conjugates;
  reciprocal form; and an inert no-denest control case).
- Full regression suite (~80 test binaries) passes unchanged.

## simp: reciprocal nested-radical denesting (2026-05-13)

Closes the user-reported identity
`Simplify[Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3] + 1/Sqrt[5 + 2 Sqrt[6]]] -> 0`
and its multi-extension cousins
(e.g. `1/Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]] + 1/Sqrt[5-2 Sqrt[6]] -> 2 Sqrt[3]`).

**The gap:** `simp_denest_sqrt_walk` (the half-sum nested-radical
denester) only matched `Power[X, 1/2]`. The reciprocal form
`Power[X, -1/2]` (i.e. `1/Sqrt[X]`) walked past untouched, so any
expression where the cancellation required `1/Sqrt[a + b Sqrt[c]]` to
be rewritten as the conjugate-rationalised `(Sqrt[P] -/+ Sqrt[Q])/s`
failed to reach zero — the downstream `qa_substrate_general_pq` pass
never saw the linear-basis form it needed.

**The fix:**

1. Extracted a shared helper `denest_compute_pq_s(plus_node, ctx,
   &P, &Q, &s, &b_is_negative)` from `try_denest_sqrt_radicand`. On
   success this returns the half-sum data
       `(A + b Sqrt[C]) = (Sqrt[P] + sign * Sqrt[Q])^2`,
       `s = P - Q = Sqrt[A^2 - b^2 C]`.
   Both the forward and reciprocal paths reuse it, so the branch-
   soundness prover (`denest_is_nonneg`), the `D = A^2 - b^2 C`
   polynomial scaffolding, and the `Sqrt[m/n]` rationaliser all live
   in one place.

   Required fixing a latent dangling-pointer hazard in the original
   forward code path: `s` was consumed when constructing `Times[-1, s]`
   to build `Q = (A - s)/2`, then leaked afterwards. The new shared
   helper has to *return* `s`, so the consume site now takes a copy.

2. Added `is_inv_sqrt(e)` — true on `Power[X, Rational[-1, 2]]` — and a
   new builder `try_denest_recip_sqrt_radicand` that emits
       `(Sqrt[P] -/+ Sqrt[Q]) / s`
   using the conjugate-rationalisation identities
       `1 / (Sqrt[P] + Sqrt[Q]) = (Sqrt[P] - Sqrt[Q]) / (P - Q)`
       `1 / (Sqrt[P] - Sqrt[Q]) = (Sqrt[P] + Sqrt[Q]) / (P - Q)`.
   The sign in front of `Sqrt[Q]` flips relative to the forward path.

3. Extended `simp_denest_sqrt_walk` to dispatch on
       `is_sqrt(target) || (inv = is_inv_sqrt(target))`
   and route to the appropriate builder. Bottom-up traversal,
   branch-soundness checks, and idempotency all carry over unchanged
   from the forward path.

**Behavioural coverage:**

| Input | Output |
|-------|--------|
| `Simplify[Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3] + 1/Sqrt[5 + 2 Sqrt[6]]]` | `0` |
| `Simplify[1/Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]] + 1/Sqrt[5-2 Sqrt[6]]]` | `2 Sqrt[3]` |
| `Simplify[Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]] - 1/Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]]]` | `2 Sqrt[2]` |
| `Simplify[1/Sqrt[3 + 2 Sqrt[2]]]` | `-1 + Sqrt[2]` |
| `Simplify[1/Sqrt[5 - 2 Sqrt[6]]]` | `Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3]` |
| `Simplify[1/Sqrt[2 + Sqrt[3]]]` | `(Sqrt[6] - Sqrt[2])/2` |
| `Simplify[1/Sqrt[1 + Sqrt[2]]]` | unchanged (negative discriminant) |
| `Simplify[1/Sqrt[x + Sqrt[y]]]` | unchanged (branch unverifiable) |

Standalone cases where the rationalised form does not strictly reduce
`LeafCount` (e.g. `1/Sqrt[5+2 Sqrt[6]]` alone, where both sides count
13 leaves) are added to the candidate seed set but Simplify's measure
keeps the input. Cross-term cancellation still works in these cases
because the seed reaches downstream rounds via `cs_add_or_free`.

**Tests:** `tests/test_simp_denest_inv_sqrt.c` — 32 cases across 9
blocks: user-report cancellation, standalone wins, non-denestable
guards, idempotency, large-discriminant stress, multi-extension
`Q(sqrt(2),sqrt(3))` chains, walker placement, coefficient
combinations, paranoia.

## simp: top-level algebraic-rational fast path + cancel_with_extension defensive bail (2026-05-13)

Closes two issues on the motivating example
`Simplify[D[Integrate[a x/(x^3+2), x], x]]`:

1. **Wrong-answer ComplexInfinity** — `cancel_with_extension` (rat.c) ran
   `PolynomialGCD[num, den, Extension -> α]` over Q(α)[x], but when the
   input carried opaque non-α algebraic factors (Sqrt[3], nested
   Sqrt[radicand-with-α-inside], ...) with hidden relations to α the
   substrate doesn't see, the subsequent
   `PolynomialQuotient[den, g, var, Extension -> α]` could collapse to
   literal 0, baking `Power[0, -1] = ComplexInfinity` into the result.
   E.g. `Simplify[term1 + term3]` of the headline expression silently
   returned ComplexInfinity.

   Fix: detect the literal-zero quotient before the
   `Power[new_den, -1]` build and return NULL so the caller falls back
   to the un-cancelled `combined` form (Together's pre-cancel output).
   Correct-but-unsimplified, which is the contract for
   `cancel_with_extension`.

2. **Failure to converge** — even after (1) the full
   `Simplify[D[Integrate[a x/(x^3+2), x], x]]` hung. simp_bottomup's
   per-subnode descent never combines the 3-fraction sum into a single
   common-denominator form because `simp_pipeline_rational`'s
   has_non_integer_power gate refuses to factor radical-bearing inputs.

   Fix: at the top of `builtin_simplify` (after the SHAPE_RATIONAL fast
   path), when the input is a `Plus` over a multi-generator algebraic
   tower (`n ≥ 2` from `extension_autodetect`) and free of explicit
   complex literals, run `Together[expr, Extension -> Automatic]` as a
   pre-pass.  builtin_together's Phase F multi-gen single-α fallback
   collapses the 3-fraction sum back to `(a x)/(2 + x^3)`.  Strict
   leaf-count gate so the pre-pass never regresses inputs where Together
   is a no-op or worse.

Tests: `tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c::test_simplify_headline_d_integrate`.

## qa: canonicalise Q(γ)-constants to linear-basis form (2026-05-13)

`qa_cancel_with_tower`'s no-variable branch (the path that lifts a
Q(γ)-element to a QANum via `qa_div` and renders it back as
`gamma_render` substituted into the γ-polynomial) previously stopped at
plain `evaluate` of the substituted form. For γ a sum of atomic
radicals (e.g. γ = Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3]), the surface form was an
unsimplified γ-polynomial:

```
Together[1/(Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3]) + 1/(Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3]),
         Extension -> Automatic]
   →   -(Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3])^3 + 9 (Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3])     (before)
   →   -2 Sqrt[2]                                          (now)
```

### Fix

After substituting γ_internal → `gamma_render`, run two extra passes
before the leaf-count gate:

1. **Expand** — collapses `(Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3])^k` into the linear basis
   `c_0 + c_1 Sqrt[2] + c_2 Sqrt[3] + c_3 Sqrt[6]`.
2. **Together (no extension)** — folds radical denominators (e.g.
   `c/Sqrt[6] + c' Sqrt[6]`) via Sqrt-base polynomial GCD. This also
   catches arithmetically-zero spurious forms that Expand alone leaves
   in `c/Sqrt[6] + c'·Sqrt[6]` shape (a side-effect of the qa_div lift
   not fully killing the algebraic relation between independent
   autodetect generators).

The existing leaf-count gate rejects the candidate when the canonical
form is larger than the input.

### User-visible wins

- `Together[1/(Sqrt[2]+Sqrt[3]) ± 1/(Sqrt[2]-Sqrt[3]), Extension -> Automatic]`
  → `-2 Sqrt[2]` / `2 Sqrt[3]`.
- `Cancel[(Sqrt[2]+Sqrt[3])^2 - 5 - 2 Sqrt[6], Extension -> Automatic]`
  → `0`.
- `Cancel[1/(Sqrt[2]+Sqrt[3]), Extension -> Automatic]`
  → `Sqrt[3] - Sqrt[2]` (rationalised).
- `Cancel[(Sqrt[2]+Sqrt[3])/(Sqrt[2]-Sqrt[3]), Extension -> Automatic]`
  → `-5 - 2 Sqrt[6]`.
- `Together[(Sqrt[2]-Sqrt[3])^2 + (Sqrt[2]+Sqrt[3])^2, Extension -> Automatic]`
  → `10`.

Tests:
`tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c::test_together_qgamma_constant_canonical_linear_basis`.

Suite: 96 PASS / 14 FAIL — identical pre-existing failure set.

## qa: multi-gen tower fallback to single-α Together/Cancel (2026-05-13)

Closes the motivating headline case
`Together[D[Integrate[a x/(x^3 + 2), x], x], Extension -> Automatic]`,
which previously bailed to the generic no-extension path and returned a
combined-but-not-cancelled fraction in `2^(1/3)` and `2^(2/3)`.

### Problem

When `extension_autodetect` builds a tower with `n ≥ 2` generators,
`builtin_together` and `builtin_cancel` route through
`qa_cancel_with_tower`. Step 1 of that path substitutes each user-side
α_i with its γ-polynomial form; on deep multi-fraction inputs this blows
the leaf count past the safety gate (`lc_out > 100 && lc_out > 2 lc_in`,
or `lc_out > 200`). The function returns NULL and the caller drops to
the generic no-extension `together_recursive`, which cannot see the
algebraic relations between generators and produces a non-cancelled
output.

### Fix

In both `builtin_together` and `builtin_cancel` (`src/rat.c`), when the
tower path declines, try each tower generator in turn as a *single-α*
extension via `together_recursive_ext` / `cancel_with_extension` before
falling back to the generic path. Run a final no-extension `Together`
fold-up on each candidate to combine like-coefficient terms that the
single-α path treats as polynomial-variable coefficients. Pick the
smallest result by `leaf_count_internal` that strictly beats the input.

The single-α path treats the remaining generators as opaque polynomial-
variable coefficients but still cancels correctly over Q(α)[x]; the
final no-extension `Together` then combines like terms (e.g. it pulls
`1/a` out of `1/(144 a) + x^3/(288 a)` to give `(2 + x^3)/(288 a)`).

### Verification

- `Together[D[Integrate[a x/(x^3 + 2), x], x], Extension -> Automatic]`
  collapses to `(a x)/(2 + x^3)` (LeafCount 7), down from the previous
  partial result of LeafCount ~30. Test:
  `tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c::test_together_headline_d_integrate`.
- `Cancel` form returns the same canonical result.
- Full suite: 96 PASS / 14 FAIL — identical pre-existing failure set
  (no regressions).

## algebraic: autodetect harvests absorbed nested radicals + tower-blowup safety gate (2026-05-13)

Two coordinated `qafactor.c` fixes that keep the algebraic-extension
pipeline running cleanly when the Power canonicaliser (2026-05-12 +
2026-05-13 Power-factor patch) absorbs a nested radical into existing
integer-base generators.

### Autodetect: handle absorbed nested generators

`autodetect_canonicalise_post` previously rebuilt every GEN_NESTED
generator's render via `autodetect_canonicalise_radicand`. When the
canonical form is no longer a single atomic radical -- e.g.
`Sqrt[-1/9/2^(2/3) + 2/9·2^(1/3)]` canonicalises to `Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)]`
which the Power canonicaliser then reduces to `1/(2^(1/3) Sqrt[3])`,
a Times of inverse powers -- the borrowed render was non-atomic and
`qa_resolve_extension` couldn't build a tower from it.
`extension_autodetect` returned NULL, costing every downstream caller
(Together / Cancel with `Extension -> Automatic`) the chance to use
algebraic-extension reasoning.

New helper `autodetect_is_atomic_radical_surface(e)` detects the
absorbed case. A new enum value `GEN_ABSORBED` marks affected
entries. When canonicalisation produces a non-atomic surface, the
post-canon pass:

1. Re-walks the simplified surface with `autodetect_walk` to harvest
   any newly-exposed integer-base components (deduping into existing
   `GEN_INT_BASE` entries via `autodetect_add_int`).
2. Marks the original entry as `GEN_ABSORBED`.
3. Step 2's dedup-and-compact sweep drops `GEN_ABSORBED` entries
   along with structurally-duplicate nested entries.

Result: `extension_autodetect` now produces a tower spanning just the
integer-base generators when the nested radical is absorbed, and
`Together` / `Cancel` route through the algebraic-extension code
path where they previously fell back to the non-extension default.

### Safety gate: Step 1 substitution blowup

`qa_cancel_with_tower`'s Step 1 substitution replaces each user-α
render with its polynomial-in-γ form. For deep multi-fraction inputs
(e.g. the unintegrated Risch result for `Integrate[a x/(x^3+2), x]`)
each `Power[c, p/q]` occurrence expands to a degree-up-to-deg(γ)
polynomial, and the post-Step-1 leaf count can be 3-10× the input.
Step 2's downstream `Together` (no-extension) then runs multivariate
polynomial GCD over `Q[γ_internal, x, ...]` on the inflated form,
which is intractable.

New gate after Step 1: if the substituted leaf count exceeds 100
**and** more than doubles the original, return NULL so the caller
falls back to the non-tower path (which gives the partial
combined-but-not-cancelled result that the user already had before
the autodetect harvest fix unlocked this path). Empirically tuned to
let the small `Sqrt[A] - Sqrt[B] → 0` and `(Sqrt[2]+Sqrt[3])(Sqrt[2]-
Sqrt[3]) → -1` cases through while bailing on the deep
`Together[D[Integrate[a x/(x^3+2), x], x], Extension -> Automatic]`
input.

The blow-up case is the right next layer of work: a multi-generator
analogue of `together_recursive_ext` that threads the tower's
polynomial relations through `PolynomialLCM` / `PolynomialQuotient`
without pre-expanding to γ-polynomial form. Deferred; tracked in
`tasks/qa_substrate_general_pq.md`.

### Tests

`tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c::test_autodetect_absorbs_canonical_radical`:
`Cancel[(Sqrt[-1/9/2^(2/3) + 2/9 2^(1/3)]) Sqrt[3] 2^(1/3) - 1,
Extension -> Automatic] → 0`. Without the autodetect fix, autodetect
returned NULL and the Cancel left the input unevaluated.

Full suite 96 pass / 14 fail -- identical pre-existing failure set.
Zero new regressions.

## power: Power[Times[positives], p/q] admits Power factors that compose cleanly (2026-05-13)

The `Power[Times[positive_factors], p/q]` distribution rule
(`src/power.c`, 2026-05-12) gated distribution on at least one factor
being an integer or rational that **fully reduces** under `Power[_, p/q]`
(`factor_fully_reduces_under_q` -- residue 1 on both numerator and
denominator). This left examples like `Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)]` and
`Sqrt[3/2^(2/3)]` unevaluated even though the `Power[2, -2/3]` factor
*would* compose cleanly under the outer `Sqrt[_]` -- the issue was
that no factor was a perfect square.

New companion predicate `power_factor_composes_cleanly(f, p_out, q_out)`
admits a `Power[positive_base, p'/q']` factor as a distribution
trigger when composing the outer exponent `p_out/q_out` with the
inner `p'/q'` introduces **no new radical complexity**: composed
reduced denominator `<= q'`. The arithmetic reduces to a single
divisibility check: `q_out | |p' * p_out|`.

Examples now reduced:

```
Sqrt[3/2^(2/3)]       ->  Sqrt[3] / 2^(1/3)
Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)]     ->  1 / (2^(1/3) Sqrt[3])
Sqrt[Pi/2^(2/3)]      ->  Sqrt[Pi] / 2^(1/3)
```

Mathematica-faithful adjacency cases stay untouched (the divisibility
check rejects them):

```
Sqrt[2 Sqrt[3]]       ->  Sqrt[2 Sqrt[3]]    (q_out=2 does not divide 1)
Sqrt[2 Pi]            ->  Sqrt[2 Pi]         (no Power factor present)
(4 Pi)^(2/3)          ->  (4 Pi)^(2/3)       (4 has no cube factor)
```

Tests: `tests/test_power_corpus.c::test_power_of_times_power_factor_composes`.

### Knock-on effect: algebraic-extension headline

This patch is the substrate fix for the deeper Together motivating
example. With nested `Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)]` now simplifying,
`Together[D[Integrate[a x/(x^3+2), x], x], Extension -> Automatic]`
produces a clean rational expression in `x` and `2^(1/3)/2^(2/3)`
(no nested Sqrts) instead of an opaque form. Full collapse to
`a x / (x^3 + 2)` is gated on a downstream polynomial-GCD-over-Q(γ)
step which is not yet wired into Together's cancel path. Tracked as
a remaining limitation in `tasks/qa_substrate_general_pq.md`.

### Regression risk

Full test suite 96 pass / 14 fail -- identical pre-existing failure
set. Zero new regressions.

## power: rational-base and rational-exponent canonicalisation (2026-05-12)

`Power` (`src/power.c`) now reduces fractional powers of rational
bases that previously stayed unevaluated, and composes Powers of
positive bases under non-integer outer exponents. The motivating
failures were:

```
In[1]:= (1/54)^(2/3)
Out[1]= (1/54)^(2/3)         (* expected: 1/(9 * 2^(2/3)) *)

In[2]:= Sqrt[(1/54)^(2/3)]
Out[2]= Sqrt[(1/54)^(2/3)]   (* expected: 1/(3 * 2^(1/3))   *)
```

Three coordinated additions to `builtin_power`:

1. **Rational-base + rational-exponent distribution.** For
   `Power[Rational[n, d], p/q]` with `q > 1`, distribute as
   `Power[n, p/q] * Power[d, -p/q]` and recurse. Each piece routes
   through the existing integer-base + rational-exponent path which
   extracts the q-th-power coefficient and leaves a residue
   `Power[r, b/q]`. Triggering is gated on at least one piece
   simplifying: `|n| == 1`, or `factor_out_kth_power(|n|, q)` /
   `factor_out_kth_power(d, q)` extracts a factor > 1. This keeps
   `Sqrt[2/3]` and `(4/9)^(2/3)` unevaluated (Mathematica-faithful)
   while reducing `(1/54)^(2/3)`, `(8/27)^(2/3) -> 4/9`,
   `Sqrt[4/9] -> 2/3`, `Sqrt[1/4] -> 1/2`, and
   `(-1/8)^(1/3) -> (-1)^(1/3)/2`.

2. **`Power[Times[positive_factors], p/q]` distribution.** Distributes
   the outer Power when every factor is known positive and at least
   one factor cleanly reduces to a rational coefficient under
   `Power[_, p/q]` (factor_out residue == 1 on both numerator and
   denominator). Examples: `Sqrt[4 Pi] -> 2 Sqrt[Pi]`,
   `(Pi/8)^(2/3) -> Pi^(2/3)/4`, and -- crucially for chaining --
   `Sqrt[(1/9) * 2^(-2/3)] -> (1/3) * 2^(-1/3)`. Stays conservative
   for `(4 Pi)^(2/3)` (no clean cube extraction) and
   `Sqrt[2 Sqrt[3]]` (the Power factor cannot fully reduce).

3. **Power-of-Power composition for positive base + rational outer.**
   Generalises the existing integer-outer-exponent rule to
   `Power[Power[B, E_inner], p/q] -> Power[B, E_inner * p/q]` when
   `B` is known positive. Fixes `Sqrt[2^a] -> 2^(a/2)` and
   `Sqrt[Pi^2] -> Pi`; carefully leaves `Sqrt[x^4]` unevaluated since
   `x` has unknown sign. This is what reduces the inner
   `Power[Power[2, -2/3], 1/2]` to `Power[2, -1/3]` during evaluation
   of `Sqrt[(1/54)^(2/3)]`.

The cascade for the user's case:

```
Sqrt[(1/54)^(2/3)]
  -> Sqrt[(1/9) * 2^(-2/3)]                  (rational-base distribution)
  -> Sqrt[1/9] * Sqrt[Power[2, -2/3]]        (Times-of-positives distribution)
  -> (1/3) * Power[2, -1/3]                  (rational-base + Power-of-Power)
```

Soundness: every distribution is gated on positive sub-bases or on
integer outer exponents, so no principal branch cut is crossed.

## simp: trig-rational fast path for large derivative-of-Risch-Norman inputs (2026-05-12)

`Simplify` now ships a polynomial-time algebraic normal-form
pre-check (`src/trigrat.c`, `simp_trig_rational`) that handles
rational functions of trigonometric and hyperbolic functions
without entering the heuristic round-loop. It runs from
`builtin_simplify` (`src/simp.c`) before `simp_bottomup` and is also
hooked into `simp_dispatch` for the `SIMP_SHAPE_TRIG` case, with a
strict leaf-count gate so it cannot regress any existing case.

### Motivation

Two concrete failures on the previous build (both hung
indefinitely):

- `Simplify[D[Integrate`RischNorman[Tan[x]^2 + Tan[x] + 1, x], x]]`
- `Simplify[D[Integrate`RischNorman[x^4 Sin[x] Cos[x], x], x]]`

These are derivatives of Risch-Norman integration outputs and
should simplify back to the original integrand (or an equivalent
compact form). `simp_search` was slow because its
`Together`/`Cancel`/`Factor`/`TrigFactor` pipeline treats every
`Log[trig(x)]` subtree as an algebraic generator, and the
resulting multivariate polynomial GCDs blow up.

### Algorithm

Pure rational-function reduction in the polynomial quotient ring

    K[ s_i, c_i, sigma_j, chi_j, other_vars ]
        / < s_i^2 + c_i^2 - 1,  chi_j^2 - sigma_j^2 - 1 >

for distinct trig arguments {a_i} and hyperbolic arguments {b_j}.

1. **Preprocess + substitute** (single top-down walk in
   `tr_walk_subst`). Walks transparently through `Plus`/`Times`/
   `Power[_, integer_exp]`/`Rational`/`Complex`. Rewrites
   `Tan`/`Cot`/`Sec`/`Csc`/`Tanh`/`Coth`/`Sech`/`Csch` to their
   `Sin`/`Cos` (or `Sinh`/`Cosh`) form using *non-evaluating*
   constructors (the evaluator otherwise canonicalises
   `Sin[x]/Cos[x] -> Tan[x]` and infinite-loops the preprocess).
   `Sin`/`Cos`/`Sinh`/`Cosh` with a single arg get a fresh `(s, c)`
   or `(sigma, chi)` generator. Every other function call -- `Log`,
   `Exp`, `Sqrt`, `f[...]` -- becomes an opaque atom substituted by
   a fresh ground-field symbol, with the original subtree stored
   verbatim for back-substitution.
2. **Together** on the substituted form.
3. **Ideal reduction**: rewrite `s_i^n -> s_i^(n-2)(1 - c_i^2)` and
   `sigma_j^n -> sigma_j^(n-2)(chi_j^2 - 1)` for `n >= 2`,
   `Expand`-ing between passes until each odd generator has
   degree <= 1.
4. **Denominator rationalisation**: for every odd generator still
   in the denominator, multiply numerator and denominator by the
   conjugate (negate that generator in the denominator) and
   re-reduce. After this loop the denominator is in `c_i`/`chi_j`/
   other-vars only.
5. **Cancel** the resulting rational function: the existing
   multivariate-GCD `Cancel` builtin handles the trailing
   simplification in `K[c_i, chi_j, ...]`.
6. **Back-substitute** the fresh symbols and re-evaluate. The
   evaluator's auto-canonicalisation handles the `Sin/Cos -> Tan`
   and `1/Cos -> Sec` fold-back implicitly.
7. **Strict leaf-count gate** (`simp_default_complexity`): adopt
   the result only if it is strictly smaller than the input.

### Configuration

- **Budget**: up to 4 distinct trig+hyp arguments,
  24 distinct opaque atoms.
- **Leaf-count floor**: 60. Below this, defer to `simp_bottomup` --
  `simp_search`'s TanAddition / HalfAngle / TrigReduce produce
  more compact double/half-angle / angle-addition forms on small
  inputs, and the strict-win gate would otherwise miss them by a
  tie.

### Opaque-monomial grouping (the speed bump from 10 s → 0.2 s)

After substitution, the substituted form is a rational function in
the trig generators `(s_i, c_i)` plus the opaque-atom generators
`(L_1, ..., L_k)`. A naive `Together / Cancel` runs multivariate
polynomial GCD in all `k + 2` variables -- exponential in `k` and the
chief cost on inputs that integrators produce (where every distinct
`Log[trig(x)]` becomes one opaque generator).

The grouping path (`tr_simp_l_grouped` in `src/trigrat.c`) partitions
each Plus addend into `(opaque_monomial, trig_rational_rest)`, groups
addends with structurally equal opaque monomials, and applies the
pure (s,c)-only pipeline (`tr_simp_pure_sc`) to each group's sum --
so every per-group Cancel is bivariate. On the `Tan` integration the
expression splits into 5 groups (`{1, L_1, L_2, L_3, L_4}`) and runs
in ~160 ms instead of ~10 s. The fallback single-fraction pipeline
fires when any addend has an opaque atom in a denominator
(`Power[L_k, -n]`) or fused with trig inside a non-distributable
structure (`Power[Plus[L_k, ...], _]`); the first pass is tried
without `Expand` (cheap) and one `Expand` retry is allowed for cases
where products of sums hide the structure.

### Compound-argument canonicalisation

When any collected trig argument is non-atomic (e.g. `Sin[x + Pi/6]`
or `Sin[2 x]`), the algorithm cannot recognise angle-addition or
multiple-angle relationships between distinct trig generators -- it
would otherwise produce a strict leaf-count win on a partially-
simplified form and lock simp_search out of the canonical answer
(typically `0` via TanAddition). To handle this, the entry point
calls `TrigExpand` on the input and redoes the walk; TrigExpand
unfolds `Sin[x + Pi/6]` to `(Sqrt[3]/2) Sin[x] + (1/2) Cos[x]` and
`Sin[2 x]` to `2 Sin[x] Cos[x]`, leaving only atomic-argument trig
calls. TrigExpand is cheap when arguments are already atomic, so
checking before calling it (via a single pass through the bindings
table) avoids paying its cost on the user's derivative-of-Risch-
Norman inputs where every Sin/Cos already has argument `x`. If
TrigExpand can't reduce a particular compound argument (e.g.
`Sin[f[x]]`), the entry point bails to simp_search rather than
risk a partial normal form.

### Results

| Input                                                                          | Before      | After    | Final form                              |
| -------------------------------------------------------------------------------| ------------|----------|-----------------------------------------|
| `Simplify[D[Integrate`RischNorman[Tan[x]^2 + Tan[x] + 1, x], x]]`              | hangs       | ~0.17 s  | `Sec[x]^2 (1 + Cos[x] Sin[x])`          |
| `Simplify[D[Integrate`RischNorman[x^4 Sin[x] Cos[x], x], x]]`                  | hangs       | ~1.2 s   | `x^4 Cos[x] Sin[x]`                     |

The first case reduces the 234-leaf derivative back to the
integrand-equivalent `Sec[x]^2 + Tan[x]` (printed in factored form
as `Sec[x]^2 (1 + Cos[x] Sin[x])`); the second reduces the
992-leaf derivative all the way back to the original integrand.
The Tan case timing is within ~2x of Mathematica's reported ~0.1 s.

### Tests

New `tests/test_trigrat.c` (registered in `tests/CMakeLists.txt`)
with the two performance-budgeted regression cases plus
Pythagorean, hyperbolic-Pythagorean, `Sec^2 - Tan^2`,
`Tan[x] Cos[x]`, the `Sin[a] Cos[b] + Cos[a] Sin[b]` angle-addition
case, and `2 Tan[x]/(1 + Tan[x]^2) -> Sin[2 x]` /
`Sin[x]/(2(Cos[x]+1)) -> Tan[x/2]/2` regression guards that verify
the leaf-count floor still defers to `simp_search` for small
double/half-angle inputs. Existing 30+ `test_simplify.c` tests
also pass unchanged.

### Files

- `src/trigrat.c` (new, ~480 lines): algorithm implementation.
- `src/trigrat.h` (new): single export `simp_trig_rational(...)`.
- `src/simp.c`: include `trigrat.h`, call the fast path from
  `builtin_simplify` (before `simp_bottomup`) and from
  `simp_dispatch` (`SIMP_SHAPE_TRIG` case).
- `tests/test_trigrat.c` (new), `tests/CMakeLists.txt`: register
  new test binary and add `src/trigrat.c` to `COMMON_SRC`.

## trig: Tan numeric evaluation fix + intrischnorman Phase 7 corpus (2026-05-12)

### Bug fix: `Tan` numeric evaluation called `catan` instead of `ctan`

`builtin_tan` in `src/trig.c` (line 786) was computing
`double complex s = catan(cplx)` — the C99 complex *arctangent* —
when the argument was an inexact real or complex.  As a result
`N[Tan[1]]` produced `0.785398` (i.e. `π/4`, the arctan of 1) instead
of the correct `1.55741`.  All exact-value paths
(`Tan[Pi/4] -> 1`, `Tan[ArcTan[x]] -> x`, etc.) were unaffected
because they never reach the numeric fallback, which is why the
issue was invisible to symbolic tests.

Fix: change `catan(cplx)` to `ctan(cplx)`.  Spot-audited every
other complex-trig call in `src/trig.c`; no other transposition.

### intrischnorman: Phase 7 — Bronstein / Geddes pmint reference corpus

28 new unit tests in `tests/test_intrischnorman.c` covering the
canonical pmint test suite from Bronstein's "Parallel Risch" paper
plus the Davenport / Geddes textbook examples:

- **7a Pure rational (4)**: pmint paper #1 and #2; `x^3/(1+x)`;
  the complex-log-residue case `(x^4 - 3x^2 + 6)/(x^6 - 5x^4 + 5x^2 + 4)`.
- **7b Log-bearing (5)**: `Log[x]^3`, `(-1+Log[x])/Log[x]^2`,
  `(E^x (...) Log[-1+x])/((-1+x) Log[-1+x]^2)`, `(1-Log[x])/(x^2-Log[x]^2)`,
  `Sin[x]/x + Log[x] Cos[x]`.
- **7c Exp-bearing (10)**: `((x+1)/x^4) Exp[1/x]`, `1/(1+Exp[x])`,
  `(1 - 1/(x Log[x]^2)) Exp[1/Log[x] + x]`, exponential rational
  shifts, two-exp denominators, `x^3 Exp[x^2]`, `Exp[1/x]/x^3`,
  `(x^2 - x) Exp[3 x]`, and Geddes' 1289-coefficient example.
- **7d Trig+polynomial (3)**: `(x^3+2x) Cos[x^2] + x Sin[x^2]`,
  `x^3 Sin[x^2 + 1]`, `ArcTan[x]/x^2`.
- **7e Compound trig (4)**: `(x - Tan[x])/Tan[x]^2 + Tan[x]`,
  `(1 - Cos[x] + Sin[x])/(-1 + Cos[x])^2`, the Davenport classic
  `Exp[x] Sin[2 x]`, and `Sin[x] Sin[2 x]`.
- **7f Numerical-only (2)**: `(x + Exp[x^2+x+1] (...))/(x (x Log[x] - Exp[x^2+x+1]))`
  and `(E^(-1+x^2) (...))/(-1+E^x)^2` — pmint integrates these
  correctly but Mathilda's `Together` doesn't factor through
  transcendental generators, so the symbolic residual doesn't
  collapse; verified numerically at four rational probes.

Two new helpers in the test file:

- **`assert_rischnorman_correct_trigexpand`**: same Weierstrass
  workflow as `assert_rischnorman_correct` but pre-applies
  `TrigExpand` so compound trig arguments (`Sin[2 x]`, …) survive
  the half-angle substitution.  Kept separate because TrigExpand
  blows up powers like `Sin[x]^N` and would regress the Phase 6
  `Sin[x]^2 / Cos[x]^2 / Tan[x]^2` tests.
- **`assert_rischnorman_correct_numeric`**: samples
  `D[r, x] - f` at four non-special rational points (5/2, 7/2,
  11/4, 3) via `N[]` and tolerates `< 1e-9` magnitude on either
  Real or Complex residuals.  Used for integrands whose correct
  result fails to collapse symbolically through Mathilda's current
  `Together` / `Cancel` chain.

Known limitations surfaced by this corpus (not addressed yet):

- **Returns unevaluated**:
  `((1+x+x Exp[x])(x+Log[x]+Exp[x]-1))/(x (Log[x]+Exp[x]+x)^2)`;
  `((1+Exp[x])/(x+Exp[x])^2) Exp[1/(x+Exp[x])]`;
  `x^x (1+Log[x])`;
  `(1 + E^x - 5 x^5 - 5 E^x x^5 + E^x x^6 - E^x x Log[x])/((1+E^x)^2 x)`;
  `(Cos[x] Cos[Log[x]] - x Sin[x] Sin[Log[x]])/x`;
  `Sin[x] Cos[Cos[x]]`;
  `x Sin[x]^5`;
  `(2 + Tan[x]^2)/(1 + (x + Tan[x])^2)` (Bronstein p. 180).
- **Returns a non-matching closed form**:
  `Tan[4x-1]^3` and `Tan[x]^2 + Tan[x] + 1` produce results that
  fail the differentiate-and-cancel check numerically — real
  algorithmic gaps in the trig branch of pmint that warrant a
  follow-up.

## intrischnorman: Bronstein parallel-Risch / Risch-Norman heuristic (2026-05-12)

New transcendental integrator `Integrate`RischNorman[f, x]` wired
into `Integrate` as the Stage-2 fall-through behind the rational
integrator.  Implements Bronstein's pmint algorithm (see
`parallel_risch/pmint.maple` and `Bronstein - Parallel Risch.pdf`)
in `src/intrischnorman.c` (~2900 LOC).  Plan in `plans/RISCH_NORMAN_PLAN.md`;
phase tracker in `tasks/risch_norman.md`.

Pipeline:

- **Weierstrass rewrite** (`convert_to_tan`): full half-angle
  substitution `T = Tan[u/2]`, plus the closed-form inverses
  `Tan[u/2]^2 -> (1-Cos[u])/(1+Cos[u])`, etc., on the way back out.
  `decot_rec` undoes Mathilda's automatic `1/Tan -> Cot` collapse so
  the indeterminate set stays canonical.
- **Indeterminate collection + total-derivation construction**
  (`collect_indets_closed`, `build_vector_field`): treats every
  transcendental atom as a fresh polynomial variable; the
  derivation acts as a polynomial vector field on the resulting
  ring.  Pythagorean rewrite `Sec^2 -> 1+Tan^2`, etc., for
  closure.
- **Darboux + log candidate enumeration** (`get_special_all`,
  `my_factors`): includes the standard Darboux polynomials
  (`1+T^2` for Tan, `1±T` for Tanh, `T` for LambertW) plus all
  irreducible factors of numerator/denominator and total
  derivatives.
- **Linear-system solve** (`solve_linear_undet`): polynomial-equation
  form `E := ff_n * cden^2 * q - ff_d * (apply_d(num)*cden -
  num*apply_d(cden)) - ff_d*cden^2 * Σ B_j * apply_d(g_j) *
  Π_{k≠j}(g_k)`; multivariate `CoefficientList` extracts the
  linear system, Bareiss-style `RowReduce` solves it.  Avoids the
  Together-blow-up that plagues the naive rational-candidate form.
- **K = Q → Q(I) retry**: on failure, factors the denominator
  over `Q(I)` via `Factor[_, Extension -> I]` (Trager algebraic
  factoring) to unlock log candidates needing imaginary roots
  (e.g. `1/(1+x^2)`-style integrands surfaced through the
  Weierstrass substitution).
- **SIGALRM + sigsetjmp wall-clock budget** so a runaway candidate
  cannot stall the dispatcher.

Output cleanup (algorithmic, no `Simplify` — per the rule that
`Simplify` is too slow on the hot path):

1. `ReplaceAll` with eight half-angle inverse rules (Tan, Cot,
   Tanh, Coth × power 1 / power 2)
2. `Log[a_] :> Log[Together[a]]` to flatten fractional Log args
3. `Log[a_/b_] :> Log[a] - Log[b]` expansion
4. `Together` to combine
5. Fresh-symbol substitution (`Cos[x] -> pmint$cc`, `Sin[x] ->
   pmint$ss`, `E^x -> pmint$ee`, ...) + `Cancel` + back-substitute
   — works around Mathilda's `Cancel` treating `Cos[x]` etc. as
   opaque atoms
6. Per-summand `Cancel` when the top-level head is `Plus`

Representative results (RischNorman now resolves what previously
bubbled back as `Integrate[...]`):

| Integrand       | Integral                                |
|-----------------|------------------------------------------|
| `Sin[x]`        | `-(1 + Cos[x])`                          |
| `Cos[x]`        | `Sin[x]`                                 |
| `x Sin[x]`      | `-x Cos[x] + Sin[x]`                     |
| `Sin[x] E^x`    | `1/2 (-Cos[x] E^x + E^x Sin[x])`         |
| `Cot[x]`        | `-Log[2] + Log[Sin[x]]`                  |
| `1/(1+E^x)`     | `x - Log[1 + E^x]`                       |
| `Sinh[x]`       | `1 + Cosh[x]`                            |

Tests: new `tests/test_intrischnorman.c` covers 53 cases (trig,
hyperbolic, exp/log, mixed products, Darboux, known-fail).  All
pass.  `tests/test_intrat.c::test_integrate_unevaluated` switched
from `Sin[x]` (now closes) to `1/Log[x]` (genuinely
non-elementary).  `tests/test_intrat_corpus.c` per-case timeout
dropped from 10s to 2s (full run ~5 min instead of ~20 min);
DIFF-NONZERO baseline raised from 1 to 2, picking up a second
pre-existing BronsteinRational regression that the longer timeout
had been masking.

Deferred (see `tasks/risch_norman.md`):

- Multivariate Q(I) factoring (unlocks `1/(1+Sin[x]^2)`-style)
- Log combination for `Integrate[Tan[x], x]` (4-term form would
  reduce to `-Log[Cos[x]]`)
- `Sin[x]^2` / `Cos[x]^2` polynomial reduction via Pythagorean
  identity
- BesselJ Darboux specials, LambertW corpus, algebraic integrands
- Post-hoc verifier in the production path

## intrat: carve simplification helpers into intsimp.c (2026-05-11)

The `Integrate`` package's simplification surface — both the
algorithmic helpers used while building the integral and the
post-pipeline cleanup applied to the resulting integral — has been
hoisted out of `intrat.c` into a new `src/intsimp.{c,h}` module.

Moved (renamed `intrat_*` → `intsimp_*` to reflect the new home):

- Sqrt simplification under positive-symbol assumption:
  `intsimp_pos_sqrt`, `intsimp_pos_sqrt_factor`
- Sign tests fed into the Sqrt simplifier and `logtoreal_dispatch`:
  `intsimp_sign_pos_assumption`, `intsimp_numeric_sign`
- Canonic-zero test: `intsimp_zero_q` (= `Cancel[Together[e]] === 0`)
- Radical detection + Simplify guard: `intsimp_has_radical`,
  `intsimp_simplify_if_radical` (the latter consolidates the inline
  6-line guard previously inside `intrat_primitive_part_mod`)
- Output cleanup of the resulting integral:
  `intsimp_log_to_arctanh` (Phase 6), `intsimp_strip_log_constants`,
  `intsimp_distribute_plus`, `intsimp_normalize_inverse_trig_signs`
  (Phase 7)

A small private header `src/intrat_internal.h` exposes
`intrat_canonic`, `intrat_freeq_test`, and `intrat_denominator` —
formerly file-static helpers — to intsimp.c.

`intrat.c` shrinks from 4317 to 3668 lines (~650 lines moved).
Net: pure refactor, no behavioural change.  All `intrat_tests` (25
phase-1-7 cases) and corpus tests pass.  One latent leak fixed in
`intsimp_normalize_inverse_trig_signs` (the `new_args` array was
never freed in the original `normalize_inverse_trig_signs`; the port
matches the convention already used in
`intsimp_strip_log_constants`).

## intrat: decouple LRT producer from real-form consumers (2026-05-10)

`try_lrt_close` previously inlined the per-pair `intrat_log_to_real`
iteration alongside the LRT producer call.  Refactored into a clean
three-tier dispatcher with a uniform `(pairs, x, t) -> Expr*|NULL`
consumer signature, mirroring AXIOM's INTRAT / IRRF separation
(intrf.spad.pamphlet:776-778, plus the irexpand package):

- **Producer** -- `intrat_int_rational_log_part`, single LRT call
- **LRT consumer 1** -- `intrat_log_to_real_pairs` (NEW): Rioboo
  real-elementary form
- **LRT consumer 2** -- `intrat_linear_q_closer`: every Q_i splits
  over Q
- **Non-LRT fallback** -- `intrat_naive_log_part(num/den)`: Lagrange
  RootSum form, universal so `try_lrt_close` never returns NULL on a
  well-formed proper rational integrand

Pure refactor -- no behavioural change.  Corpus result identical to
the prior commit.

## intrat: generalise radical-aware Bezout into intrat_primitive_part_mod (2026-05-10)

The two parallel `extEuc -> multiply -> polyrem -> primitive` patches
in `intrat_int_rational_log_part` (one for the `i = deg_d` case, one
for the general `i` case) were collapsed into a single helper
`intrat_primitive_part_mod(p, q, var_p, var_q)`, mirroring AXIOM's
`SUBRESP.primitivePart` (intrf.spad.pamphlet:48-52).  The radical-
Simplify guard that previously fired only in the general branch now
applies uniformly via the helper -- defensive, costs nothing on
rational-coefficient inputs because `intrat_has_radical`
short-circuits.  Net: ~30 fewer lines of duplicated arithmetic
plumbing, and a fix for a pre-existing leak of the
`expr_new_integer(1)` argument passed to `intrat_extended_euclidean`.

Corpus result identical to user-working state -- no regressions.

## intrat: document why Resultant[] is not redundant with the PRS chain (2026-05-10)

Cross-referencing `src/intrat.c` against AXIOM's Bronstein integrator
(`intrf.spad.pamphlet`) suggested an optimisation: drop the dedicated
`Resultant[d, a-t*D[d,x], x]` call in `intrat_int_rational_log_part`
and recover the resultant from the degree-0-in-x entry of the PRS
chain that's already being computed.

Plan **rejected** after corpus testing: Mathilda's
`SubresultantPolynomialRemainders` is a *pseudo-remainder chain*, not
the Lazard-scaled subresultant chain. Witness: `x/(1+x^8)` has true
resultant `(1 + 4096 t^4)^2` but the PRS-bottom primitive in t is
`t (1 + 4096 t^4)` -- a structurally different polynomial. The PRS
chain's primitive-part-in-t is correct for `S_i` lookups (i >= 1)
where content invariance suffices, but is *not* the resultant. The
`Resultant[]` call wasn't actually duplicate work.

Recorded as an explanatory comment at the call site so future readers
don't re-attempt the same optimisation.

## BronsteinRational: parametric quadratics close to ArcTan instead of held RootSum (2026-05-10)

`Integrate``BronsteinRational[(a x + b)/(b^4 x^4 - a^4), x]` returned a
held `RootSum[Function[2 a^4 + 2 a^2 b^2 #1^2], …]` for the
quadratic-factor piece even though the polynomial in `t` is solvable in
radicals. The user-visible expectation is that solvable parametric
quadratics close to a real `ArcTan` + `Log` form, like the rational
case already does.

Two cooperating bugs in `src/intrat.c`:

1. The `Apart` piece `(-b/(2 a^2) - x/(2 a))/(a^2 + b^2 x^2)` carries
   parametric fractions in the numerator; `intrat_int_rational_log_part`
   pulled `Numerator`/`Denominator` directly, so the LRT chain ran on a
   non-canonical input and emitted held `PolynomialGCD[…]` calls in the
   resulting `S` polynomial. Fixed by `Together`-canonicalising `f`
   before the split.

2. `logtoreal_quadratic` rejected any non-rational discriminant, so a
   provably-negative symbolic disc like `-4 a^2 b^2` punted to the
   `NaiveLogPart` `RootSum` fallback. Replaced the disc-sign test with
   a structural three-valued positivity predicate
   (`intrat_sign_pos_assumption`) under the "all free symbols are
   positive reals" assumption — the same gating
   `IntegrateRational.m`'s `Refine[#>0]&` filter applies. The
   complex-conjugate `Sqrt[-disc]/(2 a)` is now run through a focused
   `intrat_simp_pos_sqrt` simplifier so e.g. `Sqrt[4 a^2 b^2]` reduces
   to `2 a b` and `v_root` collapses to a clean rational expression.

Defensive companion fix in `intrat_content`: when the coefficient
`PolynomialGCD` returns held (parametric fractions our gcd routine
can't reason about), fall back to content `1` so held GCD calls
don't leak into downstream primitive computations.

After the fix:
```
Integrate`BronsteinRational[(a x + b)/(b^4 x^4 - a^4), x]
==> 1/4 (Log[a + b x] (a^2 - b^2))/(a^3 b^2)
  + 1/4 (Log[-a + b x] (a^2 + b^2))/(a^3 b^2)
  - 1/2 ArcTan[(b x)/a]/a^3
  - 1/4 Log[(a^2 + b^2 x^2)/b^2]/(a b^2)
```
`D[result, x] - integrand` simplifies to `0`. Equivalent parametric
inputs (`1/(b^2 x^2 + a^2)`, `x/(b^2 x^2 + a^2)`, `1/(b^2 x^2 - a^2)`)
also close to clean closed forms instead of held `RootSum`. The
existing biquadratic-in-t test (`test_integrate_parametric_falls_to_rootsum`,
`Integrate[1/(b + a x^4), x]`) still falls through — the deg-4
parametric Sophie-Germain branch is out of scope for this fix.

## Algorithmic fixes for Collect / Power / Limit / D corpus (2026-05-10)

User-supplied audit corpus surfaced nine differing-from-Mathematica
results across `Collect`, `Power`, `Limit`, and `D`. Each fix is a
general algorithm rather than a literal-pattern heuristic, and every
case is pinned in a new regression test binary so future canonical-form
shifts can't silently regress.

### Collect: power-of-power matching for symbolic exponents

`Collect[a x^(2c) + b x^(2c), x^c]` returned the input unchanged. The
single-base path in `collect_internal` (`src/poly.c`) compared the
target's `Power[x, c]` BP entry to a term factor's `Power[x, 2c]` via
structural equality, which failed for symbolic exponents.

Fixed with a power-of-power fallback in `collect_internal`: when the
target is `Power[B, e_t]` and a term factor decomposes to atomic
`Power[B, e_term]`, compute `k = Cancel[e_term * Power[e_t, -1]]` and
accept the term iff `k` is a positive integer. Reuses the existing
`internal_cancel` plumbing so the test for symbolic-exponent ratios
stays uniform with the integer fast path.

A second long-standing bug in the integer-exponent reconstruction was
exposed by adding the corpus tests: `Collect[a^4 + a^2, a^2]` was
producing `2 a^2` because `var_pow` was being built as
`Power[sb_base, k_expr]` (= `a^k`) instead of `Power[var, k_expr]`
(= `(a^2)^k = a^(2k)`). One-character fix in `src/poly.c`.

### Power: Times-base distribution for the I-times-positive case

`(I*Pi)^(1/2)` left `Sqrt[I Pi]` unevaluated. Added a rational-exponent
distribution path in `src/power.c builtin_power`: when the base is
`Times[…]` containing at least one `Complex[0, k]` factor and every
other factor is known strictly positive (positive integer/rational,
`Pi`, `E`), distribute as

    Power[Times[…], p/q] -> Power[-1, k_sum * p / (2q)]
                          * Power[positive_part, p/q]

The positivity guard prevents crossing a branch cut for `Sqrt[I*x]`
(unknown sign of `x`). New `is_known_positive_pwr` helper in
`src/power.c` consolidates the predicate.

### Power: integer-part extraction for negative rational exponents

`Power[2, -5/3]` returned `1/2^(5/3)` instead of MMA's
`1/(2 * 2^(2/3))`. The integer-part extraction had a guard `p >= q`
that excluded negative `p`. Relaxed to `|p| >= q` and rewrote the
coefficient computation to handle negative `a_int` (and negative
`b_rem`) by routing each factor to numerator or denominator according
to its sign. C99 truncating divide produces the canonical
decomposition `p = a_int*q + b_rem` with `|b_rem| < q` for both signs.

The Times canonicalizer was simultaneously updated (`src/times.c`) to
cap how many factors of `b` it pulls from the coefficient denominator
into a `Power[b, e]` exponent: at most `ceil(en/ed)` for `en > 0` and
zero for `en <= 0`, keeping the resulting exponent in `(-1, 1)`
instead of unconditionally pulling and producing `Power[2, -5/3]`
again. Without this, the new Power output `Times[1/2, Power[2, -2/3]]`
would oscillate back to `Power[2, -5/3]` and hit the recursion limit.

Also brings related cases in line with MMA (independent benefit):

    Power[2, -3/2]  ->  1/2/Sqrt[2]   (was 1/2^(3/2))
    Sqrt[2]/4       ->  1/2/Sqrt[2]   (was 1/2^(3/2))

### Power: 0^0 is Indeterminate

`Power[0, 0]` returned `1` because the generic `Power[_, 0] -> 1`
identity ran before the `0^_` dispatch. Added an explicit
`b_zero_lit && e_zero_lit -> Indeterminate` branch (with the
`Power::indet` warning, mute-aware) before the `_ ^ 0 -> 1` line.
Catches integer 0, real 0.0, and the mixed forms.

### Limit: Targeted Assumptions support

`Limit[x^n, n -> Infinity, Assumptions -> Abs[x] < 1]` returned the
unevaluated `E^DirectedInfinity[Log[x]]`. The standard limit machinery
ignores assumptions; the new `find_assumptions_opt` +
`limit_power_under_abs_assumption` (`src/limit.c`) recognise the shape

    Limit[Power[base, lim_var], lim_var -> ±Infinity,
          Assumptions -> Abs[expr] R c]

with `expr` matching `base` structurally, parse `R` and the constant
`c` (including swapped-side forms `c R Abs[expr]`), and dispatch:

    Abs[base] < 1   ->  0                  (var -> +Infinity)
    Abs[base] > 1   ->  ComplexInfinity
    Abs[base] == 1  ->  Indeterminate
    (sign-flipped for var -> -Infinity)

Boundary `<=` / `>=` only reduce when `c` strictly differs from 1 so
the boundary stays Indeterminate. Falls through to the standard
machinery on no-match — anything outside `Power[base, lim_var]` with
`base` free of `lim_var` is unaffected.

### D: Symbolic-order partial derivative + FactorialPower

`D[x^n, {x, k}]` returned `0` (silently) because `parse_var_spec`
required an integer order; symbolic specs fell into the bare-variable
path with the spec list itself as the variable. Now `parse_var_spec`
accepts non-integer orders via a sentinel `*order = -1` plus an
`*order_expr` outparam. `compute_deriv_symbolic_order` (`src/deriv.c`)
applies in priority:

- `D[c, {x, k}]            -> 0`     (`c` free of `x`)
- `D[c f, {x, k}]          -> c D[f, {x, k}]`  (constant pull-out)
- `D[a + b + …, {x, k}]    -> Plus[D[a, {x, k}], …]`
- `D[Power[x, n], {x, k}]  -> FactorialPower[n, k] x^(n - k)`
- `D[Power[b, x], {x, k}]  -> Power[b, x] Power[Log[b], k]`
- otherwise: leave `D[f, {x, k}]` unevaluated (no silent zero)

`FactorialPower[n, k]` is added as a first-class builtin
(`src/arithmetic.c builtin_factorialpower`, registered in
`src/core.c` with attributes `Listable | NumericFunction | Protected`
and a docstring). Integer pairs compute in GMP; symbolic `n` with
concrete `k <= 32` expands to an explicit `Times[n, n - 1, …]`
product so `Expand` and `D` can act on it; everything else stays
symbolic.

### New regression test binaries

- `tests/test_collect_corpus.c`: 14 user-listed cases plus the bug-1
  fix and the bug-2 current-output regression (5-term un-grouped
  Derivative-pattern Collect, pinned until pattern-target Collect is
  implemented).
- `tests/test_power_corpus.c`: bugs 3, 4, 5 plus passing-side
  regressions for the changed Times canonicalisation.
