- `src/qafactor.c`: new file-static helpers
  `expr_is_atomic_algebraic`, `exprlist_push_unique_borrowed`,
  `expr_collect_atomic_algebraics`, `expr_zn_minus_base`,
  `expr_qx_squarefree_part`, `expr_qx_is_irreducible`,
  `qa_resolve_nested_radical`, plus a forward declaration at the
  top of the file.  `qa_resolve_extension`'s `c^(1/n)` branch falls
  through to the new branch on non-integer base.
- `tests/test_qafactor.c`: 5 new tests (45 total) — headline
  `x^8 + 1` over `Q(Sqrt[2 - Sqrt[2]])`, the min-poly-of-α splits
  case, Sqrt[2+Sqrt[3]], the denested Sqrt[5+2Sqrt[6]] case, and
  the `Sqrt[5] ∉ Q(α)` irreducible-stays-unfactored edge.

## Resultant: Bronstein subresultant PRS as the default algorithm (2026-05-09)

`Resultant[A, B, var]` previously built the (n+m)x(n+m) Sylvester
matrix and called `Det`.  For matrices over Q, `bareiss_det` works
in O(n^3) with exact integer divisions.  For matrices with
symbolic-or-algebraic-number coefficients, however, `bd_exact_div`
cannot certify exact division and the path silently falls back to
`laplace_det` at O(n!), which on inputs from
`BronsteinRational[...]`'s LRT-log-part call (typically an
(n+m)x(n+m) matrix where n+m ≈ 11) effectively hangs.

The new default is Bronstein's subresultant algorithm (Symbolic
Integration I, p.24).  The chain runs entirely in D[x] for the
coefficient ring D, making only:

- `min(deg(A), deg(B))` calls to a **standard** pseudo-remainder
  `lc(B)^(deg(A)-deg(B)+1) * A mod B`, and
- one **scalar** exact division per chain step
  (`R_{i+1} = pprem / β_i` with `β_i ∈ D`, not `D[x]`).

That replaces ~n^3/3 polynomial-coefficient divisions in the matrix
path with ~n scalar divisions in the chain, and the chain never
needs the O(n!) Laplace fallback.

### Algorithm

Initial state: `R_0 = A`, `R_1 = B`, `δ_1 = deg(A) - deg(B)`,
`γ_1 = -1`, `β_1 = (-1)^(δ_1+1)`.

Loop while `R_i ≠ 0`:

```
pprem  = lc(R_i)^(deg(R_{i-1}) - deg(R_i) + 1) * R_{i-1} mod R_i
R_{i+1} = pprem / β_i              ;; exact in D
γ_{i+1} = (-r_i)^δ_i · γ_i^(1-δ_i)
δ_{i+1} = deg(R_i) - deg(R_{i+1})
β_{i+1} = -r_i · γ_{i+1}^δ_{i+1}
```

Termination: let `k = i - 1` (last non-zero R).
- `deg(R_k) > 0`: common factor exists → return 0.
- `deg(R_{k-1}) = 1`: return `R_k`.
- otherwise: return `s · c · R_k^deg(R_{k-1})` where `s` and `c` are
  the Bronstein τ_k accumulator running over `j = 1..k-1`.

Argument-order swap (when `deg(P) < deg(Q)`) multiplies the result
by `(-1)^(deg(P)·deg(Q))` per Theorem 1.4.1.

### Guards and fallback to Sylvester

Two early-exit guards keep the implementation from regressing
edge cases:

1. **Algebraic-content gate**.  Any input subterm of the form
   `Power[X, Rational[a, b]]` with `b > 1` (i.e. `Sqrt[N]`, cube
   roots, etc.) routes the call directly to the Sylvester+Det path.
   Reason: pseudo-remainder over `Q(α)[t][x]` produces
   `Power[α, k/m]` forms (e.g. `Sqrt[3]^3 → 3^(3/2)`) that don't
   combine via `Plus` with the equivalent `Times[α^q, Sqrt[α]]`,
   so chain elements bloat geometrically.  This is fundamentally a
   limitation of our algebraic-number canonicalisation, not of the
   subresultant scheme.

2. **Size budget**.  If any chain element exceeds 30x the input
   leaf-count (or 5000 leaves, whichever is larger), the path
   returns `NULL` and the caller (`resultant_internal`) falls back
   to `Sylvester+Det`.  This catches pathological symbolic inputs
   without affecting the common case.

### Performance impact

- `Resultant[x^10 - 5 x^7 + 3, x^9 - 2 x^4 + 7, x]`: 5.8 ms
  (formerly Sylvester+Det, comparable but no Laplace risk).
- `Discriminant[x^7 - 5 x^3 + 11, x]`: 1.4 ms.
- Q(√3) cases (LRT log-part calls in BronsteinRational): correctly
  routed to Sylvester+Det via the algebraic-content gate; 5.5 ms
  for a degree-3 chain, 40 ms for a degree-4 chain.  No regression.
- The hang in `Integrate[(... + Sqrt[3] ...)/((4+x^2)(... + Sqrt[3] ...))]`
  is **not** addressed by this change; that case requires
  architectural Q(α) arithmetic improvements (qaupoly substrate or
  modular-resultant) that are out of scope here.

### Files

- `src/poly.c`:
  - new static helpers `subres_leaf_count`, `subres_has_algebraic`,
    `pseudo_rem_standard`, `poly_divide_by_scalar`,
    `resultant_subresultant`.
  - `resultant_internal` calls `resultant_subresultant` first;
    on `NULL` it falls back to the existing Sylvester+Det code.
- Existing tests (`test_poly.c::test_resultant`,
  `test_poly.c::test_discriminant`, the BronsteinRational pipeline
  tests in `test_intrat*.c`, the qafactor tests) all pass
  unchanged.

## Radical canonical forms (`power.c`, `times.c`, 2026-05-10)

Mathilda's automatic evaluator now produces Mathematica-compatible
canonical forms for several radical patterns that previously survived
unevaluated. The work is split between three cooperating rewrites,
all implemented directly on GMP integers without round-tripping
through the evaluator on the hot path.

### 1. Integer-part extraction with rational coefficients

`Power[n, p/q]` for a positive integer base `n`, `p ≥ q > 1`,
decomposes the exponent as `p = a·q + b` with `0 ≤ b < q` and
combines with the existing perfect-q-th-power reduction
(`n = m^q · r`) to produce
`n^(p/q) = (n^a · m^b) · r^(b/q)` in a single GMP pass. The Times
canonicalizer additionally pulls factors of the base out of the
rational coefficient (`num_prod` / `den_prod`) — always from the
denominator, and from the numerator only enough to keep the
exponent ≤ 0, avoiding a re-extraction loop with the Power-side
rule. Together these turn:

| Input              | Output            |
|--------------------|-------------------|
| `Sqrt[2]/2`        | `1/Sqrt[2]`       |
| `2^(1/3)/2`        | `1/2^(2/3)`       |
| `3^(3/2)`          | `3 Sqrt[3]`       |
| `8/Sqrt[2]`        | `4 Sqrt[2]`       |
| `3^(3/2)+3^(5/2)+3^(7/2)` | `39 Sqrt[3]` |

### 2. Generalized radical fusion in Times (integer-ratio exponents)

The Times canonicalizer now collapses `Power[a, e_i] * Power[b, e_j]`
into a single Power whenever `a, b` are positive numerics and `e_j`
is an integer multiple of `e_i` (or vice-versa). With both
exponents reduced to lowest terms the integer ratio `k = p_j / p_i`
is well defined when the denominators match; the result is
`Power[a · b^k, e_pri]` where `pri` is whichever group has the
smaller-magnitude numerator. This subsumes the basic radical
fusion (k = -1) and same-exponent product collapse (k = +1) as
special cases:

| Input                      | k    | Output      |
|----------------------------|------|-------------|
| `Sqrt[2] Sqrt[3]`          | +1   | `Sqrt[6]`   |
| `2^(1/3) 3^(1/3)`          | +1   | `6^(1/3)`   |
| `Sqrt[6]/Sqrt[2]`          | -1   | `Sqrt[3]`   |
| `12^(1/3) 4^(-1/3)`        | -1   | `3^(1/3)`   |
| `12^(1/3) 2^(-2/3)`        | -2   | `3^(1/3)`   |
| `2^(1/3) 8^(2/3)`          | +2   | `4 2^(1/3)` |

The rewrite is restricted to positive numeric bases for principal-
branch correctness and to non-trivial denominators (q > 1) so
ordinary integer-exponent multiplication is left alone.

### 3. Perfect-power base unification

`Power[b^k, p/q]` with `b^k` a positive integer perfect power
rewrites to `Power[b, k·p/q]`, choosing `b` minimal (equivalently
`k` maximal). The detection uses `mpz_perfect_power_p` for the
fast yes/no, then iteratively factors small primes (table of 31
primes up to 127) out of the exponent via `mpz_root`. The
reduced expression then flows through the existing integer-part
extraction, so the residue under the radical is always over the
smallest possible base. Closes a visible gap in our output:

| Input         | Output       |
|---------------|--------------|
| `4^(2/3)`     | `2 2^(1/3)`  |
| `9^(1/3)`     | `3^(2/3)`    |
| `9^(2/3)`     | `3 3^(1/3)`  |
| `16^(2/3)`    | `4 2^(2/3)`  |
| `1024^(1/2)`  | `32`         |
| `64^(1/3)`    | `4`          |
| `100^(1/3)`   | `10^(2/3)`   |

The unification is restricted to **positive** bases. Negative
perfect powers (e.g. -8 = (-2)^3) are NOT unified because
`(-n)^(p/q) ≠ ((-n)^(1/k))^(k·p/q)` on the principal complex branch
(e.g. `(-8)^(1/6)` is not `(-2)^(1/2)`).

### 4. Sign normalization in negative-base radicals

For `(-n)^(p/q)` with positive `n` and **odd** `q`, the principal-
branch identity `(-n)^(p/q) = (-1)^(p/q) · n^(p/q)` lets us pull
the perfect-q-th-power factor out of `|n|` while leaving `(-1)^(b/q)`
(or `(-r)^(b/q)` when there's a non-trivial residue base `r`) under
the radical. Decomposing the exponent as `p = a·q + b` and noting
that `(-1)^a · n^a = (-n)^a` gives the integer part its sign:

| Input            | Output             |
|------------------|--------------------|
| `(-8)^(1/3)`     | `2 (-1)^(1/3)`     |
| `(-8)^(2/3)`     | `4 (-1)^(2/3)`     |
| `(-8)^(5/3)`     | `-32 (-1)^(2/3)`   |  (a_int = 1 odd → coeff negated)
| `(-72)^(1/3)`    | `2 (-9)^(1/3)`     |
| `(-200)^(1/3)`   | `2 (-25)^(1/3)`    |
| `(-2)^(1/3)`     | `(-2)^(1/3)`       |  (m=1, no extraction)

Even q with negative base remains intentionally unevaluated for
q > 2 (q = 2 still goes through the existing I-extraction path).

### Files

- `src/power.c`:
  - new static helper `find_min_perfect_base`: given a positive
    `mpz_t`, finds the smallest base and largest exponent of any
    perfect-power decomposition. Uses `mpz_perfect_power_p` for
    the fast reject and a small-prime table for iterative
    reduction.
  - perfect-power unification block before the existing rational-
    exponent extraction (recurses via `evaluate` with a strictly
    smaller base, guaranteed termination).
  - extended rational-exponent block: tracks `n_negative` /
    `abs_n`, sign-flips the integer-part coefficient when
    `(a_int % 2 == 1)`, builds `Power[-r, b/q]` residues for
    negative bases with odd q.
- `src/times.c`:
  - replaced separate "radical fusion" and "same-exponent
    collapse" loops with a single generalized-fusion loop that
    handles arbitrary integer-ratio exponents (k ∈ ℤ, |k| ≥ 1).
  - the existing coefficient-pulling pass (extracts factors of
    the base from `num_prod`/`den_prod`) is unchanged.
- `tests/test_radical_canonical.c`: extended to cover same-exponent
  collapse, generalized fusion (negative and positive k),
  perfect-power unification, sign normalization, and combinations
  thereof. ~70 new assertions across 14 test functions.

## Multi-radical Together / Cancel: hangs eliminated, soundness gates added (2026-05-10)

`Together` and `Cancel` previously hung indefinitely on inputs whose
denominators contained sums of distinct surds over Q (e.g.
`1/(Sqrt[2] a + Sqrt[3] + Sqrt[5] + Sqrt[7])` subtracted from its
already-rationalised equivalent). The hang was a multivariate
Euclidean coefficient explosion in `poly_gcd_internal`: when
`PolynomialLCM` claims that `den_i` divides `lcm_den` in some
algebraic-extension ring (true) but `cancel_exact_div_wrapper` cannot
realise the quotient as a polynomial in `Q[vars]` (also true),
returning a symbolic `Times[lcm_den, Power[den_i, -1]]` propagated a
`Power[Plus, -1]` into the combined numerator and the downstream
`PolynomialGCD` call ran multivariate Euclid on a rational input.

Four soundness gates now bound this work:

- `exact_poly_div` at `var_count == 0` only returns the symbolic
  `Times[A, Power[B, -1]]` rational fallback when both operands lie
  in a field (Q or Q[i]). For non-field atoms (Sqrt[2], symbolic
  radicals) it returns NULL — a sound "not exactly divisible" signal.
- `together_recursive` Plus branch uses a new `cancel_exact_div_strict`
  helper that exposes the NULL-on-non-exact behaviour of the line
  above; on any failure it abandons the combine and returns the input
  Plus unchanged, leaving the algebraic structure intact for
  downstream `simp_algebraic`.
- `cancel_recursive` runs an embedded-rational guard before
  `PolynomialGCD`: if either `num` or `den` carries a
  `Power[Plus/Times, negative]` subterm, the input is not a clean
  polynomial fraction and the cancellation is skipped.
- `poly_gcd_internal` adopts a `subres_leaf_count`-bounded budget
  (`max(input_size, 2000)`) plus a 50-iteration cap; on exhaustion it
  returns the content GCD — a sound (over-estimate-safe) divisor that
  lets the cancel pipeline proceed without coefficient explosion.

Result: `Together` on the case-13/14/20 inputs now completes in
seconds. The downstream `Simplify`-to-zero path is still slow on
case 13 (the seed pipeline iterates Together/Cancel many times) and
benefits from future optimisation.

## Plus auto-distributes `Times[-1, Plus[…]]` (2026-05-10)

`builtin_plus` now distributes a leading `-1` over an inner Plus
before grouping like-terms. Without this step the expression

  Plus[x, x^2, Times[-1, Plus[x, x^2]]]

never collected (three distinct bases) and stayed as written.
Mathematica returns 0 here. The distribution is gated on the literal
coefficient -1 only — `a + 2 (b + c)` still stays unexpanded, matching
MMA's behaviour. Cases like `Collect[expr, x] - expr` now reduce to 0
without needing Simplify.

## Collect handles compound monomial / Plus keys (2026-05-10)

`collect_internal` rewritten in `src/poly.c` to dispatch by the key's
BP-decomposition shape:

- Single-base key (atoms `x`, `Power[x, k]`, Plus keys
  `Plus[c, s]`): group each term by `term_exp / var_exp`, the
  rational/symbolic exponent at which the key's base appears.
- Multi-factor key (`Times[x, y, z]`, `x*f[x]`, `x*Log[x]`, etc.):
  use the existing `get_k` to find the integer multiplicity at which
  `var` divides each term, then residualise.

For Plus keys, expansion is skipped — `expand_patt` would distribute
the Plus across Times factors and destroy the structure we want to
collect on. Now:

  Collect[a (Cos[x]+Sin[x]) + b (Cos[x]+Sin[x]), Cos[x]+Sin[x]]
                                  ->  (a+b) (Cos[x]+Sin[x])
  Collect[a x y + b x y, x y]    ->  (a+b) x y
  Collect[a x f[x] + b x f[x], x f[x]]  ->  (a+b) x f[x]

Single-symbol Collect with fractional/symbolic exponents (e.g.
`Sqrt[x]`, `x^(2/3)`, `x^c`) is preserved.

## Power/Log identities under positivity and integer-exponent (2026-05-10)

Three additions in `src/simp.c`:

- `prov_int` accepts `Element[x, PositiveIntegers]` and the other
  ±-tagged integer subdomains.
- `prov_even` propagates through `Times`: a product is even when at
  least one factor is even and every factor is integer.
- `logexp_top_rewrite` adds two unconditional Power rules:
  `Power[-1, k] -> 1` when `prov_even(ctx, k)`, and
  `Power[E, Plus[t_1, …, t_n]] -> Product Power[E, t_i]` (after
  Expand of the exponent). Combined with the existing
  `Power[E, c Log[u]] -> u^c` rule, this collapses
  `Exp[k (Log[a] + Log[b])]` to `a^k b^k` for any `k`.

Cases now reducing to 0 under `Simplify`:

  (-1)^(2 n) - 1        (with Element[n, PositiveIntegers])
  Exp[3 (Log[a] + Log[b])] - a^3 b^3
  Exp[y (Log[a] + Log[b])] - (a b)^y    (with a > 0 && b > 0)

## intrat: parametric closure for quadratics, biquadratics, and bi-quadratics-in-t (2026-05-11)

Three closely-related fixes in `src/intrat.c` widen the parametric
reach of the LRT-then-real-form pipeline so that the families

  Integrate[1/(a x^2 + b x + c), x]                  (parametric quadratic)
  Integrate[1/(b + a x^4), x]                        (parametric Sophie-Germain)
  Integrate[1/(x^4 + a^4), x]
  Integrate[1/(a x^4 + b x^2 + c), x]                (parametric biquadratic)
  Integrate[x^2/(a x^4 + b x^2 + c), x]

now close to a real `Plus` of `ArcTan`/`Log` instead of falling through
to NaiveLogPart's held `RootSum`.

1. **`logtoreal_quadratic` parametric branch**.  When the discriminant
   sign is indeterminate under the positive-symbol assumption (the
   canonical case `disc = b^2 - 4 a c` with `a, b, c` independent
   symbols), the dispatcher now defaults to the negative-disc / ArcTan
   branch with a held `Sqrt[-disc]`.  That formula is the principal
   antiderivative for both signs of the discriminant — `ArcTan`
   continues analytically through imaginary argument — and matches
   Mathematica's parametric-quadratic output.

2. **Sqrt-simplifier negation distributes**.  The negation step
   `neg_disc_raw = -1 * disc` now passes through `expr_expand`, so the
   downstream `intrat_simp_pos_sqrt` sees a flat Plus rather than
   `Times[-1, Plus[...]]`.  Without this, the Sqrt simplifier walked
   the Times factors and pulled `Sqrt[-1] = I` out of the leading
   `-1`, producing an imaginary `v_root` that collapsed
   logtoreal_quadratic's output to 0.  The bug was masked on rational
   inputs (no Plus survived the constant fold) and only surfaced for
   the parametric quadratic now reachable via fix (1).

3. **Sophie-Germain `ratio_pos` widens to positive-symbol assumption**.
   The deg-4 dispatch's `ratio_pos = c0/c4 > 0` check accepted only
   literal positive integers/rationals.  It now accepts any expression
   provably positive under the positive-symbol assumption (e.g.
   `1/(256 a^12)` for the parametric `1/(x^4 + a^4)` family).

4. **Biquadratic-in-`t` branch (NEW)**.  The deg-4 dispatch gains a
   `c1 = 0, c3 = 0, c2 != 0` path that splits
   `c4 t^4 + c2 t^2 + c0` via the substitution `u = t^2` into
   `(t^2 - u_+)(t^2 - u_-)` with
   `u_± = (-c2 ± Sqrt[c2^2 - 4 c0 c4]) / (2 c4)`, then dispatches each
   factor through `logtoreal_quadratic` (whose new parametric branch
   from fix (1) handles the unknown-sign discriminant
   `4 u_±` cleanly).  This is what catches the
   `1/(a x^4 + b x^2 + c)` family.

Verified mathematically by numeric substitution
(`D[result, x] - integrand /. {a -> 2, b -> 5, c -> 7, x -> 3}`
evaluates to ≤ 1e-17 in `N[]`).  All `intrat` and `simplify` test
suites pass; the test
`tests/test_intrat.c::test_integrate_parametric_falls_to_rootsum` is
renamed to `test_integrate_parametric_biquadratic_closes` and updated
to verify the new closed-form behaviour.

Remaining out-of-scope parametric cases (still return RootSum):

  Integrate[1/(b - a x^3), x]                  (cubic — needs deg-3 closer)
  Integrate[x^4/(a + b x^3)^2, x]              (Hermite-reduced cubic)
  Integrate[1/(x^5 + 1), x]                    (cyclotomic quartic
                                                factor — needs real
                                                quadratic split over
                                                Q[Sqrt[5]])

The non-parametric Sophie-Germain regression (`1/(x^4 + 1)` and
similar) is unaffected; the existing path still triggers when
`ratio_pos` evaluates literally.

## facpoly: defensive NULL handling for non-field exact_poly_div (2026-05-11)

Fixed a crash in `Simplify` when the input contains an algebraic
generator (e.g. `Sqrt[a]`) shared between numerator and denominator:

  Simplify[(Sqrt[a] - Sqrt[a] x) / (2 Sqrt[a] + 2 Sqrt[a] x)]   (segfault, now -> -(1 - x)/(2(1+x)))

Root cause: the recent `exact_poly_div` field-vs-ring soundness fix
(2026-05-10) made the helper return NULL when its operands sit outside
a field (`Q`, `Q[i]`).  Two of `heuristic_factor_impl`'s call sites
in `src/facpoly.c` then fed that NULL straight into
`heuristic_factor`, which dereferenced `P->type` and segfaulted.

Two minimal edits:

1. `heuristic_factor_impl` now treats `pp == NULL` from
   `exact_poly_div` as "no content extractable at this level" and
   returns the input unchanged (matching the existing pp == 1 guard).

2. `heuristic_factor` itself gets a defensive top-of-function
   `if (!P) return NULL;` so any other future caller passing NULL
   propagates the signal instead of crashing.

This unblocks `Simplify[D[Integrate[1/(x^4 + a^4), x], x] - 1/(x^4 + a^4)]`
and any other parametric integral verification that produces a
nested-radical fraction with a shared algebraic factor.  Numerically
the result is still 0 (verified at concrete instantiations) but the
symbolic Simplify now leaves the radical-laden form un-reduced rather
than crashing.  Closing this nested radical to 0 is a separate task
(Simplify cannot yet recognise `Sqrt[2 Sqrt[1/(256 a^12)]]` as
rational in a^(-3)).

## intrat: biquadratic-in-t gate to preserve correctness on Sqrt[3]-laden inputs (2026-05-11)

Refined the biquadratic-in-`t` branch (added earlier today) with an
inner-discriminant soundness gate.  The branch substitutes `u = t^2`
and splits Q(t) into two quadratics `(t^2 - u_±)`, where
`u_± = (-c2 ± Sqrt[c2^2 - 4 c0 c4]) / (2 c4)`.  When the inner
discriminant `c2^2 - 4 c0 c4` is negative or sign-indeterminate, `u_±`
form a complex conjugate pair, the sub-factors have complex
coefficients, and `logtoreal_quadratic` (which assumes real
coefficients) silently miscomputes — typically collapsing to 0 because
the imaginary contributions cancel between the two sub-factor calls.

Caught by the IntegrateRationalTests corpus (case 54, a Sqrt[3]-
coefficient quartic with negative inner discriminant) which the
ungated branch was returning 0 for instead of the correct
~LeafCount-1700 expression.

The gate uses the existing `intrat_sign_pos_assumption` helper.  The
practical effect: parametric biquadratic families like
`1/(a x^4 + b x^2 + c)` (whose inner disc `16 (b^2 - 4 a c)^3` has
sign-indeterminate `(b^2 - 4 a c)^3` under the positive-symbol model)
revert to NaiveLogPart's held RootSum form (correct, just unsimplified)
rather than risk a silent wrong answer.  The `1/(b + a x^4)` and
`1/(x^4 + a^4)` families remain closed via the older Sophie-Germain
branch (a different code path with a unconditional positive
discriminant).

This is the conservative-correctness trade.  A future "decide whether
b^2 > 4 a c is generically expected" hint would let the branch fire
for those parametric biquadratics too.

## poly: PolynomialGCD content-extraction handles Plus bases (2026-05-11)

Fixed a structural-correctness bug in `builtin_polynomialgcd`'s
integer-content (`numG`) accumulation:

  Cancel[4/(4 + 4 x)]      -> 4/(4 + 4 x)            (now: 1/(1 + x))
  Cancel[4/(4 + 8 x)]      -> 4/(4 + 8 x)            (now: 1/(1 + 2 x))
  Cancel[4 x/(4 + 8 x)]    -> (4 x)/(4 + 8 x)        (now: x/(1 + 2 x))

Root cause: the j-loop that peels integer content into `num_i` only
fired on `is_number(base)` factors of the bp-decomposition.  For an
input like `4 + 4 x` the bp had a single Plus factor (`Plus[4, 4 x]`,
exp=1); `is_number(Plus[...])` is false, so `num_i` stayed at 1.  The
asymmetry meant `PolynomialGCD[4, 4 + 4 x]` returned 1 (rather than 4),
and `Cancel` then refused to reduce.

Two cooperating edits in `src/poly.c`:

1. `get_int_content` extends to Plus expressions: returns the GCD of
   summand contents, with a short-circuit at 1.

2. The j-loop in `builtin_polynomialgcd` gains a Plus-base branch.
   When a bp factor is `Plus[...]` with integer content `c > 1`, it
   accumulates `c` into `num_i` AND replaces the base with its
   primitive part `Plus[a_i / c]` so the downstream `poly_gcd_internal`
   does not extract the same content again (which would multiply numG
   by the factor twice -- causing
   `PolynomialGCD[4 + 4 x, 8 + 8 x]` to incorrectly return
   `(4 + 4 x) * 4` instead of `4 + 4 x`).

Verified on Cancel cases above plus the existing
`Cancel[(4 + 4 x)/(8 + 8 x)] -> 1/2` regression (still passes).  All
`poly`, `rat`, `parfrac`, `facpoly`, `intrat`, `simp`, `simplify`,
`expand`, `deriv` test suites pass.

## intrat: prefer intrat_simp_pos_sqrt over Simplify for Sophie-Germain roots (2026-05-11)

Replaced two `Simplify[Sqrt[...]]` calls in `logtoreal_dispatch`'s
Sophie-Germain branch with direct calls to `intrat_simp_pos_sqrt`.
Simplify alone leaves `Sqrt[1/(256 a^12)]` un-reduced; the helper
walks Times factors under the positive-symbol assumption and collapses
it to `1/(16 a^6)` (and similarly `Sqrt[2 * 1/(16 a^6)] -> 1/(2 a^3)`).

The visible effect on the user-reported parametric biquadratic family:

  Integrate`BronsteinRational[1/(x^4 + a^4), x]
    -> 1/2 ArcTan[(a + Sqrt[2] x)/a]/(Sqrt[2] a^3)
       + 1/2 ArcTan[(-a + Sqrt[2] x)/a]/(Sqrt[2] a^3)
       + 1/4 Log[Sqrt[2] a x + a^2 + x^2]/(Sqrt[2] a^3)
       - 1/4 Log[-Sqrt[2] a x + a^2 + x^2]/(Sqrt[2] a^3)

(LeafCount 117 vs ~300 with the held nested-Sqrt form).  Crucially,
`Simplify[Together[D[result, x] - 1/(x^4 + a^4)]] == 0` now succeeds
where it previously returned the unreduced 318-leaf nested-Sqrt
diff; the canonicalisation made `Together` self-cancel.

## simp: Simplify rational pipeline tries Factor on already-cancelled inputs (2026-05-11)

`simp_pipeline_rational` only ran the Factor candidate against the
Cancel'd form `cn`, so when Cancel returned NULL (input already in
lowest terms) Factor was never tried.  This left Simplify unable to
reduce inputs like `x/(x^3 + a b + a x + b x^2)` whose Factor'd form
`x/((a + x^2) (b + x))` has lower LeafCount.

Two related edits in `src/simp.c`:

1. Factor branch now falls through to `tg ? tg : seed` when `cn` is
   NULL, so it always runs against the most-canonical form available.
   Same fall-through for the per-variable Collect candidate.

2. Push a NULL `factor_memo` around the Factor call so it uses its
   normal (separate num/den variable lists) behaviour rather than the
   inside-Simplify combined-scope path.  The combined-scope mode
   refuses to factor parametric denominators like
   `x^3 + a b + a x + b x^2` (univariate-in-x with parametric
   coefficients in {a, b}).  Direct user `Factor[expr]` already used
   the separate-scope mode -- this aligns Simplify's Factor candidate
   with the user-visible Factor.  The lessons-md `simp_factorial`
   workaround uses the same trick.

Visible effect:

  Simplify[x/(x^3 + a b + a x + b x^2)]
  -> x/((a + x^2) (b + x))    (was: input unchanged, LC 19 -> LC 14)

  Simplify[D[Integrate`BronsteinRational[x/((x^2 + a) (x + b)), x], x]]
  -> x/((a + x^2) (b + x))    (was: x/(x^3 + a b + a x + b x^2))

All `poly`, `rat`, `parfrac`, `facpoly`, `intrat`, `simp`, `simplify`,
`expand`, `deriv`, `factorial_simplify`, `collect_corpus` test suites
pass.  Pre-existing 5 main-branch failures (`linalg`, `list_tests`
Min-bug, `parfrac` Apart factoring, `polymod` print format,
`extension_options` Apart-with-Extension format) unchanged.

## power: principal-value evaluation for Power[I, n/2] and Power[-I, n/2] (2026-05-11)

`Sqrt[I]`, `Sqrt[-I]`, `(I)^(3/2)`, `(-I)^(3/2)` previously stayed as
opaque held Powers, leaving downstream Simplify unable to canonicalise
expressions like

  Log[Sqrt[I] + x] / (I)^(3/2)

that intrat emits when the LRT pipeline closes a quartic factor over
the complex linear extension (e.g. for the irreducible `x^4 + 1`
factor inside `x^3/((x-1)^2 (x^4+1))`).

Added a symbolic principal-value branch in `src/power.c`'s Power
evaluator that fires before the cpow numeric path:

  Sqrt[I]      = (1 + I) / Sqrt[2]
  Sqrt[-I]     = (1 - I) / Sqrt[2]
  (I)^(3/2)    = (-1 + I) / Sqrt[2]
  (-I)^(3/2)   = (-1 - I) / Sqrt[2]

(Standard principal branch from arg = atan2(im, re), exponent
n/2 reduced mod 4 to {0, 1, 2, 3}; even residues fall through to the
existing integer-power path.)

Visible effect:

  Sqrt[I]                     -> (1 + I)/Sqrt[2]
  Simplify[D[Integrate[x^3/(x^6 - 2 x^5 + x^4 + x^2 - 2 x + 1), x], x]]
                              -> x^3/((-1 + x)^2 (1 + x^4))
                                 (LeafCount 16, was 146 with held
                                  (I)^(3/2) blockers)

The integral itself is still emitted in complex-Log form (intrat's
LRT pipeline routes parametric-numerator `f/(x^4 + 1)` through the
linear-Q closer rather than the Sophie-Germain real-quadratic path,
which only fires on `c4 t^4 + c0` Q polynomials).  Closing the
parametric-numerator quartic via real form is task #6 (cyclotomic /
irreducible-real RootSum closure), out of scope for this commit.

All `poly`, `rat`, `parfrac`, `facpoly`, `intrat`, `simp`, `simplify`,
`expand`, `deriv`, `power_corpus`, `numeric` test suites pass.

## intrat: empty LRT pair list returns NULL (silent wrong-zero fix) (2026-05-11)

`intrat_log_to_real_pairs` and `intrat_linear_q_closer` returned
`Integer[0]` when the LRT pair list was empty.  But an empty pair
list means the LRT producer could not decompose the input (denominator
irreducible over the working ring) -- *not* that the integral is zero.
The `Integer[0]` then propagated up through `try_lrt_close`,
short-circuiting the universal NaiveLogPart fallback, and the user saw

  Integrate`BronsteinRational[x^3/(-1 - x^8 + x^16), x]   -> 0    (WRONG)

Both consumers now return NULL on empty pair list, allowing
`try_lrt_close` to fall through to the NaiveLogPart RootSum form.
The case above now correctly returns

  RootSum[Function[-1 - #1^8 + #1^16],
          Function[Log[x - #1] #1^3/(-8 #1^7 + 16 #1^15)]]

(differentiates back to the integrand under positive-symbol
assumption; verified num-diff = 0 at x = 7/4).

Pre-existing wrong-answer regression on `IntegrateRationalTests` case 33
is now correct.  Case 46 (degree-16 squared denominator) still
produces a wrong result -- separate bug, likely in the Hermite
reduction or derivative-recognition for the squared part.

## intrat: closed-form completions for five RootSum-leak inputs (2026-05-11)

Five `Integrate`BronsteinRational[...]` inputs reported as still
returning unevaluated `RootSum` (or otherwise unsimplified) now
close to real-elementary form:

  1.  `1/(b - a x^3)`                          (cubic / nth-root w. params)
  2.  `1/(x^5 + 1)`                            (palindromic-quartic Q)
  3.  `x^4/(a + b x^3)^2`                      (Hermite-reduced cubic)
  4.  `(-1 + x^2)/(1 - 2 x^2 + 2 x^4)`         (biquadratic Q, neg. inner disc)
  5.  `1/x/(1 - 2 x^2 + 2 x^4)`                (post-processing distribution)

Each issue corresponded to a distinct gap in the C port's
`logtoreal_dispatch` / `expand_simple_rootsum` / final-cleanup
chain.  The five fixes are independent:

**Phase A — output post-processing.**  Two new passes in
`intrat_integrate_rational`:

  -  `intrat_distribute_plus(e)` calls `expr_expand` to flatten
     `Times[scalar, Plus[…]]` that the per-summand `c_k · piece_int_k`
     accumulator leaves held (Times has no built-in Plus-distribution
     attribute).
  -  `intrat_strip_log_constants(e, x)` rewrites `Log[c · p]` to
     `Log[p]` whenever `FreeQ[c, x]`.  The `Log[c]` summand is a
     constant of integration, harmless to drop, and the stripping
     lets the downstream `intrat_log_to_arctanh` pairing rule fire
     across previously-blocked term boundaries.

Both passes run before AND after `intrat_log_to_arctanh` so the
log-pairing rule sees fully-distributed sums and any newly-formed
`Times[scalar, Plus[…]]` from the pairing is re-distributed.

Fix for issue 5.

**Phase B — Sophie-Germain-with-c2 for biquadratic with negative
inner discriminant.**  `logtoreal_dispatch` deg-4 `c1z && c3z`
branch previously bailed when `c2^2 − 4 c0 c4 < 0`; now it falls
into a new sub-branch that factors

    c4 t^4 + c2 t^2 + c0
       = c4 (t^2 + α t + β)(t^2 − α t + β)

with `β = Sqrt[c0/c4]` and `α = Sqrt[2 β − c2/c4]`, both real under
the negative-inner-disc regime (algebraically: `c2^2 < 4 c0 c4`
forces `2 Sqrt[c0 c4] > |c2|`, hence `2 Sqrt[c0/c4] − c2/c4 > 0` when
`c4 > 0`).  Each real-coefficient quadratic factor has discriminant
`α^2 − 4 β < 0`, dispatching through `logtoreal_quadratic`'s ArcTan
branch.

Fix for issue 4.

**Phase C — cubic dispatch in `logtoreal_dispatch`.**  New deg-3
branch for nth-root cubics `c3 t^3 + c0` (c1 = c2 = 0): real root
`r0 = −(c0/c3)^(1/3)` (principal real cube root, sign-selected by
`intrat_sign_pos_assumption` so positive-symbol parameters route
correctly).  Factor as

    c3 (t − r0)(t^2 + r0 t + r0^2)

and dispatch the linear factor through `build_log_term` and the
quadratic through `logtoreal_quadratic` (discriminant `−3 r0^2 < 0`,
always ArcTan branch).

Fix for issues 1 and 3.  Non-depressed cubics (`c1` or `c2` non-zero)
remain unhandled — Cardano's formula port is a future extension.

**Phase D2 — palindromic-quartic real-form expansion in
NaiveLogPart.**  New helper `expand_palindromic_quartic_real`
detects palindromic `d_t = c0 t^4 + c1 t^3 + c2 t^2 + c1 t + c0`
(c0 == c4, c1 == c3), solves the `u = t + 1/t` substitution
`c0 u^2 + c1 u + (c2 − 2 c0) = 0` for u_±, and for each conjugate
root pair `α_k = u_k/2 ± i Sqrt[(4 − u_k^2)/4]` builds the real
contribution directly:

    C_re · Log[(x − u_k/2)^2 + (4 − u_k^2)/4]
       + 2 C_im · ArcTan[Sqrt[(4 − u_k^2)/4] / (x − u_k/2)]

where `C = a(α_k) / d'(α_k) = C_re + i C_im` is split via the
existing `split_re_im` helper.  This bypasses the LogToReal /
LogToAtan chain entirely, which otherwise overwhelms on the
nested-radical S polynomials from the scaled-palindromic LRT path.

Fix for issue 2.

**Soundness gates.**  Every new sign decision is gated through
`intrat_sign_pos_assumption` first (symbolic positive-symbol walk),
then a fresh `intrat_numeric_sign` helper that runs `N[expr]` for
expressions like `Sqrt[5] − 5` that the symbolic walker leaves at
sign-unknown but a numerical sample resolves cleanly.  Failure to
decide a sign always falls through to the held-`RootSum` form
rather than risking a silent miscomputation.

**Tests.**  `tests/test_intrat.c` adds five regressions
(`test_closed_cubic_params`, `test_closed_quintic_one`,
`test_closed_x4_over_cubic_sq`, `test_closed_biquadratic_neg_disc`,
`test_closed_coefficient_distribution`).  Each asserts (a) the
result has no `RootSum` / `Function` head leak and (b) the
derivative matches the integrand — either symbolically via
`Cancel[Together[…]]` (issue 5, where the printed form is exact)
or numerically via `N[…]` at 1–3 sample points (issues 1–4, whose
nested-radical results aren't reducible to literal zero by
Mathilda's current simplifier).

## intrat: general nth-root cyclotomic factorisation in logtoreal_dispatch (2026-05-11)

Replaces the deg-3 nth-root and deg-4 Sophie-Germain shortcuts in
`logtoreal_dispatch` with a single sparse-polynomial handler
`logtoreal_nthroot_sparse(base, deg, s, x, t)` that closes
`c_n t^n + c_0` (all intermediate coefficients zero) for every
n ≥ 3.

**Motivation.**  The 2026-05-11 Phase-C cubic fix only handled
`c_3 t^3 + c_0`.  Nearby inputs like `1/(b - a x^4)`,
`1/(b - a x^5)`, `1/(b - a x^6)`, `1/(b + a x^6)`, `1/(b + a x^8)`,
`1/(b + a x^9)` all still produced `RootSum[Function[…], …]`
because their LRT-Q polynomials are sparse nth-root forms with
n ∉ {3} or the Sophie-Germain n = 4, q > 0 case.  Each of them is
factorable in real closed form via the standard cyclotomic
decomposition; the C port just wasn't doing it.

**Algorithm.**  For `c_n t^n + c_0` let `q = −c_0 / c_n`.

  -  If `q > 0`: roots are `r · exp(2π i k / n)` for k = 0..n−1
     with `r = q^(1/n) > 0`.  Real roots are `t = r` (always) and
     `t = −r` when n is even.  Complex pairs are indexed
     k = 1..⌊(n−1)/2⌋ (skipping k = n/2 when n even); the matching
     conjugate is at index `n − k`.

  -  If `q < 0`: roots are `r · exp((2k+1) π i / n)` for k = 0..n−1
     with `r = |q|^(1/n) > 0`.  Real root `t = −r` exists only for
     odd n (at k = (n−1)/2, angle π).  Complex pairs are k = 0..⌊(n−2)/2⌋
     with the matching conjugate at `n − 1 − k` (skipping the real
     root index when n is odd).

Each complex pair contributes a real quadratic factor
`t^2 − 2 r cos(θ_k) t + r^2` whose discriminant
`−4 r^2 sin^2 θ_k` is always strictly negative, so the ArcTan
branch of `logtoreal_quadratic` always fires.  Mathilda evaluates
`Cos[k π / n]` to closed radical form for the cyclotomically nice
n (3, 4, 5, 6, 10, 12, …); for other n (8, 9, 11, …) the `Cos`
remains held but the result is still real-elementary (no `RootSum`
or `Function` leak).

**Sign selection.**  The branch fires when
`intrat_sign_pos_assumption(q)` is definite, falling back to
`intrat_numeric_sign(q)` (an `N[]`-based decision with a 1e-12
dead zone).  Both gates undecidable ⇒ bail to the held-`RootSum`
form — sound under all sign instances.

**Subsumes.**  The previous deg-3 nth-root branch and the deg-4
Sophie-Germain (c_1 = c_2 = c_3 = 0) branch are now removed.
The deg-4 biquadratic (c_1 = c_3 = 0, c_2 ≠ 0) and palindromic
sub-branches are kept for non-sparse quartics.  Behaviour for
inputs the old branches handled is unchanged.

**Tests.**  `tests/test_intrat.c` adds six new regressions
(`test_closed_nth_root_quartic_minus` / `_quintic_minus` /
`_sextic_minus` / `_sextic_plus` / `_octic_plus` /
`_nonic_plus`).  Each asserts no `RootSum` / `Function` head and
numerically verifies the derivative at two sample points.

**Regression risk.**  Full test suite shows 90 pass / 15 fail both
before and after this change — identical failure set (canonical-
ordering pre-existing failures from commit `cc8b164`).  Zero new
regressions.

## algebraic: automatic extension detection across Together / Cancel / polynomial functions (2026-05-13)

`Extension -> Automatic` on the rational-function and polynomial
builtins now scans the input for algebraic-number generators of the
form `Power[c, p/q]` (integer base `c`, |c| ≥ 2) and `Sqrt[c]` and
routes through the existing Q(α)[x] substrate
(`src/qa.c` / `src/qaupoly.c` / `src/qafactor.c`).  Same-base
generators are merged by LCM of exponent denominators — an input
containing both `Power[2, 1/3]` and `Power[2, 1/2]` resolves to a
single generator `2^(1/6)` of degree 6.

Previously `Extension -> Automatic` was silently treated as
`Extension -> None`; users had to write the generator explicitly
(`Extension -> Power[2, 1/3]`) to invoke the Q(α)-aware path.

**Affected builtins** (auto-detect runs when the user passes
`Extension -> Automatic`):

- `Cancel`, `Together`  (`src/rat.c`).
- `PolynomialGCD`, `PolynomialLCM`  (`src/poly.c`).
- `PolynomialQuotient`, `PolynomialRemainder`,
  `PolynomialQuotientRemainder`  (`src/poly.c`).
- `Apart`  (`src/parfrac.c`).
- `Factor`  (`src/facpoly.c`).

**New API surface** (`src/qafactor.{h,c}`, `src/options.{h,c}`):

- `QATower* extension_autodetect(const Expr* e)` — walk one
  expression and build the corresponding compositum tower.
- `QATower* extension_autodetect_args(Expr* const* args, size_t n)`
  — walk an array (used by builtins that take multiple polynomial
  args).
- `extract_extension_option_full(res, &argc, &automatic_out)` —
  variant of `extract_extension_option` that distinguishes
  `Extension -> Automatic` from `Extension -> None` and the absence
  of any `Extension` option.  The legacy `extract_extension_option`
  continues to treat both `None` and `Automatic` as "no extension"
  so existing callers are unaffected.

**Limitations (tier 1).**

- Auto-detect only finds generators *present in the input*
  expression.  `Factor[x^3 - 2, Extension -> Automatic]` does NOT
  split, because `x^3 - 2` has no radical sub-expression —
  discovering that it has a root at 2^(1/3) is a separate
  root-finding problem.
- Non-integer base (rational, polynomial, nested-radical) under a
  fractional exponent bails the detector.  `Sqrt[x+1]` and
  `Sqrt[2^(1/3)/6]` both cause auto-detect to return NULL.
- Multi-generator towers with n ≥ 2 are detected but currently fall
  back to the no-extension path (tier-2 work).

**Tests.**

- `tests/test_extension_autodetect.c` — 18 unit tests covering
  generator collection, LCM merging, multi-base towers, and bail
  paths.
- `tests/test_extension_auto_builtins.c` — 17 integration tests
  asserting `Extension -> Automatic` matches the explicit
  `Extension -> α` form on Cancel, Together, Apart, Factor, and the
  five PolynomialGCD/LCM/Quotient/Remainder/QuotientRemainder
  builtins.

**Regression risk.**  Full test suite 93 pass / 16 fail (vs the
baseline 92 pass / 16 fail — identical failure set, one new passing
binary for the integration tests above).  Zero new regressions.

## simp_algebraic: cube-root and higher-order generators (2026-05-13)

`Simplify` now handles single-generator algebraic radicals of arbitrary
order (`Power[c, p/q]` with q ≥ 2), not just square roots.  Previously
`simp_algebraic` (`src/simp.c`) bailed on any `q != 2` because its
rationalisation step (`alg_sigma_negate`) only handles the q = 2 case
(sign-flip conjugate).

The new path is a small shortcut at the top of `simp_algebraic_impl`:
when `extension_autodetect` returns a single-generator tower, route
through `Together[expr, Extension -> α]` instead.  Together's
extension path uses the existing qaupoly substrate
(`qaupoly_gcd` / `qaupoly_divrem`), which handles q ≥ 2 natively via
the Q(α)[x] minimal-polynomial reduction.

**Worked examples** that now collapse under `Simplify`:

```
Simplify[Power[2, 1/3] Power[2, 2/3]]                     → 2
Simplify[(1 + Power[2, 1/3] + Power[2, 2/3]) (Power[2, 1/3] - 1)]
                                                          → 1
Simplify[(x^3 - 2)/(x - Power[2, 1/3])]                   → 2^(2/3) + 2^(1/3) x + x^2
Simplify[Power[5, 1/4] Power[5, 3/4]]                     → 5
Simplify[Power[Power[5, 1/4], 2]]                         → Sqrt[5]
```

The Phase B Sqrt-only multi-generator path (alg_sigma_negate
rationalisation) is retained unchanged as the fallback — only the
single-generator case is intercepted by the new shortcut, and the
complexity gate ensures the original input is returned on a tie or
regression.

**Tests.**  `tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c` — 9 new tests
covering cube and quartic roots, the minimum polynomial identity
`(α^2 + α + 1)(α - 1) = α^3 - 1 = 1` over Q(2^(1/3)), and the q = 2
regression cases.

**Regression risk.**  Full test suite 93 pass / 16 fail (identical
failure set; one new passing test binary for the cube-root tests
above; the Phase B integration-test binary remains in the pass set
unchanged).  Zero new regressions.

## algebraic: nested-radical generators in extension_autodetect (2026-05-13)

`extension_autodetect` (`src/qafactor.c`) previously bailed on any
`Power[base, p/q]` whose base wasn't an integer literal — meaning
`Sqrt[1 + Sqrt[2]]`, `Sqrt[2^(1/3)]`, and similar nested radicals
caused the entire detection to return NULL.

The walker now surfaces nested radicals as a separate `GEN_NESTED`
generator class, deferring resolution to `qa_resolve_nested_radical`
(Phase G8 in `src/qafactor.c`).  Integer-base generators (the original
`GEN_INT_BASE` class) are unchanged.

Concretely:

```
Sqrt[1 + Sqrt[2]]            → 1 generator, deg 4 (compositum minpoly y^4 - 2 y^2 - 1)
Sqrt[2^(1/3)]                → 1 generator, deg 6 (= 2^(1/6))
```

And in the `Simplify` pipeline:

```
Simplify[Sqrt[1 + Sqrt[2]]^2]            → 1 + Sqrt[2]
Simplify[(Sqrt[2^(1/3)])^2]              → 2^(1/3)
Simplify[Sqrt[2^(1/3)/6] Sqrt[2^(1/3)/6]] → 1/(3 2^(2/3))
```

**Design note.**  The walker does NOT recurse into a nested radical's
base.  `Sqrt[1 + Sqrt[2]]` does not also surface `Sqrt[2]` as a
separate generator — G8 builds its own sub-tower from the base's
atomic radicals.  Recursing would double-count the inner radical and
inflate the compositum degree.

**Limitations remaining.**

- Structural-equality dedup only: two nested radicals that are
  mathematically equal but written differently (e.g.
  `Sqrt[-1/9·2^(-2/3) + 2/9·2^(1/3)]` vs `Sqrt[1/(3·2^(2/3))]`, both
  equal `Sqrt[2^(1/3)/6]`) are still treated as distinct generators.
  Mathematical-equality dedup would require a canonical-form pass
  over the radicand before generator collection.
- Multi-generator detection (n ≥ 2) still bails at the Cancel/Together
  wiring layer to no-extension — tier-2 work to route towers through
  the qaupoly substrate end-to-end.

**Tests.**  Extends `tests/test_extension_autodetect.c` (2 new tests:
`test_sqrt_of_sqrt`, `test_sqrt_of_cbrt`) and
`tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c` (3 new tests:
`test_nested_sqrt_squared`, `test_sqrt_of_cbrt_squared`,
`test_sqrt_of_cbrt_quotient_squared`).

**Regression risk.**  Full test suite 94 pass / 16 fail (identical
failure set, one further new passing test from the cube-root binary
that incorporates these tests).  Zero new regressions.

## algebraic: multi-generator tower routing for Cancel / Together (2026-05-13)

`qa_cancel_with_tower` (`src/qafactor.{c,h}`) is a new public helper
that handles the n ≥ 2 case of `extension_autodetect`.  When the
input contains multiple independent algebraic generators (e.g.
`Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3]`), the helper:

1. Substitutes each user-side α_i in the input with its polynomial-
   in-γ form (where γ is the tower's primitive element).
2. Runs the standard `Together` to combine into a single fraction.
3. Lifts numerator and denominator to QAUPoly over Q(γ).
4. Divides by their `qaupoly_gcd`.
5. Renders back through `qaupoly_to_expr_alpha` with γ's surface
   form.

Wired into both `builtin_cancel` and `builtin_together` (`src/rat.c`)
under `Extension -> Automatic`.  Previously these fell through to the
no-extension path on multi-generator detection.

**Worked example** that now collapses end-to-end:

```
Cancel[(Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3]) (Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3]), Extension -> Automatic]
   →  -1
```

Direct evaluation expands to `2 - 3 = -1`; the qa_cancel_with_tower
path reaches the same answer through the Q(γ) lift + qaupoly_gcd.

**Limitations.**

- The render-back step uses γ as the surface "α" so results sometimes
  expose `γ` as `Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3]` (or whatever the primitive element
  is) inside the rational form.  Mathematical equivalence is preserved;
  cosmetic minimisation (re-expressing γ-polynomials in terms of the
  user's original α_i basis) is not yet done.
- Lift failures (a coefficient that isn't in Q(γ)) cleanly return
  NULL and fall back to the no-extension path.

**Tests.**  `tests/test_extension_auto_builtins.c` adds 2 new tests
(`test_multigen_sqrt2_sqrt3_collapse`, `test_multigen_together_no_op`).

**Regression risk.**  Full test suite still 94 pass / 16 fail —
identical failure set.  Zero new regressions.

## algebraic: canonical-form dedup of nested radicals (2026-05-13)

`extension_autodetect` now runs a post-walker canonicalisation pass on
nested-radical generators (`GEN_NESTED`).  Each radicand is rewritten
via `Together[radicand, Extension -> α]` against the surfaced
integer-base generators, then re-split into atomic radicals (so that
`Power[c, p/q]` with `|p| > 1` is rewritten as
`c^floor(p/q) · Power[c, (p mod q)/q]`).  After canonicalisation,
structurally-distinct-but-mathematically-equal `Sqrt[u]` terms collapse
to a single generator.

Surfacing integer bases from inside a nested radicand's base is done
via a dedicated `autodetect_walk_intbase_only` sub-walker that ONLY
collects non-atomic `Power[c, p/q]` (p != 1) forms.  Atomic
`Power[c, 1/q]` / `Sqrt[c]` sub-expressions are deliberately skipped —
G8's nested-radical resolver already handles them via its own
sub-tower, and surfacing them again at the top level created a
redundant degree-doubling compositum (regression test:
`Sqrt[1+Sqrt[2]]` correctly resolves to a single generator of
degree 4, not 8).

**Worked example.**  Two structurally distinct but mathematically
equal nested Sqrts now compare equal under `Simplify`:

```
Simplify[Sqrt[-1/9/2^(2/3) + 2/9 2^(1/3)] - Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)]]   →  0
```

(Both radicands canonicalise to `1/3·2^(-2/3)` so the two Sqrts dedup
to a single GEN_NESTED generator, and Simplify's complexity-driven
search drives the difference to zero.)

**Limitations remaining.**

- The motivating end-to-end case (the derivative of `Integrate[a x /
  (x^3 + 2), x]` collapsing to `a x^2 / (x^3 + 2)`) still doesn't
  close: even after canonicalising both radicands to identical
  `Sqrt[1/3·2^(-2/3)]`, G8's `expr_is_atomic_algebraic` recogniser
  rejects `Power[2, -2/3]` inside the radicand (it only accepts
  `Power[c, 1/n]`).  The deeper reason is that Mathilda's Times
  canonicaliser (`src/times.c` around line 481) deliberately
  absorbs integer coefficient factors into Power exponents — for
  example `(1/6)·2^(1/3)` is canonicalised to `(1/3)·2^(-2/3)`,
  pulling the factor of 2 in the `1/6 = 1/(2·3)` denominator into
  the radical's exponent.  This is Mathilda's chosen canonical form
  and is referenced widely, so the right fix is to extend the
  qa-substrate (`qa_resolve_extension` and
  `qa_expr_to_qaupoly_with_alpha`) to accept `Power[c, p/q]` for any
  integer `p`, lifting it as the polynomial-in-α form via
  `qa_inverse` for negative exponents.  Deferred as a multi-hundred-
  LoC substrate change for follow-up.

**Tests.**  `tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c` adds 1 new test
(`test_canon_dedup_equal_radicands_subtract`).

**Regression risk.**  Full test suite still 94 pass / 16 fail —
identical failure set.  Zero new regressions.

## qa substrate — Power[c, p/q] for general integer p (2026-05-13)

Extends `qa_resolve_extension` (`src/qafactor.c`),
`expr_is_atomic_algebraic` (G8 atom recogniser), and the QAUPoly lift
(`qa_expr_to_qaupoly_with_alpha`) to accept `Power[c, p/q]` with any
integer `p` (previously only `p == 1`).  This is the substrate fix
that lets Mathilda's Times-canonicaliser-produced forms like
`Power[2, -2/3]` participate in algebraic-extension reasoning.

### A. Recogniser broadening

After gcd-reducing `p/q` to lowest terms `p_red/q_red`, the recogniser
and resolver now accept any `q_red >= 2` with integer base `|c| >= 2`.
`qa_resolve_extension` returns a QAExt for `y^q_red - c` with
`*render_out` set to the natural form `Power[c, 1/q_red]` (or
`Sqrt[c]` when the user originally typed `Sqrt[c]` with `p == 1` for
byte-for-byte compatibility with existing tests).

### B. Lift inputs containing `Power[c, p/q]`

New helper `qa_alpha_power_signed(ext, p)` in `qa.{c,h}`: computes α^p
∈ Q(α) for any integer p, using `qa_inverse` for `p < 0` and
repeated-squaring for efficiency.

New helper `expand_radicals_to_atomic_poly` in `qafactor.c`: rewrites
every `Power[c_base, p/q]` whose reduced denominator divides
`q_natural` into the polynomial-in-`alpha_sym` form representing α^k,
where α = c_base^(1/q_natural).  Raw structural rewrite — does NOT
call `evaluate()` so Mathilda's Times canonicaliser doesn't undo it.

`qa_expr_to_qaupoly_with_alpha` infers `(c_base, q_natural)` from the
QAExt's `y^q - c` shape and runs `expand_radicals_to_atomic_poly`
before the existing `alpha_render → alpha_sym` substitution.  G8's
`qa_resolve_nested_radical` and `qa_cancel_with_tower` both also run
the expand pass per-α_i before substituting α_i into γ.

### C. Complexity gate in `qa_cancel_with_tower`

When the compositum's primitive element γ is a sum of generators,
rendering Q(γ)-polynomials in user-α form can produce expressions
much larger than the input.  Added a `leaf_count_internal`-based gate
at both the variable-bearing and no-variable return paths: return
NULL when the candidate output exceeds the input by leaf count, so
the caller falls back.  `leaf_count_internal` is now exposed via
`core.h` for this purpose.

### D. Proper Q(γ)-arithmetic in the no-variable path

For Q(γ)-constant inputs, the previous implementation substituted
`γ_internal → γ_render` into the intermediate polynomial form,
producing high-degree user-form polynomials.  The new path reduces
num/den modulo γ's minimal polynomial via `PolynomialRemainder`,
lifts each to a QAUPoly with a dummy variable, extracts the QANum
constant, divides via `qa_div` (real Q(γ)-arithmetic), and renders
the canonical QANum's coefficient array.  Result:
`Cancel[(Sqrt[2]+Sqrt[3])(Sqrt[2]-Sqrt[3]), Extension -> Automatic]`
now produces `-1` instead of the degree-16 γ-polynomial expansion.

### Worked examples

```
Cancel[Power[2, -2/3] x^2 - x/Power[2, 1/3], Extension -> Power[2, 1/3]]
   → 1/2 (-2^(2/3) x + 2^(1/3) x^2)

Cancel[(Sqrt[2] + Sqrt[3])(Sqrt[2] - Sqrt[3]), Extension -> Automatic]
   → -1
```

### E. Input-side radicand canonicalisation

`canonicalise_nested_radicands(e, c_base, q_natural)` walks `e` and
rewrites every `Sqrt[u]` / `Power[u, p/q]` whose base `u` is a
non-integer expression mentioning `c_base` by canonicalising `u` via
`Together[u, Extension -> Power[c_base, 1/q_natural]]`.  This is the
input-side counterpart of Phase F's `autodetect_canonicalise_post`
(which canonicalised the generator-set surface forms).  Without it,
`Together[Sqrt[A] - Sqrt[B], Extension -> Automatic]` with `A == B`
mathematically (but structurally distinct) missed one of the Sqrts at
substitution time.

Step 0 of `qa_cancel_with_tower` runs this pass against each
integer-base generator in the tower (`Power[c, 1/q]` or `Sqrt[c]` with
`|c| >= 2`) before the user-α → polynomial-in-γ substitution loop.

`autodetect_canonicalise_post` was also generalised: it now handles
both `Sqrt[radicand]` (1-arg) and `Power[radicand, p/q]` surface forms
and rebuilds every nested generator's render with a positive `1/q`
exponent.  This collapses the `Power[X, -1/q]` shape that Mathilda's
Power canonicaliser produces (e.g. from `1/Sqrt[X]`) into the same
canonical generator as `Sqrt[X]` / `Power[X, 1/q]`, so the autodetect
dedup pass merges them.

A zero-numerator shortcut was added at the Q(γ)-constant return path:
when the QAUPoly numerator is zero (regardless of denominator
representation), return `0` directly instead of running it through
`qa_div`.  Required because the input-side canonicalisation can now
turn `Sqrt[A] - Sqrt[B]` into a literal `0` before the tower lift, and
the previous path bailed when the polynomial form was zero.

### Worked example

```
Together[Sqrt[-1/9/2^(2/3) + 2/9 2^(1/3)] - Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)],
         Extension -> Automatic]
   → 0
```

### Limitations remaining

- `Together[D[Integrate[a x/(x^3+2), x], x], Extension -> Automatic]`
  still produces a non-collapsed form containing `Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)]`
  embedded in arithmetic.  Closing this requires factoring the integer
  power out of nested radicands so that `Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)]` is
  recognised as `Sqrt[3]/(3·2^(1/3))`, putting `Sqrt[3]` and `2^(1/3)`
  into the autodetected generator set rather than the opaque
  `Sqrt[1/3/2^(2/3)]`.

### Tests

`tests/test_simp_algebraic_cuberoot.c` adds 3 new tests
(`test_power_neg_pq_lift`, `test_multigen_qgamma_constant_collapse`,
`test_together_equal_nested_radicals`).

### Regression risk

Full test suite 96 pass / 14 fail — identical pre-existing failure
set.  Zero new regressions.

A separate finding: `assert_eval_eq` in `tests/test_utils.h` uses
lowercase `assert()` which is elided under the CMake `Release`
build's `-DNDEBUG`.  Mismatches in tests using this helper have
been silently passing.  A strict-assert experiment surfaced 5
pre-existing latent failures unrelated to this work; addressing them
needs a separate cleanup commit.

## sort: order-independent variable collection in expr_compare (2026-05-15)

`expr_compare` (the canonical comparator that drives `Sort`,
`OrderedQ`, and every Orderless-attribute Plus/Times sort in the
evaluator) was silently truncating its variable-collection buffer at
64 distinct symbol names.  The comment claimed both sides saw the
same truncated set; in fact `collect_symbols_in` early-exited as soon
as the buffer filled, so collection from `a` could fill the buffer
and leave none of `b`'s unique symbols represented.  The result was
an asymmetric comparator: `compare(A, B)` and `compare(B, A)` could
both return `1`, violating qsort's antisymmetry contract.

### Symptom

Inputs that build large polynomial ansatzes (e.g.,
`Integrate\`RischNorman` candidates with hundreds of unknowns alongside
a small log-bearing term) hit `$IterationLimit exceeded`.  The
top-level `Plus` containing the polynomial and the log term sorted
its args one way on one iteration, the opposite way the next, and
the evaluator's fixed-point loop oscillated until the 4096-iteration
cap fired.  The eventual returned answer was still correct (the
oscillation was purely cosmetic re-ordering of Plus args), but the
warning was alarming and 4096 wasted iterations were burning real
cycles.

### Fix

`src/sort.c`: replace the fixed `const char* vars[64]` with a
growable `SymSet` (stack buffer for the common ≤64-symbol case, heap
fallback that doubles on demand).  `collect_symbols_in` now never
truncates; the resulting variable set is always `vars(a) ∪ vars(b)`
regardless of argument order, restoring antisymmetry.

### Verification

- Repro: `Integrate\`RischNorman[((1 + x + x Exp[x])(x + Log[x] +
  Exp[x] - 1))/(x (Log[x] + Exp[x] + x)^2), x]` no longer prints
  `$IterationLimit exceeded`; result unchanged (`Log[x + E^x + Log[x]]
  + 1/(x + E^x + Log[x])`).
- 52-case `bench_intrischnorman` corpus: 1.33 s best-of-3, same
  range as the prior 1.23 s baseline (within run-to-run noise).
- Full 116-binary test suite: 116/116 pass.

## eval: hold LHS args of Set/SetDelayed that contain pattern constructs (2026-05-15)

### Problem

Calling `Integrate[1/(x^2 - 1)^3, x, Method -> "CRCTable"]` for the
first time triggered the lazy `Get` of
`src/internal/CRCMathTablesIntegrals.m` and printed several
`SetDelayed::wrsym: Symbol Times is Protected` / `Symbol Plus is
Protected` diagnostics before returning the integrand unevaluated.

Root cause: the Set/SetDelayed dispatcher (`src/eval.c`) evaluates the
arguments of the LHS to support `f[x] = 1` (with `x = c` →
`f[c] = 1`).  But that evaluation also runs the generic evaluator on
pattern-bearing LHSes such as
`IntegrateTable[1/(x_ Sqrt[x_^2 - a_^2]), x_]`.  An earlier rule

```
IntegrateTable[1/x_ Power[b_. x_^2 + a_, -1/2], x_]
    := -ArcTanh[Sqrt[b x^2 + a]/Sqrt[a]]/Sqrt[a]
```

matches the held pattern (binding `b = 1`, `a = -a^2`) and rewrites the
LHS into a `Times[...]`-headed expression.  `apply_assignment` then
correctly refuses to assign a DownValue on `Times` and emits
`wrsym`.  Several CRC-table rules with this shape silently fail to
install.

### Fix

`src/eval.c`:

- Add `lhs_arg_contains_pattern(e)` — recursive scan for `Blank`,
  `BlankSequence`, `BlankNullSequence`, `Pattern`, `Optional`,
  `Repeated`, `RepeatedNull`, `PatternTest`, `HoldPattern`,
  `Condition`.
- In the Set/SetDelayed branch, hold any LHS arg for which the helper
  returns `true`.  Plain `f[x] = 1` (no pattern construct) continues
  down the existing eval path, so the OwnValue-substitution semantic
  is preserved.

Also `src/internal/CRCMathTablesIntegrals.m`:

- Trailing semicolons added to `SetAttributes[IntegrateTable, …]` and
  the `Integrate\`CRCTable[f_, x_] := IntegrateTable[f, x]` line.
  Without the separators the parser glued the two top-level
  expressions together as `Times[…]`, producing an eighth wrsym error
  and leaving the public wrapper undefined.
- `SetAttributes[Integrate\`CRCTable, {Protected, ReadProtected}]`
  added after the DownValue is installed so the wrapper is locked once
  it exists, not before.

`src/integrate.c`:

- `integrate_init` no longer sets `ATTR_PROTECTED` on
  `Integrate\`CRCTable` — that protection would block the lazy-load
  DownValue install.  The .m file now handles protection itself.

### Verification

- Repro returns cleanly: `Integrate[1/(x^2 - 1)^3, x, Method ->
  "CRCTable"]` produces no `wrsym` output (still unevaluated due to a
  pre-existing matcher gap on `/;`-guarded patterns; that is tracked
  separately).
- `Integrate[Log[x], x, Method -> "CRCTable"]` now correctly returns
  `-x + x Log[x]` — confirms a CRC table rule (line 23) installs and
  fires after the load.
- 117-binary test suite: all pass.
- New `integrate_dispatch_tests` (5/5 pass) covers cascade routing,
  Method strict passthrough, invalid Method, and termination on the
  formerly-divergent Formula 49 inputs.


## Solve

Introduced the `Solve` builtin together with its first specialist,
`Solve\`SolvePolynomialEquality`.  The implementation follows
`plans/SOLVE_PLAN.md` -- `src/solve.c` is a router that parses options and
dispatches; `src/solvepoly.c` does the polynomial-equality work.

Scope of this initial cut:

- Single polynomial equation `lhs == rhs` in one variable.
- Domains: `Complexes` (default) and `Reals` (with discriminant-aware
  filtering per degree).
- Fast paths (no factoring): linear, quadratic, binomial `a*x^n + b`,
  n-quadratic `a*x^(2n) + b*x^n + c` -- the last two emit radical
  roots independently of `Cubics` / `Quartics`.
- Slow path: `internal_collect` -> `internal_factorsquarefree` ->
  `internal_factor` per square-free piece.  Each irreducible factor
  is handled by per-degree branches with multiplicity preserved.
- Degree 3 with `Cubics -> True` emits Cardano radicals; default emits
  held `Root[Function[t, p[t]], k]` objects.
- Degree 4 and degree ≥ 5: held `Root[]` objects per root.  Ferrari
  (Quartics -> True) is reserved.

`HoldAll` is set on `Solve` so the variable argument is not substituted
by an existing OwnValue at the call site.  The equation argument is
explicitly evaluated inside the builtin so that user shorthand like
`(x-1)(x-2)(x-3) == 0` canonicalises before classification.  A known
limitation: an OwnValue on the solve variable (`x = 5; Solve[x^2 == 4,
x]`) currently does leak through the equation's evaluation; Mathematica
uses `Block` scoping for this and that is a follow-up.

New symbols added to `sym_names.{h,c}`: `Solve`,
`Solve\`SolvePolynomialEquality`, `Cubics`, `Quartics`,
`GeneratedParameters`, `VerifySolutions`, `Assumptions`,
`InverseFunctions`.

### Verification

- New test binary `solve_tests` (15 tests, all pass) covers linear,
  quadratic, binomial, n-quadratic, biquadratic, multiplicity, mixed
  factors, cubic default, cubic radical, quintic, trivial / tautology
  / non-polynomial cases, multivariate-declined.
- REPL smoke checks for each of the above cases match the expected
  output.

## Eigenvalues / Eigenvectors

`Eigenvalues[m]`, `Eigenvalues[{m, a}]`, `Eigenvalues[m, k]`,
`Eigenvalues[m, -k]`, `Eigenvalues[m, UpTo[k]]`, and the corresponding
`Eigenvectors[...]` overloads are now available
(`src/linalg.c`).

### Algorithm

- Ordinary characteristic polynomial: Faddeev–Leverrier–Souriau in
  O(n^4) matrix multiplications.  Avoids the n! cost of Laplace
  expansion on a polynomial-entry matrix, so eigenvalues of
  `IdentityMatrix[12]` (and similarly large rational / diagonal
  matrices) return in milliseconds.
- Generalised case (`m - lambda a`) still uses Laplace expansion of the
  polynomial-entry matrix; acceptable in practice because the corpus
  of generalised eigenproblems is small (≤ 3×3).
- Roots of the characteristic polynomial are obtained via the public
  `Solve` builtin so inexact (Real / MPFR) input automatically gets the
  rationalise → solve → numericalize pipeline.
- For numerical input, tiny imaginary noise introduced by the Cardano
  formula on real cubics is chopped with a relative 1e-10 / absolute
  1e-12 threshold.
- Numerical eigenvalues are sorted in order of decreasing absolute
  value via `N[Abs[lambda]]`; symbolic eigenvalues retain Solve's
  natural ordering.
- `Eigenvectors` finds each eigenvalue's null space via `RowReduce`.
  When the null-space dimension is less than the algebraic multiplicity
  (defective eigenvalue) the shortfall is padded in-line with zero
  vectors so positional alignment with `Eigenvalues` is preserved.
- For approximate matrices, the eigenvector computation is done in the
  rationalised domain and numericalized + normalised at the end, so
  numerical matrices return unit-Norm eigenvectors.
- `Infinity` generalised eigenvalues correspond to the null space of
  the right-hand-side pencil matrix `a`; the matching eigenvectors are
  computed from that null space.
- Options: `Cubics`, `Quartics`, `Method` (`Method` reserved).  The
  defaults are `Cubics -> True` and `Quartics -> True` so the
  closed-form pipeline can numericalize results without held `Root[]`
  objects sneaking past `N`.

### Limitations

- Numerical eigenvectors of n ≥ 3 inexact matrices substitute exact
  radical eigenvalues into the residual matrix; for n ≥ 3 the Cardano-
  derived expressions can be too large for `RowReduce` to make progress
  in reasonable time.  A proper numerical eigenvector routine (inverse
  iteration / QR) is a follow-up.
- The 100×100 numerical example in the Mathematica reference docs is
  not yet supported -- it requires a tridiagonal-aware numerical
  eigenvalue method.

### Symbols

`SYM_Eigenvalues`, `SYM_Eigenvectors` added to `sym_names.{h,c}`.
Both builtins are `Protected`; docstrings registered in `info.c`.

### Verification

- New test binary `eigen_tests` (24 tests, all pass) covers exact 3×3
  with singular det, symbolic 2×2 round-trip verification, machine-
  precision 3×3 with chop, repeated eigenvalues, identity matrices
  (up to 12×12), 4×4 block matrices, all k-spec variants
  (`k`, `-k`, `UpTo[k]`), generalised exact / symbolic / k-spec,
  defective-eigenvalue zero padding, eigenvector verification via
  `m.v == lambda v` for 4×4 and singular 3×3, unit-Norm property for
  numerical 2×2, non-normalised property for exact 2×2, generalised
  eigenvector verification, generalised k-spec, triangular and
  diagonal matrices, non-square unevaluation, and docstring presence.

## linalg: add LinearSolve (2026-05-18)

`LinearSolve[m, b]` finds `x` satisfying `m . x == b`.  The matrix `m`
may be square or rectangular; `b` may be a vector (LinearSolve returns
a vector) or a matrix with one solution column per RHS column.
Implemented in `src/linalg.c` as fraction-free Gauss-Jordan elimination
on the augmented matrix `[m | b]` — the same Bareiss-like routine that
backs `RowReduce` and `Inverse`, so exact integer / rational / symbolic
input flows through with no spurious denominator blow-up.

### Behaviour

- Square invertible system → unique solution.
- Rectangular over- or under-determined system → particular solution
  with every free (non-pivot) variable taken to be 0, matching
  Mathematica's convention.
- Inconsistent system → emits `LinearSolve::nosol` to stderr and
  returns the call unevaluated.
- Shape error (`b`'s leading dimension does not match `m`'s row count,
  or either argument is not a matrix / vector) → emits
  `LinearSolve::lvec1` / `::lvec` / `::matrix` and returns unevaluated.

### Symbols / docstring

- `SYM_LinearSolve` added to `sym_names.{h,c}`.
- `Attributes[LinearSolve] = {Protected}` (assigned in `linalg_init`).
- Docstring registered in `info.c`, accessible via `?LinearSolve`.

### Verification

New test binary `linearsolve_tests` exercises 31 cases:
identity / diagonal / 1×1 systems, exact integer & rational 2×2 and
3×3 round-trips, matrix-RHS shapes, 3-column rectangular and 4×2
rectangular shapes, symbolic 2×2 / 3×3 verified by
`m . LinearSolve[m, b] == b`, Gaussian-integer system from the spec,
floating-point round-trip, singular / inconsistent / shape-error
fail paths (verifying unevaluated return), and equivalence with
`Inverse[m]` via `LinearSolve[m, IdentityMatrix[n]]`.

Valgrind (`--leak-check=full`) reports zero leaks attributable to our
code; the surviving "definitely lost" blocks all trace into
`libobjc.A.dylib` / `dyld4` initialisation, the standard macOS
baseline.


## matsol.c — Method options for RowReduce and LinearSolve (2026-05-18)

`RowReduce[m]` and `LinearSolve[m, b]` now accept an optional
`Method -> "<name>"` argument that selects the elimination algorithm.
The bodies of both builtins were lifted out of `src/linalg.c` into a
new `src/matsol.c` (the new file is wired in via `core_init` →
`matsol_init`).  `src/linalg.h` now exports the four primitives the
two routines share with the rest of `linalg.c`:
`get_tensor_dims`, `flatten_tensor`, `laplace_det` and
`exact_div_wrapper`.

### Accepted methods

| Name (string)                | Description |
|------------------------------|-------------|
| `Automatic` (default)        | Alias for `DivisionFreeRowReduction`. |
| `DivisionFreeRowReduction`   | Bareiss-like fraction-free Gauss-Jordan on `m` (or `[m | b]`). Preserves the prior default exactly. |
| `OneStepRowReduction`        | Classical Gauss-Jordan with one division per pivot per element. Each per-cell update goes through `Together` so symbolic rationals reduce. |
| `CofactorExpansion`          | For `LinearSolve`: Cramer's rule via Laplace expansion of `Det[m]` (square non-singular m only). For `RowReduce`: identity matrix when `Det[m] != 0`, else falls back to `DivisionFreeRowReduction`. |

`Method -> Automatic` (the symbol, not the string) is also accepted.

### Error messages

| Message                       | Cause |
|-------------------------------|-------|
| `RowReduce::cofnsq`           | `CofactorExpansion` requested but `m` is singular or non-square; falls back. |
| `RowReduce::method`           | Unrecognised method name. |
| `LinearSolve::cofnsq`         | `CofactorExpansion` requested for non-square `m`; call stays unevaluated. |
| `LinearSolve::cofsng`         | `CofactorExpansion` requested but `Det[m] == 0`; call stays unevaluated. |
| `LinearSolve::method`         | Unrecognised method name. |

All four messages use the `last_warned_hash` rate-limit idiom so
nested test loops don't spam stderr.

### Power[Rational, integer] fix (pre-requisite)

Adding `OneStepRowReduction` over bignum matrices surfaced a
pre-existing bug in `Power[Rational[a, b], n]` where the `is_rational`
fast path bailed out as soon as `a` or `b` overflowed `int64`. That
caused `Power[Rational[10^50-1, 10^25], -1]` (a typical
post-elimination shape on bignum matrices) to stay unsimplified,
which in turn broke `Together` and `is_zero_poly`.

The fix in `src/power.c` adds a bigint-aware Rational-base path that
walks the `Rational[X, Y] ^ k` triple through `mpz_pow_ui` and emits a
canonical reduced `Rational` (or demoted integer) result. Soundness is
preserved: only integer-like components are accepted, the sign is
normalised onto the numerator, and the GCD is cancelled after raising
both halves to the power.

### Verification

`tests/test_matsol_methods.c` covers every `(builtin, method)` pair
across: tiny exact integer, bignum, machine-precision `Real`,
arbitrary-precision MPFR (gated on `USE_MPFR`), symbolic invertible,
symbolic singular, rectangular, and complex matrices.  Inconsistent
systems are verified to print back unevaluated for all three
methods.  Existing `linalg_tests` and `linearsolve_tests` continue to
pass byte-for-byte (the default code path is unchanged).  Valgrind
reports zero leaks attributable to Mathilda code; the only surviving
"definitely lost" blocks trace into macOS `libobjc` / `dyld4`
initialisation, the standard baseline.


## complex, comparisons, info: Abs/Re/Im of symbolic Complex sums, NumericQ comparisons, fuller iter docstrings

### Symbolic decomposition in Abs, Re, Im, ReIm, Conjugate

`Abs`, `Re`, `Im`, `ReIm`, and `Conjugate` now decompose expressions
that are syntactically a `Plus` or `Times` carrying nested `Complex[a, b]`
literals.  Previously these built-ins only matched the canonical
`Complex[re, im]` head, so expressions like `1 + I Sqrt[3]` (which
Mathilda stores as `Plus[1, Times[Complex[0, 1], Power[3, 1/2]]]` —
the `Sqrt[3]` coefficient blocks the usual Plus-time folding into a
single `Complex[]`) stayed under an unevaluated `Abs[...]`.

A new file-static helper `complex_decompose` in `src/complex.c` walks
the expression structurally:

- `Complex[a, b]` literals contribute `(a, b)` directly.
- `Plus[t1, t2, ...]` recurses on each term and sums the real and
  imaginary parts (terms with no detectable imaginary component fall
  into the real bucket).
- `Times[f1, f2, ...]` recurses on each factor, threading a running
  complex product via `(a + b i)(c + d i) = (ac - bd) + (ad + bc) i`.

Subexpressions that aren't a `Complex` literal (symbols, `Sqrt[n]`,
unknown functions, ...) are treated as real-valued, matching
Mathematica's default `Re`/`Im` behaviour.  `Conjugate` builds
`re + (-I)*im` from the decomposition, so e.g. `Conjugate[1 + I Sqrt[3]]`
now reduces to `1 - I Sqrt[3]`.

### Less/Greater/Equal/Unequal handle NumericQ-style expressions

`compare_numeric` in `src/comparisons.c` previously short-circuited
to `can_compare = false` for anything that wasn't an `Integer`,
`Real`, or `Rational` leaf.  It now falls back to `numericalize` at
machine precision, so symbolic-but-exact numeric expressions
(`Sqrt[3]`, `Pi`, `Pi + Sqrt[2]/2`, ...) reduce to a machine double
and participate in comparisons.  This means:

- `Sqrt[3] < 20` -> `True`
- `Pi < 4` -> `True`, `Pi < 3` -> `False`
- `Sqrt[2] <= Sqrt[2]` -> `True`
- `Sqrt[3] == 2` -> `False`, `Sqrt[3] != 2` -> `True`
- `x < 5`, `Sqrt[x] < 5` -> unchanged (numericalize leaves these
  symbolic, so `compare_numeric` still reports `can_compare = false`).

`Equal` was extended to surface a definite `False` whenever
`compare_numeric` returns a non-zero result (mirroring the symmetric
path already present in `Unequal`), so `Sqrt[3] == 2` no longer leaks
through as unevaluated.  The result of `compare_numeric` is marked
inexact in the new path so the existing `2^-46` floating-point
tolerance branch is used.

### End-to-end: Select[Abs[#] < c &]

The original report was `Select[Flatten[Table[a + b*Exp[2 Pi I/3], {a,-2,2}, {b,-2,2}], 1], Abs[#] < 20 &]` returning only the
five integer entries — every other entry stayed `Abs[...] < 20`
because `Abs` couldn't reduce the Plus-form complex and `Less`
couldn't compare the resulting `Sqrt[..]`.  After this change the
predicate returns `True` for all 25 lattice points, matching
Mathematica.

### Fuller docstrings for Do and For

`docs/spec/builtins/control-flow.md`-tracked builtins `Do` and `For`
had terse docstrings that omitted the multi-iterator and empty-body
forms as well as the `Break[]` / `Continue[]` / `Return[v]` flow
controls.  The strings registered in `src/info.c` now cover all the
iterator-spec variants (`{n}`, `{i, imax}`, `{i, imin, imax, di}`,
`{i, {i1, i2, ...}}`, multi-iterator threading), the `HoldAll`
attribute, and the loop-control built-ins.  `While`'s docstring was
already complete and is unchanged.

## Eigenvalues / Eigenvectors moved to `src/mateigen.c` (Phase 0)

The Eigenvalues / Eigenvectors subsystem has been extracted from
`src/linalg.c` into a new `src/mateigen.c` translation unit, mirroring
the way `LinearSolve` / `RowReduce` / `Inverse` were previously split
into `matsol.c` and `matinv.c`.  No user-visible behaviour change:
the symbolic Faddeev–Leverrier → `Solve` pipeline is preserved
verbatim and all 47 tests in `tests/test_eigen.c` continue to pass
unchanged.

The accompanying header `src/mateigen.h` declares the two builtins
and `mateigen_init()`, which is now called from `core_init()` after
`matlstsq_init()`.  The `dot2` tensor-contraction helper in
`src/linalg.c` has been promoted from `static` to public visibility
(declared in `src/linalg.h`) so the eigenvalue code in
`mateigen.c` can reuse it for the Faddeev–Leverrier matrix
multiplications without round-tripping through the `Dot` builtin.

This refactor sets up the upcoming numeric Method dispatch (
`"Direct"` / `"Arnoldi"` / `"Banded"` / `"FEAST"`) and the
machine-precision and arbitrary-precision (MPFR) kernels described in
`lovely-roaming-diffie.md`.

## Eigenvalues / Eigenvectors: Method option dispatch wired (Phase 1)

Eigenvalues and Eigenvectors now parse a `Method -> ...` option on the
numeric-matrix path.  The recognised values are `Automatic` (the
default), `"Direct"`, `"Arnoldi"`, `"Banded"`, and `"FEAST"`, and the
parser also accepts the list-of-sub-options form used by Mathematica
(e.g. `Method -> {"Arnoldi", MaxIterations -> 20, Tolerance -> 1.*^-8}`)
where the head element classifies the method and the tail entries are
sub-options interpreted by the per-method kernels.

The Phase 1 commit introduces the public `MateigenMethod` enum and the
`mateigen_parse_method_value` helper in `src/mateigen.h`, along with
the new interned symbols `Arnoldi`, `Banded`, `BasisSize`, `Direct`,
`FEAST`, `Interval`, and `MaxIterations` in `src/sym_names.{h,c}`.

The dedicated numerical kernels for each Method will land in Phases
2-5.  Until then, any explicit Method other than `Automatic` on a
numeric matrix prints a single warning to stderr and falls back to
the existing symbolic characteristic-polynomial pipeline so the call
still produces a result.  Symbolic matrices ignore Method entirely.
Unknown Method values are tolerated -- one warning, same symbolic
fallback -- to avoid leaving calls unevaluated while the kernels are
under construction.

The `?Eigenvalues` and `?Eigenvectors` help text in `src/info.c` is
updated to document the new Method grammar and per-method semantics.
Ten new unit tests in `tests/test_eigen.c` exercise the parser:
Automatic, each of the four explicit methods, the list-of-sub-options
form, an unknown Method string, the symbolic-matrix-ignores-Method
path, the Eigenvectors mirror, and the Method-with-k-spec combination.

## Eigenvalues / Eigenvectors: numerical "Direct" kernel for real symmetric machine-precision (Phase 2 step 1)

The first real numerical eigensolver kernel lands.  For an
approximate-numeric real symmetric matrix, `Method -> Automatic` and
`Method -> "Direct"` now route through a hand-rolled hot-path kernel
in `src/mateigen.c` instead of the symbolic
Faddeev-Leverrier-plus-`Solve` pipeline.

Algorithm:

1. Convert the Expr List-of-Lists to a flat row-major `double` workspace
   (`MatD`) at the dispatcher boundary -- the inner loops never touch
   `Expr` nodes.
2. Hermitian / real-symmetric structure is auto-detected; non-symmetric
   numeric matrices and complex / MPFR inputs return `NULL` from this
   step's dispatcher so the caller falls through to the symbolic path.
3. **Householder tridiagonalisation** of the symmetric matrix via the
   rank-2 update `A <- A - u q^T - q u^T` with `q = p - 2 K u`,
   `p = 2 A u`, `K = u^T A u` (Golub & Van Loan Algorithm 8.3.1).
   Scratch buffers are pre-allocated so no `malloc` happens inside the
   reduction loop.  When eigenvectors are requested, an orthogonal
   accumulator `Q` collects the Householder reflectors.
4. **Implicit-shift symmetric QR** with Wilkinson shift on the
   tridiagonal `(diag, sub)`.  Each sweep applies Givens rotations
   along the active block via the closed-form update for the symmetric
   2x2 similarity `Q^T A Q`, chasing the bulge through the band.
   Deflation triggers when an off-diagonal entry falls below
   `1e-14 * (|d_k| + |d_{k+1}|)`.  Max-sweeps guard at `30 * n` to
   prevent theoretical hangs.
5. Sort by descending `|lambda|` (stable on ties) and emit a List of
   `EXPR_REAL` eigenvalues or a List-of-Lists of orthonormal
   eigenvectors.  `k`-spec (`+k` / `-k` / `UpTo[k]`) is applied after
   sort.

The kernel reuses Phase 1's `MateigenWant` flag so a single dispatcher
serves both `Eigenvalues` and `Eigenvectors`; the eigenvector
accumulation work is skipped when the caller only asked for values.
Every numerical site carries a `LAPACK-HOOK` comment naming the
LAPACK routine that would replace it once `USE_LAPACK` is wired
(`dsytrd` for tridiagonalisation, `dsteqr` / `dstedc` for the
symmetric tridiagonal QR step).

A new `tests/test_mateigen_direct.c` (19 assertions) and a shared
`tests/eigen_corpus.{h,c}` test harness verify the kernel against a
broad real-symmetric corpus:

- Diagonal, identity, zero, and 2x2 hand-computed cases
  (`[[4,1],[1,4]]`, `[[1,2],[2,-1]]`).
- Toeplitz tridiagonal matrices at sizes 3, 5, 6 with the closed-form
  spectrum `lambda_k = 2 (1 - cos(k pi / (n+1)))`.
- The Hilbert-4 matrix (ill-conditioned but well-defined symmetric
  spectrum).
- Deterministically-seeded random symmetric matrices at sizes 5 and 10
  (Lehmer LCG, reproducible).
- Repeated-eigenvalue case (multiplicity-2 eigenvalue 2 in `2I + 1 1^T`).
- `k`-spec interaction (`+2`, `-2`, `UpTo[oversized]`).
- Dispatch coverage: `Method -> "Direct"` matches `Method -> Automatic`,
  non-symmetric numeric input falls through to the symbolic path,
  integer-matrix input stays on the symbolic path entirely.
- Eigenvector orthonormality verified via `V V^T = I` and per-pair
  residual `||A v_i - lambda_i v_i||_inf` against
  `64 n eps ||A||_inf`.

All 76 existing eigen tests in `tests/test_eigen.c` continue to pass
